# Primary Reference Standard Preparation

## Source Material Selection

### **MODULE 3: QUALITY**
### **SECTION 3.2.S.5: REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
### **SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.1: PRIMARY REFERENCE STANDARD PREPARATION**

---

# **3.2.S.5.1.1 SOURCE MATERIAL SELECTION**

## **1.0 Introduction and Regulatory Rationale**
The selection of source material for the establishment of the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) represents a critical milestone in the Google Health Sciences (GHS) CMC strategy. Pursuant to **ICH Q6B** (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*) and **FDA Guidance for Industry: Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation**, the primary reference standard must be a representative batch of the drug substance that has been characterized extensively and shown to be of the highest purity and stability.

The source material for the Glucogen-XR PRS (Batch ID: **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**) was derived from a pivotal Phase 3 clinical manufacturing campaign conducted at the Google Cloud Life Sciences (GCLS) South San Francisco Facility (FEI: 3004592101). This selection is predicated on the material’s demonstrated alignment with the "Quality Target Product Profile" (QTPP) and its derivation from the definitive commercial manufacturing process (Process Version 2.4).

## **2.0 Selection Criteria for Source Material**
The selection process was governed by Internal Standard Operating Procedure **GHS-SOP-QA-0098: Selection and Qualification of Primary Reference Standards**. The following criteria were established a priori for the candidate batch:

### **2.1 Process Representativeness**
*   **Cell Line Integrity:** The material must originate from the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** (CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative) cell line, harvested from a 2,000L Single-Use Bioreactor (SUB).
*   **Scale:** Must be produced at the commercial scale (2,000L) to ensure that the impurity profile (Host Cell Proteins, DNA, and glycosylation patterns) reflects the final marketed product.
*   **Process Parameters:** All Critical Process Parameters (CPPs) must have remained within the Proven Acceptable Ranges (PARs) during the entirety of the upstream and downstream operations.

### **2.2 High Purity and Low Impurity Profile**
*   **Purity by SEC-HPLC:** ≥ 99.0% (Main Peak).
*   **Purity by RP-HPLC:** ≥ 98.5% (Main Peak).
*   **HCP Concentration:** ≤ 10 ng/mg (as measured by GHS-ELISA-V4).
*   **Residual DNA:** ≤ 1 pg/mg (as measured by qPCR).

### **2.3 Long-term Stability Forecast**
The batch must demonstrate thermodynamic stability during forced degradation studies (thermal, photolytic, and oxidative) indicative of a material suitable for long-term storage at -80°C for a projected period of >120 months.

---

## **3.0 Candidate Batch Evaluation (Batch GLUC-2025-014)**
Following a comprehensive review of the 2024-2025 manufacturing campaign, Batch **GLUC-2025-014** was selected as the source material for the Primary Reference Standard.

### **Table 3.2.S.5.1.1-1: Comparative Analysis of Candidate Batches for PRS Selection**

| Parameter | Acceptance Criteria | Batch GLUC-2025-012 | Batch GLUC-2025-013 | **Batch GLUC-2025-014 (SELECTED)** |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Manufacturing Date** | N/A | 12-JAN-2025 | 28-JAN-2025 | **14-FEB-2025** |
| **Scale (Liters)** | 2,000 L | 2,000 L | 2,000 L | **2,000 L** |
| **Purity (SEC-HPLC %)** | ≥ 99.0% | 99.1% | 99.0% | **99.7%** |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC %)** | ≥ 98.5% | 98.6% | 98.5% | **99.2%** |
| **Charge Variants (CEX)** | Report % Main | 82.3% | 81.9% | **84.5%** |
| **HCP (ppm)** | ≤ 10 ppm | 8.2 ppm | 9.1 ppm | **3.4 ppm** |
| **Residual DNA (pg/mg)** | ≤ 10 pg/mg | 2.1 pg/mg | 4.5 pg/mg | **0.8 pg/mg** |
| **Endotoxin (EU/mg)** | ≤ 0.5 EU/mg | < 0.05 EU/mg | < 0.05 EU/mg | **< 0.05 EU/mg** |
| **Bioburden (CFU/10mL)** | 0 CFU | 0 CFU | 0 CFU | **0 CFU** |
| **Selection Status** | N/A | Rejected (High HCP) | Rejected (Lower Purity) | **ACCEPTED AS PRS** |

---

## **4.0 Detailed Manufacturing History of Selected Source Material**
Batch **GLUC-2025-014** was manufactured in Suite 4 of the South San Francisco facility under cGMP conditions.

### **4.1 Upstream Summary**
The upstream process utilized the GHS-CHO-001 cell line. The seed train (Inoculum Expansion) was performed using chemically defined media (CDM-GHS-02) devoid of animal-derived components, adhering to **USP <1024>** guidelines.

*   **Vial Thaw:** Cryopreserved Working Cell Bank (WCB) vial WCB-2023-A.
*   **N-1 Stage:** 200L SUB; Duration: 4 days; Viable Cell Density (VCD) at transfer: $18.4 \times 10^6$ cells/mL.
*   **Production Bioreactor (N):** 2,000L SUB; Duration: 14 days. 
    *   *Critical Parameter:* Dissolved Oxygen (DO) maintained at 40% $\pm$ 5%.
    *   *Critical Parameter:* pH maintained at 7.00 $\pm$ 0.10.
    *   *Harvest VCD:* $22.1 \times 10^6$ cells/mL with viability of 94.2%.

### **4.2 Downstream Summary**
The purification process for GLUC-2025-014 employed a three-step chromatographic sequence designed to minimize truncation products and deamidated species.

1.  **Protein A Affinity Chromatography:** Capture step using MabSelect SuRe LX. Elution pH: 3.4.
2.  **Viral Inactivation:** Low pH (3.55) for 60 minutes at 20°C.
3.  **Anion Exchange Chromatography (AEX):** Q-Sepharose Fast Flow in flow-through mode for HCP and DNA clearance.
4.  **Cation Exchange Chromatography (CEX):** Poros 50 HS in bind-elute mode for charge variant resolution.
5.  **Viral Filtration:** Planova 20N.
6.  **Ultrafiltration/Diafiltration (UF/DF):** Final formulation into 20 mM Histidine, 100 mM Arginine, 0.02% Polysorbate 80, pH 6.0.

---

## **5.0 Protocol for PRS Aliquoting and Storage (GHS-PRO-7721)**

Upon confirmation of Batch GLUC-2025-014 as the source material, the material was transferred to the Reference Standard Laboratory for final processing under ISO 5 (Class 100) conditions.

### **5.1 Step-by-Step Aliquoting Procedure**
1.  **Thawing:** Bulk Drug Substance (BDS) was thawed from -80°C in a controlled $25^{\circ}C$ water bath for 4 hours.
2.  **Homogenization:** The BDS container was gently inverted 20 times to ensure homogeneity of the protein concentration ($C = 50.0 \text{ mg/mL} \pm 1.0$).
3.  **Sterile Filtration:** The material was filtered through a 0.22 $\mu$m PES Millipak filter into a sterile receiving vessel.
4.  **Aliquoting:** Using an automated fill-finish system (Rigel-X-200), 0.5 mL of the solution was dispensed into 2.0 mL Type I borosilicate glass vials (USP <661.1>).
5.  **Stopper/Crimp:** Vials were sealed with FluroTec® coated chlorobutyl rubber stoppers and aluminum flip-off caps.
6.  **Labeling:** Each vial was labeled as:
    *   *Name:* Glucogen-XR Primary Reference Standard
    *   *Batch:* GLUC-2025-PRS-01
    *   *Concentration:* 50 mg/mL
    *   *Storage:* -80°C
    *   *Exp:* TBD (Subject to Annual Re-qualification)

### **Table 3.2.S.5.1.1-2: Yield and Distribution of PRS Aliquots**

| Item Description | Quantity | Storage Location | Unit Volume |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Primary Reference Standard (PRS) | 500 Vials | Vault 1 (GHS Main) | 0.5 mL |
| Retention Samples (Reserve) | 100 Vials | Vault 2 (Off-site Backup) | 0.5 mL |
| Characterization Inventory | 50 Vials | Lab Freezer GHS-F12 | 0.5 mL |

---

## **6.0 Statistical Justification of Homogeneity**
To ensure that the source material selected is uniform across the entire PRS fill, a Stratified Sampling Plan was executed according to **ISO 2859-1**. Vials were sampled at the Beginning (B), Middle (M), and End (E) of the filling process ($n=10$ per segment).

### **6.1 Purity Variation Analysis**
The Coefficient of Variation (CV) for purity by SEC-HPLC across the fill was calculated as follows:
$$CV = \frac{\sigma}{\mu} \times 100$$
Where:
*   $\sigma$ (Standard Deviation) = 0.04
*   $\mu$ (Mean Purity) = 99.68%
*   **Calculated CV = 0.04%**

Since the $CV < 1.0\%$, the homogeneity of the source material is confirmed for use as the Primary Reference Standard.

---

## **7.0 Summary of Regulatory Compliance**
The selection of Batch **GLUC-2025-014** complies with:
1.  **ICH Q6B:** The material is fully characterized for physicochemical properties, biological activity, and purity.
2.  **USP <1048>:** Validation of the peptide sequence and post-translational modifications.
3.  **21 CFR 211.160:** Ensuring the standard is representative of the production process and supported by reliable analytical data.

Google Health Sciences concludes that the source material selected for the Glucogen-XR Primary Reference Standard provides the highest level of assurance for the continued assessment of drug substance and drug product quality throughout the lifecycle of this application.

## Preparation and Characterization

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS

#### 3.2.S.5.1 Primary Reference Standard: Preparation and Characterization

This section provides a comprehensive description of the preparation, qualification, and characterization of the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), designated as Batch **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**. This standard serves as the highest level of metrological traceability for all subsequent working standards (WRS) and clinical lot release testing for Google Health Sciences’ Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus program.

---

### I. INTRODUCTION AND REGULATORY STRATEGY

The establishment of the Glucogen-XR Primary Reference Standard follows the mandates set forth in **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q7** (Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients). 

Given that Glucogen-XR is a recombinant GLP-1 receptor agonist peptide expressed in the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** (GS-knockout CHO-K1 derivative) cell line, the reference standard must represent the clinical material's heterogeneity, including post-translational modifications (PTMs) and the specific extended-release conformational profile.

#### 1.1 Scope of Qualification
The qualification program for GLUC-2025-PRS-01 encompasses:
1.  **Structural Confirmation:** Primary sequence, disulfide mapping, and N/C-terminal integrity.
2.  **Physicochemical Properties:** Molecular weight, isoform distribution (cIEF), and extinction coefficient determination.
3.  **Biological Activity:** Potency relative to internal bioassay standards.
4.  **Purity and Impurities:** SEC-HPLC (aggregates), RP-HPLC (chemical variants), and HCP/ProA residuals.

---

### II. PREPARATION OF PRIMARY REFERENCE STANDARD (GLUC-2025-PRS-01)

#### 2.1 Source Material Selection
The PRS was derived from a representative Phase III clinical-scale drug substance lot, **GLUC-2025-MFG-008**, produced at the South San Francisco facility (3000 Innovation Drive). This lot was selected based on its mid-range performance across all validated specifications, ensuring it represents the "center" of the manufacturing process capability.

#### 2.2 Purification and Enrichment Protocol (Step-by-Step)
To ensure the PRS provides the highest level of stability and purity, the drug substance underwent an additional polishing step and controlled lyophilization.

| Step | Procedure ID | Equipment ID | Description |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **1** | SOP-PUR-0992 | AKTA-Pure-XLS-01 | **Buffer Exchange:** DS from GLUC-2025-MFG-008 was exchanged into 20mM Histidine, 5% Sucrose, pH 6.5 using tangential flow filtration (TFF). |
| **2** | SOP-PUR-1044 | GE-AxiChrom-300 | **High-Resolution RP-Polishing:** Removal of trace truncated peptides using a specialized C18 stationary phase (10µm, 300Å). |
| **3** | SOP-OPS-0021 | Millipore-Stericup-01 | **Sterile Filtration:** 0.22µm PES membrane filtration in a Grade A laminar flow hood. |
| **4** | SOP-LYO-0455 | VirTis-AdVantage-Pro | **Lyophilization:** 2.0 mL aliquots filled into 5mL Type I borosilicate glass vials. |
| **5** | SOP-PKG-088 | Automated-Capper-04 | **Stoppering/Sealing:** Nitrogen headspace overlay, bromobutyl stoppers, and aluminum flip-off seals. |

#### 2.3 Filling Summary and Storage
*   **Total Vials Filled:** 1,250 vials.
*   **Fill Volume:** 2.1 mL ± 0.05 mL.
*   **Protein Concentration:** 10.0 mg/mL (nominal).
*   **Storage Conditions:** Controlled Temperature Unit (CTU) at -80°C ± 5°C.
*   **Inventory Tracking:** SAP-GHS-INV-01.

---

---

### IV. DETAILED ANALYTICAL PROTOCOLS

#### 4.1 Mass Spectrometry (Intact and Reduced)
**Method ID:** AM-MS-GLUC-01
**Instrumentation:** Thermo Fisher Q Exactive HF-X Orbitrap
**Procedure:**
1.  **Sample Prep:** Reconstitute PRS in MS-grade water to 1 mg/mL.
2.  **Desalting:** Online trap column (C4) to remove histidine and sucrose.
3.  **Deconvolution:** Data processed using BioPharma Finder™ 4.0.
**Calculation for Mass Accuracy:**
$$\text{Mass Error (ppm)} = \left( \frac{\text{Experimental Mass} - \text{Theoretical Mass}}{\text{Theoretical Mass}} \right) \times 10^6$$
*Result:* (4,285.62 - 4,285.60) / 4,285.60 * 1,000,000 = **4.6 ppm** (Threshold < 10 ppm).

#### 4.2 Amino Acid Analysis (AAA) for Molar Absorptivity
To establish the absolute concentration of the PRS, AAA was performed using post-column Ninhydrin derivation.
**Standard Reference:** NIST SRM 2389a.
**Calculated Extinction Coefficient ($\epsilon$):**
Based on 3 Tyr and 1 Trp residues, the theoretical $\epsilon$ at 280 nm is 1.48 mL/(mg·cm).
*Experimental Determination:* **1.492 mL/(mg·cm)** (n=6).

---

### V. PURITY AND IMPURITY PROFILING

#### 5.1 Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC-HPLC)
**Method:** TSKgel G3000SWxl, 7.8mm x 30cm; Mobile Phase: 0.2M Potassium Phosphate, pH 6.8.
**Observation:**
The chromatogram for **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** exhibits a single symmetrical peak at 12.4 minutes.
*   **High Molecular Weight (HMW) Species:** 0.22%
*   **Monomer:** 99.72%
*   **Low Molecular Weight (LMW) Species:** 0.06%

#### 5.2 Reverse-Phase HPLC (RP-HPLC)
**Method:** Zorbax 300SB-C18, 4.6 x 150mm; Gradient: 25% to 45% Acetonitrile (0.1% TFA).
**Observation:**
This method is sensitive to deamidation and oxidation.
*   **Deamidated Variant (Asn-28):** 0.45%
*   **Oxidized Variant (Met-14):** 0.32%
*   **D-Amino Acid Isoforms:** Not Detected (<0.1%)

---

### VI. BIOLOGICAL CHARACTERIZATION (CELL-BASED POTENCY)

The biological activity of GLUC-2025-PRS-01 was evaluated using a HEK-293 cell line stably transfected with the human GLP-1 receptor and a cAMP-response element (CRE) luciferase reporter.

**Statistical Analysis (4-Parameter Logistic Model):**
$$y = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B}$$
Where:
*   $A$ = Bottom Asymptote
*   $D$ = Top Asymptote
*   $C$ = $EC_{50}$ (Potency)
*   $B$ = Hill Slope

**Potency Results:**
The $EC_{50}$ of the PRS was determined to be **14.2 pM** (95% CI: 13.8 - 14.6 pM), establishing the 100% activity benchmark for all subsequent Glucogen-XR testing.

---

### VII. TRACEABILITY AND STABILITY PROGRAM

#### 7.1 Traceability Chain
*   **NIST Traceability:** All weighing equipment (Mettler Toledo XPR) calibrated with Class E2 weights traceable to NIST.
*   **Reference Material Linkage:** GLUC-2025-PRS-01 $\rightarrow$ GLUC-2025-WRS-01 (Working Standard) $\rightarrow$ Lot Release.

#### 7.2 Stability Monitoring (Protocol PRS-STAB-2025)
The Primary Reference Standard is subject to an ongoing stability program under **ICH Q1A(R2)**.

| Frequency | Storage Temp | Tests Performed |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **T=0** | -80°C | Full Qualification (See Table 1) |
| **6 Months** | -80°C, -20°C | SEC, RP-HPLC, Bioassay, Appearance |
| **Annual (5 Years)** | -80°C | Full Qualification |

**Interim Assessment:**
At the 6-month mark (Data Point: July 2025), batch **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** showed no significant changes in purity or potency (SEC Monomer: 99.70%; Bioassay: 101%).

---

### VIII. CONCLUSION

The Primary Reference Standard **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** has been prepared and characterized in accordance with high-resolution analytical techniques and regulatory expectations. The data presented herein confirm that this material is suitable for its intended use as the primary calibrator for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) program. All structural, physicochemical, and biological attributes meet the predefined acceptance criteria, providing a robust foundation for the analytical control strategy of this GLP-1 receptor agonist.

## Assignment of Value

### **3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **3.2.S.5.1 PRIMARY REFERENCE STANDARD PREPARATION**
#### **3.2.S.5.1.4 Assignment of Value**

---

### **1.0 Introduction and Scope**
The assignment of value for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) Primary Reference Standard (PRS), Lot No. **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**, follows an exhaustive multi-dimensional analytical characterization program. In accordance with **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **USP <11>** (Reference Standards), the absolute purity and potency of the PRS must be established to provide a metrological link to all subsequent working standards (WRS) and clinical/commercial release testing.

Google Health Sciences (GHS) employs a "mass balance" approach combined with absolute potency quantification via orthogonal methodologies. The value assignment integrates protein content, purity (purity/impurity profile), and biological activity into a single, comprehensive certificate of analysis (CoA).

---

### **2.0 Metrological Traceability and Calculation Framework**

The "Assigned Content" ($P_{assigned}$) of the Glucogen-XR PRS is calculated based on the mass balance principle, where the total mass is corrected for moisture, residual solvents, and inorganic impurities, and further refined by the chromatographic purity.

#### **2.1 Mass Balance Equation**
The calculation for the total peptide content (as-is basis) is derived as follows:

$$P_{content} = (100\% - \%H_2O - \%ResidualSolvents - \%ROI) \times (\frac{\%ChromatographicPurity}{100})$$

Where:
*   **$\%H_2O$**: Moisture content determined by Micro-Karl Fischer Titration (USP <921> Method 1c).
*   **$\%ResidualSolvents$**: Determined by Headspace GC-FID (ICH Q3C).
*   **$\%ROI$**: Residue on Ignition / Sulfated Ash (USP <281>).
*   **$\%ChromatographicPurity$**: Sum of the main peak area from RP-HPLC and SEC-HPLC.

#### **2.2 Potency Normalization**
Biological activity is normalized against an internal bioactive unitage, where 1.0 Unit is defined as the amount of Glucogen-XR required to elicit a 50% maximal response ($EC_{50}$) in the proprietary GHS-GLP1R-HEK293 luciferase reporter cell line.

---

### **3.0 Detailed Characterization Protocols for Value Assignment**

The following protocols were executed under cGMP conditions at the Google Health Sciences Analytical Excellence Center (GHS-AEC-04).

#### **3.1 Protein Content Determination (Nitrogen Analysis vs. UV280)**
While UV280 is used for routine monitoring, the **Assignment of Value** utilizes Nitrogen Determination (Dumas Method) and Amino Acid Analysis (AAA) for absolute quantification.

**Protocol GHS-ANA-099: Amino Acid Analysis (AAA)**
1.  **Sample Hydrolysis:** 50 µg of GLUC-2025-PRS-01 is hydrolyzed in 6N HCl with 0.1% phenol at 110°C for 24, 48, and 72 hours in vacuo.
2.  **Derivatization:** Post-column derivatization using Ninhydrin or OPA (o-phthalaldehyde).
3.  **Quantification:** Comparison against a NIST-traceable amino acid standard mix.
4.  **Recovery Calculation:** Cysteine and Tryptophan are determined via separate performic acid oxidation and alkaline hydrolysis, respectively.

**Table 1: Amino Acid Analysis Results for GLUC-2025-PRS-01**
| Amino Acid Residue | Theoretical Ratio | Experimental Ratio (n=6) | Recovery (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Aspartic Acid (Asn+Asp) | 4.0 | 3.98 ± 0.02 | 99.5 |
| Glutamic Acid (Gln+Glu) | 6.0 | 6.04 ± 0.04 | 100.7 |
| Serine* | 3.0 | 2.89 ± 0.05 | 96.3 |
| Glycine | 4.0 | 4.01 ± 0.01 | 100.2 |
| Histidine | 1.0 | 0.99 ± 0.01 | 99.0 |
| Arginine | 2.0 | 2.02 ± 0.03 | 101.0 |
| Threonine* | 2.0 | 1.91 ± 0.04 | 95.5 |
| Alanine | 3.0 | 3.00 ± 0.02 | 100.0 |
| Proline | 2.0 | 1.98 ± 0.03 | 99.0 |
| Tyrosine | 1.0 | 0.99 ± 0.01 | 99.0 |
| Valine** | 2.0 | 1.88 ± 0.06 | 94.0 |
| Isoleucine** | 1.0 | 0.92 ± 0.05 | 92.0 |
| Leucine | 3.0 | 3.02 ± 0.04 | 100.7 |
| Phenylalanine | 2.0 | 1.99 ± 0.02 | 99.5 |
| Lysine | 2.0 | 2.01 ± 0.02 | 100.5 |
| **Total Protein Content** | -- | **984.2 µg/mg** | **Pass** |
*\*Corrected for degradation during hydrolysis. \*\*Corrected for incomplete hydrolysis (72h timepoint).*

---

### **5.0 Assignment of Biological Potency**

The potency of the Primary Reference Standard is assigned based on its ability to activate the GLP-1 receptor. This is an absolute potency assignment, used to calibrate all future Bioassay Reference Materials.

#### **5.1 In Vitro Bioassay Protocol (GHS-BIO-001)**
1.  **Cell Line:** CHO-K1 cells transfected with human GLP-1R and a cAMP-response element (CRE) driving a luciferase reporter.
2.  **Dilution Series:** 10-point serial dilution (range: 0.001 nM to 100 nM).
3.  **Incubation:** 4 hours at 37°C, 5% $CO_2$.
4.  **Detection:** Addition of Steady-Glo® Luciferase Assay System; luminescence measured on a SpectraMax iD5.
5.  **Statistical Model:** 4-Parameter Logistic (4-PL) Curve Fit.

**Table 5: Potency Statistical Summary (GLUC-2025-PRS-01)**
| Parameter | Value | 95% Confidence Interval |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| $EC_{50}$ (Mean) | 14.2 pM | 13.8 - 14.6 pM |
| Hill Slope | 1.02 | 0.98 - 1.06 |
| Upper Asymptote (Max) | 1,240,000 RLU | 1,210,000 - 1,270,000 |
| **Assigned Potency** | **1.00 Unit/mg** | **Reference Definition** |

---

### **6.0 Final Value Assignment Summary**

The data generated across all modules are synthesized into the final assigned values for **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**.

**Table 6: Comprehensive Certificate of Analysis Data for Primary Reference Standard**
| Characteristic | Test Method | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual Inspection | White to off-white lyophilized cake |
| **Identity (MW)** | ESI-MS | 4182.6 Da (Conforms) |
| **Protein Content** | UV280 ($\epsilon = 1.45$) | 0.985 mg/mg (as-is) |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SEC-HPLC | 99.88% |
| **Purity (Chemical)** | RP-HPLC | 99.42% |
| **Moisture ($H_2O$)** | Karl Fischer | 1.70% |
| **Counter-ion (TFA)** | Ion Chromatography | 0.012% |
| **Bioactivity** | Cell-based Bioassay | 1.00 Units/mg (Assigned) |

#### **6.1 Final Calculation of Assigned Peptide Content**
Using the mass balance formula:
$$P_{assigned} = (100\% - 1.70\% - 0.0177\% - 0.05\%_{ROI}) \times (99.42\% / 100)$$
$$P_{assigned} = 98.2323\% \times 0.9942 = 97.66\%$$

**The assigned peptide content for Glucogen-XR Primary Reference Standard Lot GLUC-2025-PRS-01 is 976.6 µg per mg of powder.**

---

### **7.0 Stability and Re-evaluation Program**
The Primary Reference Standard is stored in the GHS Central Repository at **-80°C ± 5°C** in hermetically sealed amber vials.

#### **7.1 Monitoring Schedule**
*   **Real-Time Stability:** Testing at 0, 6, 12, 24, 36, 48, and 60 months.
*   **Parameters:** Appearance, RP-HPLC purity, SEC-HPLC purity, and Potency.
*   **Significant Change:** A decline in purity of >0.5% or a change in potency of >10% from the $t=0$ value will trigger an investigation and potential replacement of the PRS.

#### **7.2 Critical Reagents for Assignment**
All instruments used in this value assignment are qualified under GHS-SOP-772 (Equipment Qualification). The internal NIST-traceable weights used for balance verification are Lot #NIST-9982-A.

---

*   *Approved By:* Site Quality Head, GHS South San Francisco Facility.

# Primary Reference Standard Qualification

## Comprehensive Analytical Testing

### **3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **3.2.S.5.1 PRIMARY REFERENCE STANDARD QUALIFICATION**
#### **3.2.S.5.1.4 Comprehensive Analytical Testing**

---

#### **1.0 Introduction and Scope**
This section delineates the exhaustive analytical characterization performed by Google Health Sciences (GHS) to qualify the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). The designated lot for this qualification is **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**, derived from the definitive manufacturing process at the South San Francisco facility (3000 Innovation Drive). 

Qualification of the PRS follows a hierarchical tier-based approach in strict accordance with **ICH Q6B** (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*) and **ICH Q2(R2)** (*Validation of Analytical Procedures*). The objective is to establish a high-purity, well-characterized material with a defined potency to which all subsequent Working Reference Standards (WRS) and clinical drug substance/product lots will be calibrated.

#### **2.0 Material History and Lot Selection**
Lot **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** was selected based on its representative profile relative to pivotal Phase III clinical trial material. 

**Table 1: Primary Reference Standard Material Information**
| Parameter | Detail |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Manufacturer** | Google Health Sciences, Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences |
| **Batch Number** | GLUC-2025-PRS-01 |
| **Manufacturing Date** | 14-JAN-2025 |
| **Storage Temperature** | -80°C ± 5°C |
| **Container Closure** | 2.0 mL Type I Borosilicate Glass Vials, Fluorotec-coated Stopper |
| **Fill Volume** | 1.2 mL per vial |
| **Concentration** | 10.0 mg/mL (Target) |

---

#### **3.0 Tiered Analytical Characterization Framework**
The qualification program is divided into four distinct analytical pillars:
1.  **Identity and Primary Structure Confirmation** (Sequence, Disulfide Mapping, Mass Spectrometry)
2.  **Purity and Impurity Profiling** (SEC-HPLC, RP-HPLC, CEX, Residuals)
3.  **Higher-Order Structure (HOS) Analysis** (CD, NMR, FTIR, DSC)
4.  **Biological Potency and Binding Affinity** (Cell-based Bioassay, SPR)

---

#### **4.0 Detailed Analytical Protocols and Results**

##### **4.1 Identity and Primary Structure**

**4.1.1 Intact Mass Analysis by ESI-Q-TOF MS**
*   **Protocol ID:** GHS-MS-7722
*   **Equipment:** Agilent 6545XT AdvanceBio LC/Q-TOF
*   **Procedure:** 10 µg of Glucogen-XR is desalted online using a PLRP-S column. Mass spectra are acquired in positive ion mode (m/z 500-3000). Data is deconvoluted using the Maximum Entropy algorithm.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** Observed mass must be within ± 1 Da of the theoretical mass (42,568.45 Da, calculated based on the post-translationally modified peptide sequence).

**Table 2: Intact Mass Spectrometry Results for GLUC-2025-PRS-01**
| Measurement | Theoretical Mass (Da) | Observed Mass (Da) | Mass Error (ppm) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Intact Glucogen-XR | 42,568.45 | 42,568.48 | 0.70 | Conforms |

**4.1.2 Peptide Mapping with MS/MS (Sequence Coverage)**
*   **Enzymatic Digestion:** Sequential digestion using Trypsin and Asp-N.
*   **Chromatography:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC CSH C18 (1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm).
*   **Analysis:** The resulting peptides were sequenced via Collision-Induced Dissociation (CID).
*   **Results:** 100% sequence coverage was achieved. No unexpected post-translational modifications (PTMs) above 0.1% were detected.

##### **4.2 Purity and Heterogeneity**

**4.2.1 Size Exclusion HPLC (SEC-HPLC) for Aggregation**
*   **Standard:** USP <129>
*   **Column:** TSKgel G3000SWxl, 7.8 mm x 30 cm.
*   **Mobile Phase:** 0.2 M Sodium Phosphate, pH 7.0.
*   **Calculation:** 
    $ \% \text{Monomer} = \left( \frac{\text{Area}_{\text{Monomer}}}{\sum \text{Area}_{\text{All Peaks}}} \right) \times 100 $

**Table 3: SEC-HPLC Purity Data for PRS-01**
| Peak ID | Retention Time (min) | Relative Area (%) | Specification |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| HMW (Aggregates) | 6.42 | 0.12 | ≤ 0.5% |
| Monomer | 8.85 | 99.78 | ≥ 98.5% |
| LMW (Fragments) | 11.20 | 0.10 | ≤ 1.0% |

**4.2.2 Reversed-Phase HPLC (RP-HPLC) for Chemical Purity**
*   **Methodology:** Gradient elution using 0.1% TFA in Water and 0.1% TFA in Acetonitrile.
*   **Function:** Detection of oxidized, deamidated, and truncated species.

**Table 4: RP-HPLC Impurity Profile**
| Impurity | Rel. RT | Level (%) | Method Limit (LoQ) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Oxidized Species | 0.92 | 0.45 | 0.05% |
| Deamidated Species | 1.08 | 0.32 | 0.05% |
| **Total Purity** | - | **99.23** | **N/A** |

##### **4.3 Higher-Order Structure (HOS)**

**4.3.1 Circular Dichroism (CD) Spectroscopy**
*   **Far-UV CD (190-250 nm):** Determines secondary structure (α-helix, β-sheet).
*   **Protocol:** Sample diluted to 0.2 mg/mL in 10 mM Phosphate Buffer.
*   **Analysis:** Comparison against the secondary structure model of GLP-1 analogs.
*   **Data:** The spectrum for **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** exhibits characteristic minima at 208 nm and 222 nm, confirming a predominantly α-helical conformation (estimated 48.2% helix content).

**4.3.2 Differential Scanning Calorimetry (DSC)**
*   **Parameter:** Thermal Transition Temperature ($T_m$).
*   **Result:** $T_m = 68.4^\circ\text{C}$, indicating high conformational stability for the extended-release peptide construct.

---

#### **5.0 Biological Activity and Potency**

##### **5.1 In Vitro Cell-Based Bioassay**
The potency of the Primary Reference Standard is determined using a cAMP-responsive luciferase reporter gene assay in a CHO-K1 cell line overexpressing the human GLP-1 receptor (GLP-1R).

*   **Statistical Model:** Four-parameter logistic (4PL) regression.
*   **Formula:** $ y = \frac{A-D}{1+(x/C)^B} + D $
    *   *A* = Minimum response
    *   *B* = Hill slope
    *   *C* = $EC_{50}$
    *   *D* = Maximum response

**Table 5: Potency Results for GLUC-2025-PRS-01**
| Run ID | $EC_{50}$ (pM) | Confidence Interval (95%) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GHS-BIO-2025-01 | 14.2 | 13.8 - 14.6 | Valid |
| GHS-BIO-2025-02 | 14.5 | 14.1 - 14.9 | Valid |
| **Mean Potency** | **14.35** | - | **Assigned 100%** |

---

#### **6.0 Compendial and Safety Testing**

**6.1 Endotoxin (LAL) and Bioburden**
*   **Method:** Kinetic Chromogenic LAL (USP <85>).
*   **Requirement:** < 5 EU/mg.
*   **PRS-01 Result:** < 0.01 EU/mg (Complies).

**6.2 Residual Host Cell Protein (HCP)**
*   **Method:** Third-generation CHO HCP ELISA (GHS-validated).
*   **PRS-01 Result:** 2.4 ppm (Requirement: < 100 ppm).

---

#### **7.0 Assignment of Content**
The protein concentration for **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** was determined by UV-Vis Spectroscopy at $A_{280}$ using an experimentally derived extinction coefficient ($\epsilon$) of $1.58 \text{ mL} \cdot \text{mg}^{-1} \cdot \text{cm}^{-1}$.

*   **Calculated Concentration:** 10.04 mg/mL
*   **Purity Correction Factor:** 0.992 (from RP-HPLC)
*   **Assigned Content:** 9.96 mg/mL (Net peptide content)

---

#### **8.0 Stability and Re-qualification Schedule**
The Primary Reference Standard is stored at -80°C to ensure maximum stability.
*   **Retest Period:** 24 months.
*   **Protocol:** GHS-STAB-PRS-2025.
*   **Next Qualification Due:** JANUARY 2027.

#### **9.0 Conclusion**
The Primary Reference Standard, lot **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**, has been subjected to rigorous analytical, structural, and biological characterization. All results meet or exceed the predefined specifications for purity, identity, and potency. This lot is hereby qualified as the primary anchor for the Glucogen-XR program.

## Stability Data

### **3.2.S.5 Reference Standards or Materials**
#### **3.2.S.5.1 Primary Reference Standard Qualification**
#### **3.2.S.5.1.4 Stability Data (Glucogen-XR Primary Reference Standard, Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01)**

---

### **1. Executive Summary: Stability Program for Primary Reference Standard**

The stability profile of the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01, has been established through a rigorous, multi-faceted longitudinal study designed to ensure the integrity, potency, and purity of the reference material over its intended lifecycle. 

As a GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative cell line (GHS-CHO-001), Glucogen-XR is a complex, glycosylated peptide-polymer conjugate. Given the susceptibility of the peptide backbone to deamidation, oxidation, and aggregation, Google Health Sciences (GHS) has implemented a stability program that exceeds the minimum requirements set forth in **ICH Q1A(R2) (Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products)** and **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)**.

This section details the real-time, accelerated, and stress-testing data for Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01, stored under long-term conditions of -70°C ± 10°C (Ultra-Low Temperature Freezer, Equipment ID: GHS-ULT-9922).

---

### **2. Stability Protocol and Study Design**

#### **2.1 Regulatory Compliance and Guidelines**
The study was conducted in accordance with the following regulatory frameworks:
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Submitting Documentation for the Stability of Human Drugs and Biologics.*
*   **ICH Q5C:** *Stability Testing of Biotechnological/Biological Products.*
*   **USP <1049>:** *Content of Clinical Trial Quality Control and Quality Assurance.*
*   **USP <1225>:** *Validation of Compendial Procedures.*

#### **2.2 Storage Conditions and Sampling Plan**
Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01 was aliquoted into 2.0 mL medical-grade, low-binding cyclic olefin polymer (COP) vials with FluroTec® coated chlorobutyl rubber stoppers. A total of 500 aliquots (1.0 mg/mL concentration) were placed into the stability chambers.

**Table 1: Stability Storage Conditions for PRS GLUC-2025-PRS-01**

| Storage Condition | Temperature (°C) | Relative Humidity (%) | Purpose | Testing Intervals (Months) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Long-Term** | -70°C ± 10°C | N/A | Primary Shelf-Life | 0, 3, 6, 9, 12, 18, 24, 36, 48, 60 |
| **Accelerated** | -20°C ± 5°C | N/A | Degradation Kinetic Study | 0, 1, 3, 6, 9, 12 |
| **Intermediate** | 5°C ± 3°C | Ambient | Excursion/Shipment Simulation | 0, 1, 2, 3, 6 |
| **Stress** | 25°C ± 2°C | 60% RH ± 5% | Forced Degradation Pathway | 0, 0.5, 1, 2, 3 |

---

### **3. Analytical Methodologies and Acceptance Criteria**

The stability of GLUC-2025-PRS-01 is monitored using a stability-indicating profile (SIP). The methods have been validated for specificity, linearity, accuracy, and precision within the GHS Quality Control laboratory.

#### **3.1 High-Performance Size Exclusion Chromatography (HP-SEC)**
*   **Purpose:** Detection of high molecular weight species (HMWS) and low molecular weight fragments (LMWS).
*   **Equipment:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC H-Class Bio System (ID: GHS-LC-004).
*   **Column:** TSKgel G3000SWxl, 7.8 mm x 30 cm.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** Purity (Monomer) ≥ 98.5%; HMWS ≤ 1.0%; LMWS ≤ 0.5%.

#### **3.2 Reversed-Phase Ultra-Performance Liquid Chromatography (RP-UPLC)**
*   **Purpose:** Monitoring of deamidation, oxidation, and hydrophobic variants.
*   **Mobile Phase:** A: 0.1% TFA in H2O; B: 0.1% TFA in Acetonitrile.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** Main Peak Area ≥ 95.0%.

#### **3.3 In-Vitro Biological Potency (GLP-1R Activation Assay)**
*   **Purpose:** Assessment of biological activity via cAMP induction in HEK293 cells expressing human GLP-1R.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:** 80% to 125% of the initial value (T0).

---

### **4. Real-Time Stability Data Summary (-70°C)**

The following table represents the cumulative stability data for the primary reference standard under its intended storage condition.

**Table 2: Longitudinal Stability Results for PRS GLUC-2025-PRS-01 (-70°C)**

| Test Parameter | T=0 (Jan 2025) | T=3 (Apr 2025) | T=6 (Jul 2025) | T=12 (Jan 2026)* |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Clear, Colorless | Clear, Colorless | Clear, Colorless | Clear, Colorless |
| **Concentration (A280)** | 1.02 mg/mL | 1.01 mg/mL | 1.02 mg/mL | 1.02 mg/mL |
| **Purity by SEC (%)** | 99.7% | 99.6% | 99.7% | 99.5% |
| **HMWS (%)** | 0.2% | 0.3% | 0.2% | 0.4% |
| **Purity by RP-UPLC (%)** | 98.8% | 98.7% | 98.5% | 98.4% |
| **Biological Potency (%)** | 102% | 99% | 101% | 100% |
| **pH (USP <791>)** | 6.2 | 6.2 | 6.3 | 6.2 |
| **Sub-visible Particles** | ≥10µm: 120; ≥25µm: 4 | ≥10µm: 135; ≥25µm: 6 | ≥10µm: 110; ≥25µm: 3 | ≥10µm: 142; ≥25µm: 8 |

*\*T=12 and beyond are projected/simulated based on ongoing GHS GLP-1 platform data for homologous sequences.*

---

### **5. Accelerated and Stress Stability Analysis**

To determine the degradation kinetics of Glucogen-XR, Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01 was subjected to elevated temperatures. This data is critical for establishing "Use-Before" dates and handling protocols for secondary standards calibrated against this PRS.

#### **5.1 Arrhenius Analysis of Degradation**
The degradation rate ($k$) was calculated using the decrease in RP-UPLC main peak area.
$$k = A e^{-E_a / RT}$$
Where:
*   $E_a$ (Activation Energy) for Glucogen-XR deamidation: **~85 kJ/mol**.
*   $R$ (Gas Constant): **8.314 J/mol·K**.

**Table 3: Stress Testing Data at 25°C (Forced Degradation)**

| Time Point | RP-UPLC Main Peak (%) | SEC Monomer (%) | Potency (%) | Major Degradant Observed |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **0 Days** | 98.8% | 99.7% | 102% | N/A |
| **7 Days** | 97.2% | 99.4% | 100% | Asn-28 Deamidation |
| **14 Days** | 95.1% | 99.1% | 97% | Asn-28 & Gln-17 Deamidation |
| **30 Days** | 91.4% | 98.5% | 92% | Aggregates/Deamidation |

---

### **6. Statistical Evaluation and Shelf-Life Estimation**

#### **6.1 Linear Regression Analysis**
A linear regression analysis of the purity data (RP-UPLC) over 6 months at -70°C shows no statistically significant downward trend ($p > 0.05$). 

**Regression Equation:** $y = -0.016x + 98.78$
The lower 95% confidence interval for the regression line does not intersect the 95.0% specification limit within a 60-month projection.

#### **6.2 Poolability of Data**
In accordance with **ICH Q1E**, the stability data for GLUC-2025-PRS-01 was compared with the pilot-scale reference batch (GLUC-2024-PILOT-05). The slopes of the degradation curves were found to be statistically similar ($F$-test, $\alpha=0.25$), allowing for an initial shelf-life assignment of 36 months, pending real-time data.

---

### **7. Protocol for Re-Qualification (Annual Monitoring)**

To ensure the continued suitability of the PRS, a Re-qualification Protocol (GHS-SOP-6621) is executed every 12 months.

**Step-by-Step Re-qualification Procedure:**
1.  **Vial Retrieval:** Withdraw 3 vials of GLUC-2025-PRS-01 from the ULT freezer (-70°C).
2.  **Thawing:** Thaw at 2-8°C for 4 hours; do not vortex.
3.  **Physical Inspection:** Verify against the Color, Clarity, and Opalescence standards (USP <709>).
4.  **Content Measurement:** Perform $A_{280}$ protein concentration check (Extinction Coefficient: $1.45 \text{ mL}\cdot\text{mg}^{-1}\cdot\text{cm}^{-1}$).
5.  **Purity Assessment:** Execute HP-SEC and RP-UPLC in triplicate.
6.  **Bioactivity Assessment:** Compare $EC_{50}$ of the PRS against the freshly prepared working standard.
7.  **Comparison to T0:** If the purity has dropped by $>1.0\%$ from the T=0 value, an Investigation (CAPA) is initiated to evaluate the impact on all clinical assays calibrated against this standard.

---

### **8. Reference Standards Stability Conclusion**

Based on the 6-month real-time data and 30-day stress data, the Primary Reference Standard **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** demonstrates exceptional stability when stored at -70°C. The use of the GHS-CHO-001 cell line and optimized formulation (Histidine-Sucrose-Polysorbate 20) effectively mitigates the common pathways of peptide degradation.

The assigned shelf-life is currently **36 months**, supported by ongoing real-time studies. This standard remains the "Gold Standard" for all subsequent qualification of Working Reference Standards (WRS) used in the commercial release of Glucogen-XR.

---

### **1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE**

This document provides the comprehensive **Certificate of Analysis (CoA)** and supporting qualification data for the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**, designated as Batch **GLUC-2025-PRS-01**. 

As a GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via recombinant DNA technology in the proprietary **GHS-CHO-001** (CHO-K1 GS knockout) cell line, the qualification of the Primary Reference Standard is paramount to ensuring the longitudinal consistency of all subsequent Working Reference Standards (WRS) and clinical/commercial drug substance (DS) and drug product (DP) batches. This qualification follows the mandates of **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q2(R1)** (Validation of Analytical Procedures).

### **4.0 DETAILED ANALYTICAL CHARACTERIZATION PROCEDURES**

#### **4.1 Intact Mass Analysis by Electrospray Ionization Time-of-Flight (ESI-TOF) MS**
**Method ID: GHS-MS-0042**

**Procedure:**
1.  **Sample Preparation:** 50 µg of GLUC-2025-PRS-01 is diluted in 0.1% Formic Acid (FA) to a concentration of 1.0 mg/mL.
2.  **Chromatographic Separation:** Utilizing an Agilent 1290 Infinity II LC system. Column: PLRP-S 1000Å (2.1 x 50 mm). Mobile Phase A: 0.1% FA in Water; Mobile Phase B: 0.1% FA in Acetonitrile.
3.  **MS Acquisition:** Scanned from 500 to 4000 m/z.
4.  **Deconvolution:** Performed using Maximum Entropy algorithm (MassHunter software).

**Calculation of Theoretical Mass:**
The theoretical mass of the Glucogen-XR glucapeptide (C₁₈₈₂H₂₉₄₅N₅₀₅O₅₇₆S₁₄) is calculated based on the primary amino acid sequence and the specific extended-release conjugation moiety (PEG-derivative).
*   Theoretical: 42,450.54 Da.
*   Measured (GLUC-2025-PRS-01): 42,451.21 Da.
*   **Deviation:** +0.67 Da (Within instrument tolerance of ±2.0 Da).

#### **4.2 Purity Determination by Size Exclusion HPLC (SE-HPLC)**
**Method ID: GHS-QC-HPLC-01**

**Method Parameters:**
*   **Column:** TSKgel G3000SWxl (7.8 mm ID x 30 cm, 5 µm).
*   **Mobile Phase:** 50 mM Sodium Phosphate, 300 mM NaCl, pH 7.0.
*   **Flow Rate:** 0.5 mL/min.
*   **Detection:** UV at 214 nm.
*   **Injection Volume:** 20 µL (400 µg load).

**Data Summary for Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01:**

| Peak Name | Retention Time (min) | Relative Area (%) | Resolution (USP) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **HMW Species (Aggregate)** | 11.24 | 0.18 | N/A |
| **Dimer** | 13.85 | 0.04 | 1.85 |
| **Main Peak (Monomer)** | 16.42 | 99.78 | 2.40 |
| **LMW Species** | 21.15 | < 0.01 | 4.10 |

#### **4.3 Potency Determination: GLP-1 Receptor Activation Bioassay**
**Method ID: GHS-BIO-77**

The biological activity of GLUC-2025-PRS-01 is determined using a reporter gene assay in a HEK293 cell line stably transfected with the human GLP-1 receptor (GLP-1R) and a cAMP-response element (CRE) driving luciferase expression.

**Step-by-Step Protocol:**
1.  **Cell Seeding:** HEK293-hGLP1R cells are seeded at 2.5 x 10⁴ cells/well in a 96-well white-walled plate.
2.  **Incubation:** Cells are incubated for 24 hours at 37°C, 5% CO₂.
3.  **Serial Dilution:** The PRS is diluted in Assay Buffer (DMEM/F12 + 0.1% BSA) in a 10-point serial dilution (range: 0.001 nM to 100 nM).
4.  **Stimulation:** Dilutions are added to the cells and incubated for 4 hours.
5.  **Detection:** One-Glo™ Luciferase Reagent is added. Luminescence is measured using a SpectraMax M5e plate reader.
6.  **Data Analysis:** Dose-response curves are fitted using a 4-parameter logistic (4PL) model.

**Statistical Results for GLUC-2025-PRS-01:**
*   **EC₅₀ (PRS):** 0.42 nM
*   **EC₅₀ (Historical Control):** 0.41 nM
*   **Relative Potency:** 1.02 (102%)
*   **95% Confidence Interval:** 98.4% – 105.1%
*   **Slope:** 1.12 (Parallelism confirmed; p > 0.05)

---

### **5.0 IMPURITY PROFILE AND CHARACTERIZATION**

#### **5.1 Host Cell Protein (HCP) Analysis**
HCP levels were quantified using a third-generation sandwich ELISA specific to the GHS-CHO-001 cell line.

| Sample Replicate | Measured Conc. (ng/mL) | Corrected for Dilution | Result (ppm) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Rep 1** | 2.38 | 1:20 | 2.38 |
| **Rep 2** | 2.45 | 1:20 | 2.45 |
| **Rep 3** | 2.37 | 1:20 | 2.37 |
| **Mean** | **N/A** | **N/A** | **2.4 ppm** |

#### **5.2 Glycosylation and Post-Translational Modifications (PTMs)**
While Glucogen-XR is a non-glycosylated peptide, specific emphasis is placed on the **N-terminal Glu (Pyroglutamate)** and **C-terminal Deamidation** levels.

*   **N-terminal Pyro-Glu:** 0.4% (Assessed by Peptide Mapping LC-MS/MS)
*   **Deamidation (Asn¹²):** 0.8%
*   **Oxidation (Met²²):** 0.15%

---

### **6.0 STABILITY AND RE-QUALIFICATION PROGRAM**

The Primary Reference Standard GLUC-2025-PRS-01 is entered into a formal long-term stability study (Protocol: **GHS-STAB-PRS-01**).

**Testing Intervals:** 0, 3, 6, 9, 12, 18, 24, 36, 48, and 60 months.
**Monitoring Parameters:**
*   Purity by SE-HPLC and RP-HPLC.
*   Charge heterogeneity by iCE3.
*   Potency by Cell-based Bioassay.

**Re-qualification Criteria:**
The standard remains valid as long as the purity by SE-HPLC remains ≥ 98.5% and potency remains within 90-110% of the initial (T0) value.

# Working Reference Standards

## Preparation from Primary Standard

### **3.2.S.5. REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **Section 3.2.S.5.2: Working Reference Standards**
#### **Subsection: Preparation from Primary Standard (WRS-GXR-002)**

---

### **1.0 SCOPE AND OBJECTIVE**
This subsection details the comprehensive procedural framework, analytical validation, and qualification protocols for the conversion of the **Glucogen-XR Primary Reference Standard (PRS-GXR-001)** into the **Glucogen-XR Working Reference Standard (WRS-GXR-002)**. 

The objective of this preparation is to establish a secondary standard of high fidelity, ensuring that all routine batch release testing, stability monitoring, and characterization studies are anchored to a consistent, well-characterized material. This process is governed by the Quality Management System (QMS) of Google Health Sciences and adheres strictly to **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **USP <1029> (Good Documentation Guidelines)**.

---

### **2.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDELINES**
The preparation and qualification of WRS-GXR-002 are conducted in accordance with the following regulatory frameworks:
*   **ICH Q7:** Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients.
*   **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures: Text and Methodology.
*   **USP <1225>:** Validation of Compendial Procedures.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (July 2015).
*   **ISO/IEC 17025:2017:** General requirements for the competence of testing and calibration laboratories.

---

### **3.0 STARTING MATERIALS AND CRITICAL REAGENTS**

#### **3.1 Primary Reference Standard (PRS) Details**
The PRS used for this conversion is derived from the Master Cell Bank (MCB) GHS-CHO-001 and has undergone exhaustive structural characterization (including NMR and X-ray crystallography).

| Material Attribute | Specification/Identity | Batch Number |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Material Name** | Glucogen-XR (Primary) | PRS-GXR-001 |
| **Originating Bulk Drug Substance** | GLUC-2024-001-ALPHA | N/A |
| **Assigned Potency (Purity Corrected)** | 99.8% (w/w) | N/A |
| **Storage Temperature** | -80°C ± 5°C | N/A |
| **Container Closure System** | 2.0 mL Cryovial, USP Class VI | N/A |

#### **3.2 Diluents and Buffers**
All reagents are of ACS Grade or higher.
*   **Buffer A (Dilution Buffer):** 20 mM Histidine-HCl, 100 mM NaCl, 0.02% Polysorbate 80, pH 6.0.
*   **Water Source:** USP/EP Grade Water for Injection (WFI), TOC < 50 ppb.

---

### **4.0 PREPARATION PROTOCOL (SOP-GHS-772-GXR)**

#### **4.1 Environmental Controls**
The preparation is conducted within the Google Health Sciences Reference Standard Suite (Room R-102), classified as an ISO Class 5 (Grade A) environment within an ISO Class 7 background. 
*   **Temperature:** 20°C to 22°C.
*   **Relative Humidity:** 45% ± 5%.
*   **Lighting:** UV-filtered.

#### **4.2 Step-by-Step Aliquoting Procedure**
1.  **Thawing:** Retrieve five (5) vials of PRS-GXR-001 from ultra-low temperature storage. Thaw at 2-8°C for 12 hours. Do not vortex. Gently invert 10 times to ensure homogeneity.
2.  **Pooling:** Under aseptic conditions, pool the contents into a pre-chilled, sterile 500 mL borosilicate glass vessel (Equipment ID: GHS-VES-09).
3.  **Concentration Adjustment:** Measure the protein concentration using UV-Vis Spectroscopy ($A_{280}$, Extinction Coefficient $\epsilon = 1.25 \text{ L}\cdot\text{g}^{-1}\cdot\text{cm}^{-1}$). 
    *   *Calculation:* $C_{\text{final}} = (C_{\text{initial}} \times V_{\text{initial}}) / V_{\text{target}}$.
4.  **Filtration:** Sterilize the bulk solution using a 0.22 $\mu$m PVDF low-protein binding filter (Millipore Millex-GV).
5.  **Aliquoting:** Using an automated high-precision micropipetting system (Eppendorf E3x), dispense 500 $\mu$L of the solution into 1,000 pre-labeled, sterile USP Type I clear glass vials.
6.  **Lyophilization (Optional/Batch Specific):** For WRS-GXR-002, the material is maintained in a liquid-frozen state.
7.  **Sealing:** Vials are stoppered with FluroTec® coated chlorobutyl rubber stoppers and crimped with aluminum seals.

---

### **5.0 ANALYTICAL QUALIFICATION DATA (BATCH: GLUC-2025-WRS01)**

| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual (Ph. Eur. 2.2.1) | Clear to opalescent | Clear | Clear |
| **Identity (RT)** | RP-HPLC | Matches PRS $\pm$ 2% | 14.2 min | 14.1 min |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SE-HPLC | $\ge$ 98.0% | 99.4% | 99.3% |
| **Charge Heterogeneity** | cIEF | Report Profile | Main Peak: 62% | Main Peak: 61.8% |
| **Potency (In Vitro)** | GLP-1R Bioassay | 80% - 125% of PRS | 100% (Fixed) | 102% |
| **Host Cell Protein** | ELISA (GHS-CHO) | $\le$ 10 ppm | 2.1 ppm | 2.3 ppm |
| **Endotoxin** | LAL (USP <85>) | $\le$ 0.5 EU/mg | < 0.1 EU/mg | < 0.1 EU/mg |

### **7.0 ASSIGNMENT OF EXPIRY AND RETEST PERIODS**

The WRS-GXR-002 is assigned an initial shelf-life of 24 months when stored at -80°C $\pm$ 5°C. This is supported by the **Standard Qualification Program (SQP-GXR-05)**, which requires:
1.  **Real-Time Stability:** Testing at $T=0, 3, 6, 12, 18,$ and $24$ months.
2.  **In-Use Stability:** Once thawed, the WRS is stable at 2-8°C for a maximum of 48 hours. **Do not re-freeze.**
3.  **Bridge Testing:** A minimum of 6 months prior to the expiration of WRS-GXR-002, a new working standard (WRS-GXR-003) must be prepared and bridged against PRS-GXR-001.

## Qualification Against Primary Standard

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
#### 3.2.S.5.2 Working Reference Standards
#### 3.2.S.5.2.1 Qualification Against Primary Standard

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This section details the rigorous qualification protocol, analytical methodology, and formal acceptance criteria utilized by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)** for the qualification of the **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** Working Reference Standard (WRS) against the established Primary Reference Standard (PRS). 

The qualification process is designed to ensure that the WRS maintains a direct, documented link of traceability to the PRS, thereby ensuring the accuracy, precision, and consistency of all downstream analytical testing, including Release Testing, Stability Monitoring, and Characterization Studies. This qualification follows the strategic requirements outlined in **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q2(R2)** (Validation of Analytical Procedures).

---

### 2.0 TRACEABILITY AND BATCH IDENTIFICATION

The current Working Reference Standard, identified as **Batch GLUC-2025-WRS-04**, was derived from a highly purified bulk drug substance lot produced at the 3000 Innovation Drive facility. 

#### Table 2.1: Identification of Standards
| Attribute | Primary Reference Standard (PRS) | Working Reference Standard (WRS) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Batch Number** | GLUC-2023-PRS-01 | GLUC-2025-WRS-04 |
| **Manufacturing Date** | 12-Oct-2023 | 14-Jan-2025 |
| **Source Lot** | DS-EXP-9921 | DS-PROD-4402 |
| **Storage Temperature** | -80°C ± 5°C | -80°C ± 5°C |
| **Container/Closure** | 2.0 mL Cryovial (USP Class VI) | 2.0 mL Cryovial (USP Class VI) |
| **Fill Volume** | 0.5 mL | 0.5 mL |
| **Concentration (Nominal)** | 10.0 mg/mL | 10.0 mg/mL |

---

### 3.0 QUALIFICATION STRATEGY AND ANALYTICAL MATRIX

The qualification protocol (Document ID: GHS-QC-PRO-9982) employs a "Head-to-Head" comparison strategy. The WRS is analyzed in parallel with the PRS in a minimum of six (6) independent assays performed by three (3) different analysts over a period of five (5) working days to account for inter-day and inter-analyst variability.

#### 3.1 Tiered Testing Approach
Qualification is bifurcated into:
1.  **Tier 1: Identity and Primary Structure** (Confirmation of the amino acid sequence and post-translational modifications).
2.  **Tier 2: Purity and Impurity Profile** (Assessment of product-related variants and process-related impurities).
3.  **Tier 3: Potency and Biological Activity** (Cell-based GLP-1 receptor activation assay).
4.  **Tier 4: Physico-chemical properties** (Concentration, pH, Osmolality).

---

### 4.0 DETAILED ANALYTICAL PROTOCOLS

#### 4.1 Protocol for Purity Assessment by RP-HPLC
**Method ID:** MET-00122 (Reversed-Phase High-Performance Liquid Chromatography)
**Equipment:** Agilent 1290 Infinity II LC System (Asset ID: GHS-LC-09)
**Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC Peptide CSH C18, 130Å, 1.7 µm, 2.1 mm X 150 mm

**Procedure:**
1.  Equilibrate the column with 95% Mobile Phase A (0.1% TFA in Water) and 5% Mobile Phase B (0.1% TFA in Acetonitrile).
2.  Set flow rate to 0.3 mL/min and column temperature to 45°C.
3.  Inject 10 µL of PRS (diluted to 1.0 mg/mL).
4.  Inject 10 µL of WRS (diluted to 1.0 mg/mL).
5.  Perform gradient elution: 5% B to 45% B over 40 minutes.
6.  Monitor UV absorbance at 214 nm and 280 nm.

**Calculations:**
The Relative Purity is calculated using the area under the curve (AUC):
$$Purity (\%) = \left( \frac{Area_{Main Peak}}{\sum Area_{All Peaks}} \right) \times 100$$

#### 4.2 Protocol for Biological Potency (In Vitro Bioassay)
**Method ID:** MET-00550 (GLP-1R cAMP Activation Assay)
**Cell Line:** CHO-K1 cells stably expressing the human GLP-1 receptor (GHS-CHO-001 derivative).

**Procedure:**
1.  Seed cells in 96-well plates at a density of $5 \times 10^4$ cells/well.
2.  Prepare a 10-point serial dilution of both PRS and WRS (Range: 0.001 nM to 100 nM).
3.  Incubate cells with standards for 30 minutes at 37°C.
4.  Measure intracellular cAMP levels using a TR-FRET detection kit (LANCE® Ultra).
5.  Analyze data using a 4-parameter logistic (4PL) regression model.

**Statistical Requirement:**
The Dose-Response curves must meet the Parallelism Criterion (F-test, $p > 0.05$). The Relative Potency is calculated as:
$$Rel. Potency = \frac{EC_{50} (PRS)}{EC_{50} (WRS)}$$

---

### 5.0 ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA FOR WRS QUALIFICATION

For **GLUC-2025-WRS-04** to be certified as a Working Reference Standard, it must meet the following pre-defined specifications relative to **GLUC-2023-PRS-01**.

#### Table 5.1: Comparative Acceptance Criteria
| Test Parameter | Methodology | Acceptance Criteria (Relative to PRS) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Identity (MW)** | ESI-TOF MS | Consistent with PRS (± 2 Da) |
| **Identity (Sequence)** | Peptide Mapping | Correlation Coefficient (r) ≥ 0.98 |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SEC-HPLC | ≥ 98.0%; Difference from PRS ≤ 0.5% |
| **Purity (RP)** | RP-HPLC | ≥ 95.0%; Difference from PRS ≤ 1.0% |
| **Charge Heterogeneity** | cIEF | Profile comparable to PRS (pI range 4.5–5.2) |
| **Potency (Biological)** | Cell-based cAMP | 80% – 125% of PRS activity |
| **Protein Content** | UV (A280) | 9.5 – 10.5 mg/mL (Target: 10.0) |

---

### 6.0 RESULTS OF QUALIFICATION (BATCH GLUC-2025-WRS-04)

The following data summarizes the qualification of the new WRS against the PRS.

#### 6.1 Summary of Chromatographic Purity
Data represents the mean of $n=6$ independent replicates.

#### Table 6.1: Comparative Purity Data
| Analyte | PRS (GLUC-2023-PRS-01) | WRS (GLUC-2025-WRS-04) | Delta (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Main Peak (%) | 97.82 | 97.65 | -0.17 |
| Total Impurities (%) | 2.18 | 2.35 | +0.17 |
| High MW Species (%) | 0.45 | 0.48 | +0.03 |
| Acidic Variants (%) | 1.12 | 1.20 | +0.08 |

#### 6.2 Potency Results and Statistical Analysis
The relative potency of the WRS was determined via the GLP-1R activation assay.

*   **PRS $EC_{50}$ Mean:** 1.22 nM (SD: 0.05)
*   **WRS $EC_{50}$ Mean:** 1.25 nM (SD: 0.07)
*   **Calculated Relative Potency:** 0.976 (97.6%)
*   **95% Confidence Interval:** 94.2% – 101.1%
*   **Parallelism (Slope Ratio):** 0.992 (Passes criteria 0.90 – 1.10)

---

### 7.0 MAINTENANCE AND STABILITY OF THE WORKING STANDARD

#### 7.1 Storage Conditions
The WRS is stored in the GHS Central Biologics Repository (Building 4) at $-80^{\circ}C \pm 5^{\circ}C$ in ultra-low temperature freezers (Asset ID: GHS-FRZ-402) equipped with 24/7 continuous temperature monitoring and redundant power backups.

#### 7.2 Protocol for Re-qualification (Bridging)
The WRS has an initial shelf life of 24 months. Re-qualification against the PRS is required:
1.  Every 24 months (± 1 month).
2.  If any trend toward degradation is observed in the annual stability program.
3.  If any significant system suitability failures occur during routine use.

#### 7.3 Use and Handling
*   WRS vials are for single-use only to avoid freeze-thaw degradation.
*   Vials must be thawed on ice for 30 minutes prior to use.
*   Any remaining material after 8 hours at room temperature must be discarded.

---

### 8.0 CONCLUSION

The data generated during the qualification of **GLUC-2025-WRS-04** demonstrates that the material is analytically comparable to the Primary Reference Standard **GLUC-2023-PRS-01**. All pre-defined acceptance criteria for identity, purity, and potency were met. Therefore, **GLUC-2025-WRS-04** is formally approved for use as the Working Reference Standard for all Glucogen-XR drug substance and drug product analytical procedures.

## Assignment of Expiry Date

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
#### 3.2.S.5.2 Working Reference Standards
#### 3.2.S.5.2.4 Assignment of Expiry Date

---

### 1.0 PURPOSE AND SCOPE

This subsection details the systematic approach, mathematical models, and regulatory rationale employed by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)** for the assignment, extension, and management of expiration dates (and retest periods) for the **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** Working Reference Standard (WRS). 

The expiration dating strategy for Glucogen-XR WRS (Current Lot: **GLUC-2025-WRS-01**) is designed to ensure the highest degree of analytical fidelity throughout the lifecycle of the drug substance (DS) and drug product (DP) testing programs. This protocol adheres strictly to **ICH Q1A(R2)** (*Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products*), **ICH Q6B** (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*), and **USP <11>** (*USP Reference Standards*).

---

### 2.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDELINES

The assignment of the expiry date for the Glucogen-XR WRS is governed by the following regulatory framework:

*   **FDA 21 CFR 211.166:** Stability Testing Requirements.
*   **ICH Q1E:** Evaluation of Stability Data (Linear Regression and Poolability).
*   **USP <1226>:** Verification of Compendial Procedures.
*   **USP <1010>:** Analytical Data—Interpretation and Treatment.
*   **ISO 17034:2016:** General requirements for the competence of reference material producers.

---

### 3.0 STRATEGY FOR EXPIRY ASSIGNMENT

Unlike the primary reference standard (PRS), which is characterized using absolute physical constants, the Working Reference Standard (WRS) is a secondary standard calibrated against the PRS. Consequently, the expiry date of the WRS is constrained by two factors:
1.  The inherent biochemical stability of the glucapeptide molecule.
2.  The expiration or re-qualification date of the Primary Reference Standard (GLUC-2024-PRS-01) against which it was qualified.

#### 3.1 Initial Expiry Assignment (T=0)
Upon successful qualification (Protocol GHS-QC-PRO-9921), a new WRS batch is assigned an **initial expiry date of 24 months** from the date of fill, provided the material is stored at the recommended long-term storage condition of **-80°C ± 10°C**.

#### 3.2 Retest and Extension Protocol
GHS utilizes a "Rolling Expiry" model. Six months prior to the nominal expiry of the WRS, a formal stability assessment is conducted. If the stability data meets the pre-defined Acceptance Criteria (see Section 5.0), the expiry date may be extended in 12-month increments.

---

### 4.0 STABILITY PROGRAM DATA FOR EXPIRY SUPPORT (BATCH GLUC-2025-WRS-01)

The following table summarizes the real-time stability data used to justify the current 24-month expiry assignment for the active WRS batch.

**Table 3.2.S.5.2.4-1: Stability Monitoring Data for Glucogen-XR WRS (Lot: GLUC-2025-WRS-01)**
*Storage Condition: -80°C ± 10°C | Container: 2.0 mL Cryogenic Polypropylene Vials*

| Time Point (Months) | Test Date | Batch Number | Purity by RP-HPLC (%) | Purity by SE-HPLC (%) | Potency (In Vitro Bioassay) | Water Content (KF) | Visual Appearance |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **0 (Release)** | 12-JAN-2025 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | 99.42% | 99.85% | 102% of PRS | 0.45% w/w | Clear Lyophilisate |
| **3** | 12-APR-2025 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | 99.40% | 99.84% | 101% of PRS | 0.46% w/w | Clear Lyophilisate |
| **6** | 12-JUL-2025 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | 99.38% | 99.82% | 103% of PRS | 0.44% w/w | Clear Lyophilisate |
| **9** | 12-OCT-2025 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | 99.41% | 99.80% | 100% of PRS | 0.47% w/w | Clear Lyophilisate |
| **12** | 12-JAN-2026 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | 99.35% | 99.78% | 102% of PRS | 0.48% w/w | Clear Lyophilisate |
| **18 (Proposed)** | 12-JUL-2026 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | TBD | TBD | TBD | TBD | TBD |
| **24 (Proposed)** | 12-JAN-2027 | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | TBD | TBD | TBD | TBD | TBD |

---

### 5.0 MATHEMATICAL MODEL FOR SHELF-LIFE ESTIMATION

To ensure the expiry date is scientifically robust, GHS applies a 95% confidence interval (CI) to the degradation slope of the most sensitive stability-indicating parameter (Purity by RP-HPLC).

#### 5.1 Linear Regression Equation
The degradation rate ($k$) is calculated using:
$$C_t = C_0 - kt$$
Where:
*   $C_t$ = Concentration/Purity at time $t$
*   $C_0$ = Initial Purity
*   $k$ = Degradation rate constant
*   $t$ = Time in months

#### 5.2 Statistical Significance (p-value)
A p-value for the slope is calculated. If $p > 0.25$, the data from different batches may be pooled to extend the expiry of the entire WRS library.

**Table 3.2.S.5.2.4-2: Statistical Regression Analysis of Purity Data**

| Parameter | Value |
| :--- | :--- |
| Slope (k) | -0.0051% / month |
| Intercept ($C_0$) | 99.42% |
| Correlation Coefficient ($R^2$) | 0.924 |
| Lower 95% Confidence Limit at 24M | 98.92% |
| **Specification Limit** | **≥ 97.0%** |

Based on this projection, the lower 95% CI remains well above the specification limit for 24 months, justifying the initial expiry assignment.

---

### 6.0 STEP-BY-STEP PROTOCOL FOR EXPIRY EXTENSION (GHS-QC-SOP-0442)

The following protocol is executed by the Quality Control (QC) Department at Google Health Sciences to extend the life of a WRS batch.

**Step 1: Inventory Verification**
*   Verify that at least 150 vials of Lot GLUC-2025-WRS-01 remain in the Ultra-Low Temperature (ULT) freezer (**Asset ID: GHS-ULT-09**).

**Step 2: Comparative Testing**
*   Perform side-by-side analysis of the WRS against the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) using the following methods:
    1.  **RP-HPLC (GHS-MTH-102):** Assessment of related substances and deamidation.
    2.  **SE-HPLC (GHS-MTH-105):** Assessment of high-molecular-weight species (aggregates).
    3.  **HIC-HPLC (GHS-MTH-110):** Assessment of oxidation variants (Met-sulfoxide).

**Step 3: Evaluation of "Usage Drift"**
*   Analyze the "Usage Log" for the WRS. Calculate the number of times the storage box has been removed from the -80°C environment.
*   *Requirement:* Total cumulative "out-of-storage" time must not exceed 4 hours per year to maintain the assigned expiry.

**Step 4: Quality Assurance Review**
*   The Stability Review Board (SRB) reviews the cumulative data. If the purity drop is $< 0.5\%$ from T=0 and all specifications are met, a **Certificate of Analysis (CoA) Addendum** is issued, updating the expiry date.

---

### 7.0 IMPACT OF PRIMARY REFERENCE STANDARD (PRS) EXPIRY

The WRS expiry is intrinsically linked to the PRS lifecycle.

1.  If the **Primary Reference Standard (GLUC-2024-PRS-01)** expires, all dependent Working Standards (**GLUC-2025-WRS-XX**) must be re-qualified against the *newly* established PRS batch (e.g., GLUC-2026-PRS-01).
2.  The re-qualification must include a full "Identity, Purity, Potency" battery to ensure no bias was introduced during the transition.

**Table 3.2.S.5.2.4-3: Historical Expiry Assignments for Glucapeptide Standards**

| Standard ID | Type | Manufacture Date | Initial Expiry | Final Expiry (Post-Extension) | Reason for Retirement |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2021-WRS-05 | WRS | 10-MAY-2021 | 10-MAY-2023 | 10-MAY-2025 | Depletion of Stock |
| GLUC-2023-WRS-01 | WRS | 14-FEB-2023 | 14-FEB-2025 | N/A | Superseded by 2025 Lot |
| **GLUC-2025-WRS-01** | **WRS** | **12-JAN-2025** | **12-JAN-2027** | **TBD** | **Active Lot** |

---

### 8.0 STORAGE CONDITIONS AND PHOTODETERIORATION CONTROLS

The expiry date of **12-JAN-2027** for GLUC-2025-WRS-01 is only valid if the following conditions are met:
*   **Temperature:** -80°C ± 10°C (Continuous monitoring via Google Cloud IoT Core Temperature Sensors).
*   **Light:** Protected from light. Vials are stored in secondary opaque cardboard containers.
*   **Humidity:** Not applicable for frozen, hermetically sealed vials; however, the lyophilisate is protected via a nitrogen-overlay headspace.

If a deviation occurs (e.g., a "Temperature Excursion" where $T > -60°C$ for $>30$ minutes), the expiry date is immediately suspended pending an **Investigative Stability Study (ISS)**.

---

### 9.0 CONCLUSION

The assignment of the 24-month expiry for **Glucogen-XR WRS (GLUC-2025-WRS-01)** is based on extensive real-time stability data, statistical forecasting using linear regression of high-sensitivity HPLC data, and adherence to ICH Q1E guidelines. Google Health Sciences maintains a rigorous re-testing schedule every 12 months post-initial expiry to ensure the continued suitability of the standard for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapeutic monitoring.

# Storage and Handling

## Storage Conditions and Location

### 3.2.S.5 Reference Standards or Materials
#### 3.2.S.5.2 Storage and Handling
##### 3.2.S.5.2.1 Storage Conditions and Location

The establishment of rigorous storage and handling protocols for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) reference standards is critical to ensuring the integrity, potency, and stability of the material used in all comparative analytical testing. This section details the environmental specifications, physical location, inventory management systems, and contingency protocols for the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standard (WRS).

---

### I. Environmental Specifications and Validated Storage Parameters

The Glucogen-XR drug substance is a highly sensitive synthetic peptide-polymer conjugate. Degradation pathways, including deamidation at the Asn-28 residue and oxidation of the Met-14 equivalent, are highly temperature-dependent. Consequently, the storage conditions have been defined based on comprehensive accelerated and long-term stability data (refer to Section 3.2.S.7).

#### Table 1: Defined Storage Parameters for Glucogen-XR Reference Standards

| Parameter | Specification | Acceptable Range | Monitoring Frequency | Equipment ID |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary Temp.** | -70°C | -65°C to -85°C | Continuous (1-min logs) | ULT-FRZ-GHS-099 |
| **Secondary Temp.**| -20°C (Short-term) | -15°C to -25°C | Continuous (5-min logs) | FRZ-STD-GHS-042 |
| **Humidity** | Ambient | N/A (Hermetically Sealed) | Monthly Check | N/A |
| **Light Exposure** | Total Darkness | 0 Lux (Amber Vials) | Per Access Event | N/A |
| **Vibration** | < 0.001g | Negligible | Quarterly | VIB-MON-004 |

**1.1 Temperature Kinetic Mean (MKT) Calculations**
To ensure the stability of the reference standards, any excursion is evaluated using the Mean Kinetic Temperature formula as per USP <1150>:

$$T_k = \frac{\Delta H / R}{-\ln \left( \frac{e^{-\Delta H / RT_1} + e^{-\Delta H / RT_2} + \dots + e^{-\Delta H / RT_n}}{n} \right)}$$

Where:
*   $\Delta H$ = Activation energy for Glucogen-XR degradation (determined as 82.4 kJ/mol).
*   $R$ = Universal gas constant ($0.0083144$ kJ/mol·K).
*   $T$ = Absolute temperature in Kelvin.

---

### II. Physical Location and Facility Infrastructure

All reference standards are maintained at the Google Health Sciences (GHS) Reference Material Repository located at the South San Francisco manufacturing site.

**2.1 Primary Repository Site**
*   **Facility:** Google Health Sciences - Building 4, Suite 200 (Restricted Access Zone).
*   **Address:** 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080, USA.
*   **Room Specification:** ISO Class 8 (Grade D) environment for handling and secondary packaging.

**2.2 Storage Equipment Specifications**
Reference standards are housed in Ultra-Low Temperature (ULT) Freezers (Model: GHS-CryoMax 9000).
*   **Redundancy:** Dual compressors with independent cooling loops.
*   **Backup Power:** Connected to the campus-wide Uninterruptible Power Supply (UPS) and secondary diesel generators (Tier IV compliant).
*   **Security:** Biometric (Iris/Fingerprint) access control required for entry into the storage suite and individual freezer units.

#### Table 2: Detailed Equipment Inventory for Reference Standard Storage

| Batch Type | Storage Unit ID | Location | Capacity | Calibration Due Date |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **PRS (Primary)** | ULT-GHS-099-A | Zone A, Shelf 1 | 500 Vials | 12-OCT-2025 |
| **PRS (Backup)** | ULT-GHS-104-B | Zone C, Shelf 2 | 500 Vials | 15-NOV-2025 |
| **WRS (Working)** | ULT-GHS-112-W | Zone B, Shelf 4 | 2000 Vials | 08-SEP-2025 |
| **Retains** | FRZ-GHS-002-R | Zone D, Shelf 1 | 1000 Vials | 01-JAN-2026 |

---

### III. Reference Standard Batch Assignments and Inventory

As of the date of this submission, the following batches of Glucogen-XR have been designated and qualified as Reference Standards.

#### Table 3: Current Reference Standard Inventory Data

| Batch Number | Designation | Date of Manufacture | Quantity (Vials) | Purity (RP-HPLC) | Expiry/Retest Date |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |

| **GLUC-2025-109** | Qualification | 01-MAY-2025 | 500 | 99.85% | 01-MAY-2030 |

---

### IV. Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs) for Handling

To minimize freeze-thaw degradation and mechanical shear, the following SOPs are strictly enforced.

#### SOP-GHS-QC-4402: Retrieval and Aliquoting of Glucogen-XR Standards

1.  **Authorization:** Only Grade 4 Lead Analytical Scientists or higher are authorized to remove PRS vials.
2.  **Environmental Stabilization:** Vials must be removed from the ULT freezer and placed immediately into a portable cryogenic carrier (-70°C) for transport to the analytical bench.
3.  **Thawing Protocol:** 
    *   Place vial in a controlled environment at 2-8°C for exactly 45 minutes.
    *   Gently invert the vial three (3) times. **DO NOT VORTEX.**
    *   Allow to reach room temperature (20-25°C) for no more than 10 minutes prior to sampling.
4.  **Re-Freezing Policy:** 
    *   **PRS:** No re-freezing permitted. Any unused portion of a PRS vial must be discarded or redesignated as "Training Material Only."
    *   **WRS:** A maximum of two (2) freeze-thaw cycles is permitted, provided the total time out of storage does not exceed 4 hours per cycle.

#### SOP-GHS-QC-4405: Inventory Reconciliation
*   A "Reference Standard Usage Log" (Form GHS-772) must be updated in real-time via the Cloud LIMS (Laboratory Information Management System).
*   Mandatory fields: Batch No., Vial ID, Purpose of Use (e.g., Release Testing for Lot GLUC-2025-XXX), Volume Withdrawn, Remaining Volume, and Analyst Signature.

---

### V. Contingency and Disaster Recovery

In accordance with ICH Q5C and FDA Quality Systems Regulations, Google Health Sciences maintains a comprehensive Disaster Recovery Plan (DRP-GHS-LIFE-01).

**5.1 Alarm Thresholds**
*   **Level 1 (Warning):** Temp > -65°C for > 10 minutes. Triggers SMS/Email to QC Manager.
*   **Level 2 (Critical):** Temp > -60°C for > 5 minutes. Triggers Building Security and Facilities Emergency Team.
*   **Level 3 (Catastrophic):** Mechanical failure of cooling loop. Automatic transfer of samples to backup ULT freezer (ULT-GHS-104-B) via Liquid Nitrogen (LN2) stabilized transport carts.

**5.2 LN2 Backup System**
All ULT freezers are equipped with a liquid nitrogen injection backup system. In the event of a total power and generator failure, the LN2 system is calibrated to maintain the internal temperature at < -65°C for a minimum of 72 hours.

---

### VI. Regulatory Compliance and Quality Assurance

The storage conditions described herein are in full compliance with:
*   **USP <1117>** Microbiological Best Laboratory Practices.
*   **USP <659>** Packaging and Storage Requirements.
*   **ICH Q7 Section 11.17** regarding the storage of Reference Standards.
*   **21 CFR Part 211.166** Stability Testing requirements.

**6.1 Annual Retest Program**
Reference standards undergo a comprehensive "Stability Verification Protocol" annually. This includes:
1.  Full Monograph Testing (as per Section 3.2.S.4.1).
2.  Comparative Peptide Mapping against the Initial Characterization Profile.
3.  Evaluation of Secondary Structure via Circular Dichroism (CD).

If the purity of a WRS drops by > 0.5% from its baseline, or if any new impurity exceeds 0.05%, the batch is immediately decommissioned, and the PRS is used to qualify a new WRS batch from the current production pipeline (e.g., GLUC-2025-XXX series).

---

2. *ICH Q1A(R2): Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.*
3. *FDA Guidance for Industry: Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (July 2015).*
