## Aliquoting and Reconstitution

### 3.2.S.5 Reference Standards or Materials
#### 3.2.S.5.2 Storage and Handling
##### 3.2.S.5.2.1 Aliquoting and Reconstitution Procedures for Glucogen-XR Reference Standards

---

### 1. SCOPE AND OBJECTIVE
This subsection delineates the validated protocols for the aliquoting and reconstitution of the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standard (WRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release), a GLP-1 receptor agonist produced by Google Health Sciences. Given the complex secondary structure and the extended-release pharmacokinetic profile of the glucapeptide moiety, strict adherence to these thermal and mechanical handling parameters is mandatory to ensure the maintenance of biological potency and structural integrity (e.g., prevention of deamidation and aggregation).

These procedures are governed by **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **USP <1226>** (Verification of Compendial Procedures).

---

### 2. MATERIAL SPECIFICATIONS AND BATCH IDENTIFIERS
The following reference materials are subject to the aliquoting and reconstitution protocols defined herein. All materials are derived from the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line.

**Table 1: Reference Material Inventory and Batch Tracking**
| Material Description | Batch Number | Purity (SEC-HPLC) | Specific Activity (IU/mg) | Initial Concentration |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary Ref Standard (PRS)** | GLUC-2025-001-PRS | 99.4% | 1.05 ± 0.02 | 10.0 mg/mL |
| **Working Ref Standard (WRS)** | GLUC-2025-002-WRS | 98.9% | 1.01 ± 0.03 | 5.0 mg/mL |
| **Calibration Standard (CS)** | GLUC-2025-009-CAL | 99.1% | N/A | 2.0 mg/mL |
| **System Suitability (SS)** | GLUC-2025-014-SYS | 98.2% | 0.98 ± 0.05 | 1.0 mg/mL |

---

### 3. ENVIRONMENTAL AND SAFETY CONTROLS
#### 3.3.1 Cleanroom Requirements
Aliquoting must be performed in a Grade A (ISO 5) Laminar Flow Hood (LFH) within a Grade B background environment.
*   **Equipment ID:** GHS-LFH-9928
*   **Temperature:** 20°C ± 2°C
*   **Relative Humidity:** 45% ± 5%
*   **Pressure Differential:** >15 Pa

#### 3.3.2 Protective Equipment (PPE)
*   Double nitrile gloves (powder-free)
*   Sterile Tyvek coveralls
*   PAPR (Powered Air Purifying Respirator) for bulk powder handling

---

### 4. ALIQUOTING PROTOCOL (LYOPHILIZED POWDER AND BULK DRUG SUBSTANCE)

The goal of the aliquoting process is to minimize freeze-thaw cycles. Google Health Sciences utilizes a "Single-Use Aliquot Strategy" (SUAS) to ensure that no vial of Reference Standard is re-entered more than once after initial reconstitution.

#### 4.1 Preparation of Aliquot Vials
1.  **Vial Selection:** Use 2.0 mL Type 1 Borosilicate clear glass vials (USP <660> compliant).
2.  **Stopper Selection:** FluroTec® coated chlorobutyl rubber stoppers to minimize leachables/extractables and prevent peptide adsorption.
3.  **Depyrogenation:** Vials are subjected to dry heat sterilization at 250°C for 120 minutes (Cycle ID: DH-2025-V1).

#### 4.2 Calculation of Fill Volume (Vf)
The fill volume is calculated to account for the "Dead Volume" (Vd) of the analytical pipettes and the concentration requirements for the specified assays (Bioassay vs. Physicochemical).

$$V_f = (C_{target} \times V_{assay}) / C_{stock} + V_{dead}$$

*Where:*
*   $C_{target}$ = Target concentration for assay (e.g., 1.0 mg/mL)
*   $V_{assay}$ = Required volume for triplicate injection (e.g., 250 µL)
*   $V_{dead}$ = 10 µL (pipette residual)

#### 4.3 Aliquoting Procedure (Step-by-Step)
1.  **Thawing of Bulk Drug Substance (BDS):** Remove Bulk Batch **GLUC-2025-001-PRS** from -80°C storage. Thaw in a controlled 2-8°C refrigerator for 14 hours. *Do not use water baths or accelerate thawing.*
2.  **Homogenization:** Gently invert the bulk container 10 times. Avoid vortexing, which induces shear stress and protein denaturation.
3.  **Dispensing:** Utilizing an automated micro-pipetting system (Hamilton Microlab STAR), dispense 250 µL into each of the 400 pre-labeled vials.
4.  **Capping:** Immediately apply stoppers and crimp with aluminum seals (Blue for PRS, Green for WRS).

---

### 5. RECONSTITUTION PROTOCOL (FOR LYOPHILIZED MATERIAL)

The reconstitution of Glucogen-XR is a critical step, as the extended-release polymer matrix requires specific hydration kinetics to achieve a monomeric state.

#### 5.1 Reconstitution Diluent (GHS-DIL-05)
The validated diluent for all Reference Standard reconstitution is:
*   10 mM Histidine, pH 6.5
*   5% (w/v) Sucrose
*   0.02% (w/v) Polysorbate 20
*   Water for Injection (WFI)

#### 5.2 Procedure for Reconstitution
1.  **Equilibration:** Allow the lyophilized vial (e.g., Batch **GLUC-2025-005-LYO**) to reach room temperature (approx. 20-25 mins).
2.  **Sanitization:** Wipe the septum with 70% IPA.
3.  **Addition of Diluent:** Using a 21G needle, slowly inject 1.0 mL of Reconstitution Diluent along the interior wall of the vial. **DO NOT INJECT DIRECTLY ONTO THE LYOPHILIZED CAKE.**
4.  **Wet-Down Phase:** Allow the vial to sit undisturbed for 5 minutes to permit complete wetting of the protein cake.
5.  **Dissolution:** Gently swirl the vial in a circular motion on the benchtop for 60 seconds. Inspect for "fisheyes" or undissolved particulates.
6.  **Final Inspection:** The resulting solution must be clear to slightly opalescent and free of visible particulates (USP <790>).

---

### 6. ANALYTICAL VERIFICATION OF ALIQUOTING/RECONSTITUTION
Each aliquoting session must be followed by a "Verification Pull" to confirm that the handling process did not degrade the peptide.

**Table 2: Acceptance Criteria for Post-Aliquoting Verification (Batch GLUC-2025-001-PRS)**
| Test Parameter | Method | Acceptance Criteria | Result (Validation Run 1) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual (USP <790>) | Clear, color-less | Conforms |
| **Concentration** | UV-Vis (A280) | 10.0 mg/mL ± 0.5 | 10.12 mg/mL |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SEC-HPLC | ≥ 98.5% | 99.2% |
| **HMW Species** | SEC-HPLC | ≤ 1.0% | 0.4% |
| **Biological Activity** | GLP-1 Receptor Activation | 80% - 125% of Target | 104% |

---

### 7. STORAGE CONDITIONS AND STABILITY
*   **Long-term Storage:** -80°C ± 10°C (Ultra-Low Temperature Freezer GHS-FRZ-44).
*   **Short-term Storage (In-use):** 2°C to 8°C for a maximum of 24 hours post-reconstitution.
*   **Stability Monitoring:** Aliquots are sampled every 6 months under the **GHS-RS-SMP-2025** stability program to monitor for the formation of high molecular weight (HMW) species.

---

### 8. REGULATORY COMPLIANCE REFERENCES
1.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (2015).*
2.  **USP Chapter <121>:** *Insulin Assays* (modified for GLP-1 analogues).
3.  **ICH Q1A (R2):** *Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.*
4.  **Google Health Internal SOP:** *GHS-SOP-550: Reference Standard Lifecycle Management.*

---

**End of Subsection**

## Stability Monitoring

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS

#### 3.2.S.5.3 Storage and Handling
##### 3.2.S.5.3.1 Stability Monitoring of Primary and Working Reference Standards

The stability monitoring program for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standard (WRS) is designed to ensure the continued integrity, potency, and purity of the reference materials throughout their lifecycle. This program adheres to the requirements outlined in **ICH Q1A(R2) Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products**, **ICH Q6B Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products**, and **USP <1226> Verification of Compendial Procedures**.

Given the sensitive nature of the glucapeptide moiety and the extended-release formulation characteristics, Google Health Sciences (GHS) employs a multi-tiered stability strategy.

---

### I. STABILITY PROTOCOL ARCHITECTURE

The stability monitoring for Glucogen-XR reference standards is divided into three distinct categories:
1.  **Long-Term Real-Time Stability (LTRTS):** Monitoring under the intended storage conditions (-80°C ± 5°C).
2.  **Accelerated and Stress Testing:** Evaluating the degradation pathways and molecular robustness at elevated temperatures (2-8°C and 25°C).
3.  **In-Use Stability:** Monitoring the stability of the reference standard after the initial vial puncture or reconstitution for assay use.

#### 1.1 Batch Identification and Material Allocation
The current stability monitoring program involves the following representative batches:

| Material Type | Batch Number | Date of Manufacture | Site of Manufacture | Initial Purity (SEC-HPLC) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Primary Ref Standard (PRS) | GLUC-2025-PRS-001 | 12-JAN-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr. SSF | 99.4% |
| Working Ref Standard (WRS) | GLUC-2025-WRS-001 | 15-FEB-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr. SSF | 99.2% |
| Working Ref Standard (WRS) | GLUC-2025-WRS-002 | 22-FEB-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr. SSF | 99.1% |

---

### II. TEST PARAMETERS AND ANALYTICAL METHODS

The stability of Glucogen-XR is assessed using an array of stability-indicating assays. The following table defines the testing matrix:

#### Table 1: Stability-Indicating Analytical Matrix
| Test Attribute | Methodology | Acceptance Criteria | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual Inspection (USP <790>) | Clear, colorless to slightly opalescent | Detection of macro-particles/color change. |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SEC-HPLC (Waters ACQUITY) | ≥ 98.0% Monomer | Detection of aggregation and fragmentation. |
| **Purity (Charge Isoforms)** | icIEF (ProteinSimple Maurice) | Main Peak: 65.0 - 75.0% | Detection of deamidation/sialylation. |
| **Potency (Biological)** | GLP-1 Receptor Transactivation | 80% - 125% of Initial | Assessment of biological efficacy. |
| **Mass Spectrometry** | LC-MS/MS (Intact Mass) | Consistent with theoretical (± 2 Da) | Verification of primary sequence integrity. |
| **Oxidation Status** | RP-HPLC (Post-digest) | Total Oxidation ≤ 2.0% | Sensitivity of Met residues in GLP-1. |
| **Sub-visible Particles** | MFI / Light Obscuration | USP <787> Compliant | Detection of pre-visible aggregates. |

---

### III. DETAILED STABILITY SCHEDULES

#### 3.1 Primary Reference Standard (PRS) - Protocol GLUC-STAB-PRS
The PRS is stored at ultra-low temperatures to minimize kinetic energy and chemical degradation.

**Storage Condition:** -80°C ± 10°C
**Sampling Frequency:**
*   Year 1: 0, 3, 6, 9, 12 months
*   Year 2-5: Every 6 months
*   Year 5+: Annually

#### Table 2: Real-Time Stability Data (Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-001)
*Storage: -80°C; Monitoring Period: Ongoing*

| Interval (Mo) | Date | Appearance | SEC-HPLC (% Monomer) | icIEF (% Main) | Potency (%) | Bioburden (CFU) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T0 | 12-JAN-25 | Pass | 99.42 | 71.2 | 102 | < 1 |
| T3 | 12-APR-25 | Pass | 99.40 | 71.1 | 100 | < 1 |
| T6 | 12-JUL-25 | Pass | 99.39 | 71.3 | 98 | < 1 |
| T9 | 12-OCT-25 | [Pending] | [Pending] | [Pending] | [Pending] | [Pending] |

---

### IV. STEP-BY-STEP STABILITY TESTING PROCEDURE (SOP-GHS-772)

To ensure consistency in stability monitoring, the following protocol is followed during each sampling interval:

1.  **Vial Retrieval:** 
    *   Retrieve five (5) vials of GLUC-2025-XXX from Freezer ID: FRZ-GHS-009 (-80°C).
    *   Immediately transfer to a validated transport cooler at -20°C.
    *   Allow vials to equilibrate to room temperature (18-25°C) for exactly 45 minutes on a static bench.

2.  **Visual Inspection:**
    *   Perform inspection against black and white backgrounds under a calibrated 3500-lux light source (Model: LUX-900).
    *   Document any visible particulates or turbidity.

3.  **Purity Analysis (SEC-HPLC):**
    *   **Column:** TSKgel G3000SWxl (7.8 mm ID x 30 cm).
    *   **Mobile Phase:** 0.2 M Potassium Phosphate, 0.25 M Potassium Chloride, pH 6.2.
    *   **Flow Rate:** 0.5 mL/min.
    *   **Calculation:** % Monomer = (Area of Monomer Peak / Total Area) * 100.

4.  **Charge Heterogeneity (icIEF):**
    *   Sample concentration: Dilute to 1.0 mg/mL using GHS-specific dilution buffer.
    *   Ampholytes: Pharmalyte 3-10.
    *   Focusing: 1 min @ 1500V, 8 min @ 3000V.

5.  **Statistical Analysis:**
    *   Perform a linear regression analysis of purity vs. time.
    *   Calculate the 95% Confidence Interval (CI) for the slope.
    *   If the lower 95% CI intersects the specification limit before the next testing point, initiate a **Quality Notification (QN)**.

---

### V. IN-USE STABILITY AND FREEZE-THAW CYCLES

Reference standards are frequently handled. GHS has validated the stability of Glucogen-XR across multiple freeze-thaw (F/T) cycles and post-thaw handling.

#### 5.1 Freeze-Thaw Study (Batch GLUC-2025-WRS-001)
Study design: Aliquots were subjected to rapid freezing in liquid nitrogen and thawing at room temperature.

| Cycle Number | SEC-HPLC (% Monomer) | icIEF (% Main) | Visible Particles |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Initial | 99.2 | 70.5 | None |
| Cycle 1 | 99.2 | 70.4 | None |
| Cycle 3 | 99.1 | 70.4 | None |
| Cycle 5 | 98.9 | 70.1 | None |
| **Cycle 10** | **98.5** | **69.2** | **Slight Opalescence** |

*Conclusion: Glucogen-XR reference standards are limited to a maximum of three (3) freeze-thaw cycles to ensure maintenance of the monomeric profile.*

---

### VI. MATHEMATICAL MODELING OF DEGRADATION KINETICS

To predict the shelf-life of the reference standard, GHS utilizes the Arrhenius Equation for accelerated data:

$$k = A e^{-E_a / RT}$$

Where:
*   $k$ = Rate constant for degradation (measured via SEC-HPLC)
*   $A$ = Pre-exponential factor
*   $E_a$ = Activation energy (calculated as 85 kJ/mol for Glucapeptide)
*   $R$ = Gas constant (8.314 J/mol·K)
*   $T$ = Absolute temperature (K)

Based on data from the -20°C and 5°C stress studies, the predicted degradation rate at -80°C is effectively negligible ($<0.01\%$ loss of purity per year), justifying a preliminary 60-month retest period for the PRS.

---

### VII. REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND DOCUMENTATION

#### 7.1 Deviations and Out of Specification (OOS)
Any stability result failing to meet the predefined acceptance criteria (Table 1) must be investigated according to **SOP-QA-005 (Management of OOS Results)**. 
*   If a Primary Reference Standard fails, all assays utilizing that standard since the last successful stability check must be assessed for impact.
*   The "Bridging Study" (see Section 3.2.S.5.2) will be accelerated to qualify a replacement batch.

#### 7.2 Equipment Calibration
Stability monitoring is performed using equipment under the GHS Master Calibration Schedule:
*   **HPLC Units:** Calibrated bi-annually (Next: June 2025).
*   **Stability Chambers:** Continuously monitored via the Google Cloud IoT Environmental Monitoring System (G-IEMS), providing real-time alerts for excursions > 2°C for more than 15 minutes.

---

### VIII. SUMMARY OF CURRENT STATUS

As of the current filing, the Primary Reference Standard **GLUC-2025-PRS-001** shows no significant trends toward degradation. The material remains stable and fit for its intended use in quantifying the potency and purity of Glucogen-XR drug substance and drug product lots.

*Reference: Google Health Sciences Internal Report GHS-STAB-2025-04-R.*

# Requalification and Retest

## Retest Schedule

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
#### 3.2.S.5.3 Requalification and Retest Schedule

---

**Proprietary Name:** Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)  
**Non-proprietary Name:** Glucapeptide-GHS  
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences  
**Manufacturing Site:** 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080, USA  
**Document Type:** Module 3 - Quality (Quality Overall Summary / Drug Substance)  

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.1 Introduction to the Retest Strategy

The Retest Schedule for Glucogen-XR Primary and Working Reference Standards (PRS and WRS) is designed in accordance with **ICH Q1A(R2) Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products**, **ICH Q6B Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products**, and **USP <1226> Verification of Compendial Procedures**. 

Given the structural complexity of the Glucogen-XR peptide—a 42-amino acid synthetic-biologic hybrid with an extended-release fatty acid side chain—the stability of the reference material is paramount to maintaining the integrity of the entire lifecycle of the product. The retest schedule ensures that the assigned potency, purity profile, and physicochemical identity of the reference standard are maintained throughout its lifecycle.

#### 3.2.S.5.3.2 Master Retest Frequency Matrix

The following table outlines the mandated retest intervals for the current active batches of Glucogen-XR reference materials stored under long-term conditions (-70°C ± 10°C).

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-1: Reference Standard Retest Schedule and Inventory Status**

| Standard ID | Batch Number | Initial Qual. Date | Current Status | Next Scheduled Retest | Frequency |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary (PRS)** | GLUC-2025-PRS-01 | 14-JAN-2025 | Active | 14-JAN-2027 | Bi-Annual |
| **Working (WRS)** | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | 02-FEB-2025 | Active | 02-AUG-2025 | Semi-Annual |
| **Working (WRS)** | GLUC-2025-WRS-02 | 15-MAR-2025 | Validation | 15-SEP-2025 | Semi-Annual |
| **In-House RS** | GLUC-2025-IHS-01 | 20-JAN-2025 | Active | 20-JUL-2025 | Quarterly (Initial) |

*Note: Frequency for WRS is more rigorous than PRS to account for more frequent vial breach and potential moisture ingress during laboratory handling.*

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.3 Protocol for Requalification (SOP-GHS-QC-0982)

The requalification of Glucogen-XR Reference Standards follows a tiered analytical approach. Each retest event must verify that the material remains "Fit for Purpose" compared to the initial characterization data (Baseline T0).

##### 3.2.S.5.3.3.1 Tier 1: Physicochemical Integrity
1.  **Visual Appearance:** Inspection for color change, lyophilized cake collapse, or particulate formation.
2.  **Reconstitution Time:** Measurement of the time required for the solid mass to dissolve in 1.0 mL of USP Sterile Water for Injection (SWFI). Must be ≤ 60 seconds.
3.  **Water Content (Karl Fischer):** Determination of residual moisture. Limit: ≤ 2.0% w/w. (Reference: USP <921> Method 1c).

##### 3.2.S.5.3.3.2 Tier 2: Purity and Degradation Profile
1.  **RP-HPLC (Reverse Phase):** Assessment of main peak purity and detection of hydrophobic impurities (e.g., deamidation at Asn-28).
2.  **SEC-HPLC (Size Exclusion):** Assessment of high molecular weight species (HMWS) and aggregates. Limit: ≥ 99.0% monomer.
3.  **CEX-HPLC (Cation Exchange):** Monitoring of charge variants (acidic and basic species).

##### 3.2.S.5.3.3.3 Tier 3: Biological Potency
1.  **GLP-1 Receptor Activation Assay (Cell-Based):** Measurement of cAMP accumulation in HEK293 cells transfected with the human GLP-1 receptor.
2.  **Acceptance Criteria:** The relative potency must be within 80%–125% of the T0 value, with a 95% confidence interval overlapping 100%.

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.4 Statistical Evaluation of Retest Data

Google Health Sciences utilizes a "Stability Trend Analysis Tool" (STAT-GHS-v4.1) to evaluate the drift in reference standard performance.

**Calculations for Potency Drift:**
The slope of the potency vs. time plot is calculated using linear regression:
$$Y = \beta_0 + \beta_1 X + \epsilon$$
Where:
*   $Y$ = Measured Potency
*   $X$ = Time in months
*   $\beta_1$ = Degradation rate

If the 95% Lower Confidence Bound (LCB) of the regression line at the next scheduled retest interval falls below 90% of the initial value, the retest interval is shortened by 50% (e.g., from 6 months to 3 months).

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.5 Comprehensive Retest Data Table: Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01

The following table provides the longitudinal data for the primary reference standard, illustrating the historical stability and the justification for the biennial retest schedule.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-2: Longitudinal Stability Data for Primary Reference Standard (GLUC-2025-PRS-01)**

| Test Parameter | Method ID | T=0 (Baseline) | T=6 Months (Retest) | T=12 Months (Retest) | Spec Limit |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual | White Powder | White Powder | White Powder | White Solid |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | MET-GHS-001 | 99.4% | 99.3% | 99.2% | ≥ 98.0% |
| **HMWS (SEC)** | MET-GHS-002 | 0.2% | 0.2% | 0.3% | ≤ 0.5% |
| **Potency (Cell)** | MET-GHS-010 | 102% | 101% | 100% | 80-125% |
| **Moisture (KF)** | USP <921> | 0.8% | 0.9% | 0.8% | ≤ 2.0% |
| **Mass Spec (MW)** | ESI-MS | 5421.2 Da | 5421.3 Da | 5421.1 Da | ± 1.0 Da |

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.6 Protocol for Reference Standard Extension (SOP-GHS-QA-202)

In the event that a Reference Standard batch approaches its retest date without a replacement batch being available, the following "Extension Protocol" is activated:

1.  **Pre-requisite:** The previous three (3) retest points must show a linear degradation slope of < 0.1% per month.
2.  **Sampling:** Double the standard sampling size ($n=6$ vials) is pulled from the -70°C cryo-storage.
3.  **Testing:** All tests in Table 3.2.S.5.3-2 are performed in triplicate by two independent analysts.
4.  **Reporting:** A "Retest Summary Report" (RSR) is generated. If all results pass, the "Expiring" date is extended by 6 months for WRS or 12 months for PRS.
5.  **Regulatory Notification:** Any failure to meet specifications during retest results in the immediate "Quarantine" of the batch and notification to the FDA via a CBE-30 (Changes Being Effected) supplement if the standard is used for commercial release testing.

#### 3.2.S.5.3.7 Storage and Handling Requirements During Retest

To ensure that the retest results represent the true state of the bulk standard and not artifacts of handling, the following environmental controls are enforced:
*   **Storage:** Ultra-Low Temperature Freezer (Equipment ID: GHS-ULT-09). Validated range -80°C to -60°C.
*   **Alarms:** 24/7 continuous monitoring via Google Cloud Life Sciences "Sentinel" system.
*   **Excursions:** Any excursion > -55°C for more than 30 minutes triggers an immediate unscheduled retest of the affected RS batch.

---

**References:**
1. *ICH Q1A(R2) Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.*
2. *ICH Q6B Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.*
3. *USP General Chapter <11> Reference Standards.*
4. *GHS Internal Quality Standard: GHS-QS-2025-01: Lifecycle Management of Glucapeptides.*

---

## Requalification Criteria

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
#### 3.2.S.5.3 Requalification and Retest Procedures
##### 3.2.S.5.3.1 Requalification Criteria for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide)

---

**CONFIDENTIAL – PROPRIETARY INFORMATION**  
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, a Division of Google Cloud Life Sciences  
**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-REG-M3-DS-RS-004  
**Effective Date:** 24-Oct-2025  
**Supersedes:** GHS-GLUC-REG-M3-DS-RS-003  

---

### 1.0 PURPOSE AND SCOPE

This subsection defines the comprehensive requalification criteria, statistical assessment models, and rigorous analytical protocols required to maintain the integrity of the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standard (WRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). 

Glucogen-XR is a complex recombinant glucapeptide (GLP-1 receptor agonist) produced via the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line. Due to the inherent sensitivity of the peptide’s tertiary structure and the extended-release formulation components, the Reference Standard Program (RSP) at Google Health Sciences utilizes a multi-tiered requalification strategy. This ensures that any drift in potency, purity, or molecular heterogeneity is identified before it can impact the release or stability testing of clinical and commercial batches (e.g., GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-500).

### 2.0 REGULATORY ALIGNMENT

The requalification criteria outlined herein are designed to comply with the following international regulatory frameworks:
1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **ICH Q2(R2):** Validation of Analytical Procedures.
3.  **USP <111>:** Design and Analysis of Biological Assays.
4.  **USP <1048>:** Quality of Biological Products: Reference Standards.
5.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (July 2015).

### 3.0 REQUALIFICATION SCHEDULE AND FREQUENCY

The requalification interval is determined by the stability profile of the glucapeptide molecule. Initial requalification (Protocol P-RS-GLUC-01) is performed annually for the first three years, transitioning to a biennial (every 24 months) schedule thereafter, provided no significant trends are observed.

| Standard Type | Initial Qualification | Requalification Frequency | Storage Condition |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary (PRS)** | Batch GLUC-2025-P01 | Every 24 Months | -80°C ± 5°C |
| **Working (WRS)** | Batch GLUC-2025-W01 | Every 12 Months | -80°C ± 5°C |
| **In-Use Standard** | N/A | Every 3 Months | 2°C to 8°C |

### 4.0 CRITICAL QUALITY ATTRIBUTES (CQA) FOR REQUALIFICATION

The requalification of Glucogen-XR is not a mere "pass/fail" exercise but a comparative analysis against the historical baseline established during the initial characterization.

#### 4.1 Physical State and Appearance
The Glucogen-XR reference standard is a lyophilized white to off-white cake. Requalification must confirm the absence of collapse, melt-back, or discoloration (browning due to Maillard reaction between peptide amines and residual sugars).

#### 4.2 Structural Integrity and Purity (RP-HPLC / SE-HPLC)
The primary degradation pathways for Glucogen-XR include deamidation at the Asn-28 residue and oxidation of the Met-14 residue.
*   **RP-HPLC (Reverse Phase):** Used to quantify deamidated and oxidized forms.
*   **SE-HPLC (Size Exclusion):** Used to quantify high molecular weight species (HMWS) and aggregates.

#### 4.3 Biological Potency (Cell-Based Bioassay)
Potency is evaluated using a proprietary GLP-1 receptor-coupled cAMP activation assay. The requalification criterion requires the relative potency to be within 80%–125% of the initial value, with a 95% confidence interval (CI) that falls within 70%–135%.

---

### 5.0 DETAILED ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA TABLE

The following table outlines the specific numerical limits for the requalification of Batch **GLUC-2025-RS-02** (Current Working Standard).

| Test Parameter | Analytical Method | Acceptance Criteria | Alert Limit (OOT) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual Inspection | White lyophilized cake | Any slight yellowing |
| **Identity (MW)** | ESI-TOF MS | 4,285.6 ± 0.5 Da | N/A |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | SOP-GHS-AN-102 | ≥ 98.0% | < 98.5% |
| **Single Impurity** | RP-HPLC | ≤ 0.5% | > 0.3% |
| **HMWS (SE-HPLC)** | SOP-GHS-AN-105 | ≤ 1.0% | > 0.5% |
| **Potency (Relative)** | cAMP Bioassay | 80% - 125% | < 90% or > 110% |
| **Water Content** | Karl Fischer | ≤ 2.0% w/w | > 1.5% w/w |
| **pH (Reconstituted)** | USP <791> | 7.4 ± 0.2 | ± 0.1 from Baseline |

---

### 6.0 STATISTICAL ANALYSIS AND DRIFT ASSESSMENT

Google Health Sciences employs a **Equivalence Testing Approach** (Two One-Sided Tests, TOST) to determine if the "Aged" Reference Standard is equivalent to the "Baseline" data.

#### 6.1 Formula for Potency Drift Calculation
The drift ($D$) is calculated as follows:
$$D = \frac{\mu_{new} - \mu_{old}}{\mu_{old}} \times 100$$
Where:
*   $\mu_{new}$ = Mean potency of the current requalification session.
*   $\mu_{old}$ = Mean potency from the initial characterization.

**Requalification Requirement:** $|D| \leq 5\%$. If the drift exceeds 5%, a full investigation (OOS/OOT) is triggered to determine if the standard has degraded or if assay shift is responsible.

#### 6.2 Control Charting
All data points from batches (e.g., GLUC-2025-002, GLUC-2025-005) are plotted on Shewhart Control Charts. A "Warning" is issued if three consecutive requalification points show a downward trend in purity, even if they remain within the absolute specification.

---

### 7.0 PROTOCOL P-RS-GLUC-05: STEP-BY-STEP REQUALIFICATION PROCEDURE

**Step 1: Inventory Retrieval**
*   Retrieve 15 vials of Batch GLUC-2025-XXX from the -80°C cryo-storage unit (Equipment ID: GHS-FRZ-09).
*   Equilibrate to room temperature (15-25°C) for exactly 45 minutes in a desiccator.

**Step 2: Reconstitution Protocol**
*   Using a calibrated pipette (GHS-PIP-442), add 1.1 mL of Sterile Water for Injection (SWFI).
*   Gently swirl for 30 seconds; **do not vortex.**
*   Allow to stand for 5 minutes to ensure complete solubilization of the glucapeptide.

**Step 3: Multi-Detector SEC Analysis**
*   Load samples onto the Agilent 1260 Infinity II HPLC.
*   Column: TSKgel G2000SWxl, 7.8 mm x 30 cm.
*   Mobile Phase: 0.1M Sodium Phosphate, 0.1M Sodium Sulfate, pH 6.8.
*   Flow Rate: 0.5 mL/min.
*   *Requirement:* Peak symmetry (As) must be between 0.8 and 1.2.

**Step 4: Peptide Mapping (Identity Confirmation)**
*   Digest 100 µg of Glucogen-XR with Trypsin (Sequencing Grade).
*   Analyze via LC-MS/MS (Orbitrap Exploris 480).
*   Compare the "Fingerprint" against the Theoretical Sequence: `HGEGTFTSDVSSYLEGQAAKEFIAWLVKGRG`.
*   *Acceptance:* 100% sequence coverage required.

---

### 8.0 HANDLING OF OUT-OF-SPECIFICATION (OOS) RESULTS

If a reference standard batch (e.g., GLUC-2025-W02) fails to meet the requalification criteria:
1.  **Quarantine:** The batch is immediately moved to "HOLD" status in the LIMS system.
2.  **Investigation:** A Phase I investigation is initiated to rule out laboratory error.
3.  **Cross-Validation:** The failing WRS is compared against the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) GLUC-2025-P01.
4.  **Replacement:** If degradation is confirmed, the WRS is decommissioned, and a new WRS is qualified from a recent GMP batch (e.g., GLUC-2025-110) that has undergone extensive stability testing.

### 9.0 DOCUMENTATION AND STORAGE

All raw data, chromatograms, and statistical outputs are archived in the Google Cloud Life Sciences GxP-compliant repository. Requalification reports are signed by the Head of Quality Control and the Regulatory Affairs Lead.

**Reference:**  
*GHS-SOP-QC-992: Management of Reference Standards for Biological Products.*  
*GHS-STRAT-2025-01: Lifecycle Management of Glucogen-XR.*

---

## Change Management

### 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS

#### 3.2.S.5.3 Requalification and Retest Protocols

##### 3.2.S.5.3.4 Change Management and Lifecycle Maintenance for Glucogen-XR Reference Standards

The establishment and maintenance of the Reference Standard (RS) lifecycle for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) are governed by the Google Health Sciences (GHS) Quality Management System (QMS), specifically adhering to **SOP-GHS-QA-0098: Lifecycle Management of Biological Reference Materials**. This section delineates the rigorous change management protocols required to ensure the continued suitability, potency, and integrity of the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standards (WRS) throughout the product lifecycle.

All changes involving the manufacture, characterization, storage, or qualification of Glucogen-XR reference standards are classified according to their potential impact on product quality and regulatory filings, in alignment with **ICH Q5C (Stability Testing of Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)**.

---

### I. Categorization of Changes in Reference Standard Management

Change management activities for Glucogen-XR RS are categorized into three distinct tiers based on the risk to the analytical consistency of the Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus clinical program and commercial supply.

#### 1.1 Level 1: Minor Changes (Annual Reportable / Notification)
These changes have minimal potential to affect the identified quality attributes of the RS.
*   Update to internal labeling formats (non-content related).
*   Transfer of RS vials between qualified $-80^{\circ}C$ freezers within the same facility (3000 Innovation Drive).
*   Minor updates to the administrative sections of the Requalification Protocol.

#### 1.2 Level 2: Moderate Changes (CBE-30 / PAS Depending on Impact)
These changes may affect the performance of the RS in specific assays.
*   Implementation of a new analytical technology for secondary characterization (e.g., transitioning from HPLC-UV to UPLC-MS for impurity profiling).
*   Extension of the retest period based on real-time stability data exceeding the initial 24-month window.
*   Change in the secondary packaging components (e.g., vial seals or moisture-resistant secondary overwraps).

#### 1.3 Level 3: Major Changes (Prior Approval Supplement - PAS)
These changes significantly impact the continuity of the reference base.
*   Introduction of a new Primary Reference Standard (PRS) derived from a new Master Cell Bank (MCB) or significantly altered manufacturing process.
*   Change in the physical state of the RS (e.g., transition from frozen liquid to lyophilized powder).
*   Recalibration of the Potency (IU/mg) against an international standard (if available) or a previous primary lot.

---

### II. Protocol for Transitioning to a New Working Reference Standard (WRS)

When a current WRS (e.g., **Batch GLUC-2025-WRS-01**) nears depletion or its retest date, a transition protocol is initiated to qualify a replacement batch (e.g., **Batch GLUC-2025-WRS-02**). This process ensures "Bridging" to maintain analytical continuity.

#### 2.1 The Two-Tiered Bridging Strategy
The transition involves a side-by-side comparison between the "Candidate RS" and the "Current RS." The objective is to demonstrate that the Candidate RS is representative of the product and provides consistent results in the release and stability assays for Glucogen-XR.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3.4-1: Statistical Comparison Matrix for WRS Bridging**

| Parameter | Analytical Method | Acceptance Criteria for Bridge | Statistical Tool |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual (USP <790>) | Match Current RS | N/A |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SEC-UPLC | Difference in Mean $\le 0.5\%$ | Two-sample t-test ($p > 0.05$) |
| **Purity (Main Peak)** | RP-UPLC | $98.0\% - 102.0\%$ of Current | Equivalence Testing (TOST) |
| **Potency (In Vitro)** | Cell-based Bioassay | $90\% - 110\%$ Relative Potency | Parallel Line Analysis (PLA) |
| **Charge Profile** | cIEF | Consistent Electropherogram | Peak Overlay Comparison |
| **Glycan Mapping** | HILIC-FLD/MS | $\pm 10\%$ Relative Area for Major Species | Descriptive Statistics |

#### 2.2 Step-by-Step Replacement Procedure (SOP-GHS-AN-0442)

1.  **Selection of Batch:** Identify a drug substance batch manufactured under GMP (e.g., **GLUC-2025-DS-012**) with high purity and representative glycosylation profiles.
2.  **Aliquotting:** Perform aseptic filling into 2.0 mL Type 1 Borosilicate glass vials at a concentration of $10.0 mg/mL \pm 0.5 mg/mL$.
3.  **Initial Characterization:** Conduct full ICH Q6B characterization (Mass Spec, CD, Fluorescence, Peptide Mapping).
4.  **Side-by-Side Analysis:** Execute 5 independent runs of the analytical suite using both the New and Old WRS.
5.  **Data Evaluation:** The Statistical Analysis Group (Google Life Sciences - Data Division) performs a $95\%$ Confidence Interval (CI) analysis.
6.  **Approval:** Quality Assurance (QA) signs the **Reference Standard Qualification Report**.
7.  **Implementation:** The New WRS is entered into the LIMS (Laboratory Information Management System) with a status of "Active."

---

### III. Deviation Management and Out-of-Specification (OOS) Results

If a Reference Standard fails a requalification parameter (e.g., a drop in purity during the 36-month stability check), the following **Change Management Emergency Protocol** is triggered.

#### 3.1 Impact Assessment Workflow
1.  **Immediate Quarantine:** All vials of the affected batch (e.g., **GLUC-2025-WRS-03**) are electronically locked in LIMS.
2.  **Root Cause Investigation (RCI):** 
    *   Review of freezer temperature logs (Equipment ID: **GHS-FRZ-80-004**).
    *   Investigation of vial integrity (CCIT - Container Closure Integrity Testing).
    *   Assessment of assay variability (System Suitability Check).
3.  **Trend Analysis:** Compare the OOS result against the **Reference Standard Stability Profile (RSSP)**.
4.  **Product Impact:** Evaluate all Drug Substance and Drug Product batches released using the failing RS during the period between the last successful requalification and the OOS event.

#### 3.2 Corrective and Preventive Actions (CAPA)
*   If degradation is confirmed: The RS is decommissioned. A new RS is qualified from the PRS.
*   If the degradation is "Analytical Artifact": The method is re-validated or optimized before re-testing the RS.

---

### IV. Inventory and Traceability Log

Google Health Sciences maintains a "Chain of Custody" for all Glucogen-XR Reference Standards. This log is audited annually by the Regulatory Affairs department.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3.4-2: Glucogen-XR Reference Standard Inventory and Lifecycle Log (Exemplary Data)**

| RS Batch ID | Type | Parent Lot | Qualification Date | Retest Date | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2024-PRS-01** | Primary | Clinical Lot A | 12-JAN-2024 | 12-JAN-2029 | Active |
| **GLUC-2025-WRS-01** | Working | GLUC-2024-DS-05 | 05-FEB-2025 | 05-FEB-2027 | Active |
| **GLUC-2025-WRS-02** | Working | GLUC-2025-DS-02 | 15-AUG-2025 | 15-AUG-2027 | In-Qualification |
| **GLUC-2023-WRS-01** | Working | GLUC-2023-DS-01 | 10-MAR-2023 | 10-MAR-2025 | Retired (Depleted) |

---

### V. Statistical Calculation for Standard Potency Assignment

The potency of a new Working Reference Standard ($P_{WRS}$) is assigned based on the weighted mean of multiple determinations against the Primary Reference Standard ($P_{PRS}$).

$$P_{WRS} = \frac{\sum_{i=1}^{n} (w_i \cdot x_i)}{\sum_{i=1}^{n} w_i}$$

Where:
*   $x_i$ = Potency result of the $i^{th}$ run.
*   $w_i$ = Weighting factor (inverse of the variance of the assay run).
*   $n$ = Minimum of 6 independent assays performed by two different analysts over three days.

The calculated potency must fall within the **95% Confidence Interval** of the target value (e.g., $100\% \pm 2\%$ relative to PRS) for the change to be approved by the GHS Change Control Board (CCB).

---

### VI. Regulatory References and Guidance Compliance

The Change Management protocol for Glucogen-XR is designed to comply with the following:
1.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Characterization and Physicochemical Self-Similarity of Therapeutic Proteins.*
2.  **USP <1130>:** *Bioassay Strategy and Design.*
3.  **USP <1226>:** *Verification of Compendial Procedures.*
4.  **ICH Q11:** *Development and Manufacture of Drug Substances.*

---

# Compendial Reference Standards

## Use of USP or EP Standards if Available

### **MODULE 3: QUALITY**
**Section 3.2.S.5: Reference Standards or Materials**
**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-XR-M32S5-RS-004
**Subsection:** Use of USP or EP Standards if Available

---

#### **1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE**
The qualification and utilization of compendial reference standards for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** are governed by the overarching philosophy of regulatory compliance with the United States Pharmacopeia (USP), European Pharmacopoeia (Ph. Eur. / EP), and Japanese Pharmacopoeia (JP), as outlined in ICH Q6B (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*).

Google Health Sciences (GHS) utilizes USP and EP primary reference standards (RS) whenever they are available and applicable to the characterization, identification, and potency testing of the Glucogen-XR drug substance (DS). Given that Glucogen-XR is a novel long-acting glucapeptide (GLP-1 receptor agonist) produced via a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout cell line, specific USP monographs for the final "Glucogen-XR" molecule do not yet exist. However, GHS leverages established compendial standards for amino acid analysis, carbohydrate profiling, excipient verification, and system suitability for the complex analytical instrumentation used in the release of GLUC-2025-XXX batches.

#### **2.0 HIERARCHY OF REFERENCE MATERIALS**
The GHS analytical framework for Glucogen-XR follows a strict hierarchical structure to ensure metrological traceability:

1.  **Primary Compendial Standards (USP/EP):** Used for absolute quantification of relevant components, calibration of specialized detectors (e.g., CAD, ELSD, MALS), and as system suitability markers.
2.  **Primary GHS Reference Standard:** Characterized against the International Standard (if available) or by extensive orthogonal physicochemical characterization.
3.  **Secondary (Working) Reference Standard:** Calibrated against the Primary GHS Reference Standard for routine batch release of GLUC-2025-XXX series.

#### **3.0 COMPENDIAL STANDARDS UTILIZED IN ANALYSIS**
The following USP and EP standards are integrated into the Glucogen-XR testing monographs. These standards are procured through authorized distributors and stored according to the manufacturer's Certificate of Analysis (CoA).

##### **Table 3.1: Inventory of Compendial Standards for Glucogen-XR Analysis**

| Compendial Standard Name | Catalog Number | Source | Purpose | Associated Method ID |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **USP Glucagon** | 1292008 | USP | System Suitability / Peptide Mapping | GHS-MET-GLUC-08 |
| **USP Endotoxin RS** | 1235503 | USP | Bacterial Endotoxin Testing (LAL) | GHS-MET-GLUC-14 |
| **EP Insulin Human** | I0300000 | EP | Calibration of SEC-MALS (MW Marker) | GHS-MET-GLUC-22 |
| **USP Amino Acid Mix** | 1013404 | USP | Quantitative Amino Acid Analysis | GHS-MET-GLUC-05 |
| **USP Sodium Chloride** | 1614008 | USP | Buffer Preparation / Osmolality | GHS-MET-GLUC-31 |
| **EP Dextrose (Anhydrous)**| 20500 | EP | Glycation verification | GHS-MET-GLUC-09 |

---

#### **4.0 PROCUREMENT AND RECEIPT PROCEDURES (SOP-QC-RS-01)**
Google Health Sciences maintains a rigorous chain of custody for all USP/EP standards to ensure the integrity of the Glucogen-XR data package.

##### **4.1 Receipt and Verification Protocol**
Upon receipt of a compendial standard (e.g., USP Endotoxin RS, Lot #H0K321), the Quality Control (QC) analyst must perform the following:
1.  **Visual Inspection:** Verify the integrity of the tamper-evident seal.
2.  **Documentation Review:** Confirm the Lot Number matches the current "Official" status per the USP Daily Update or EP Knowledge Database.
3.  **Storage Assignment:** Immediately transfer to the specified storage condition (e.g., -20°C ± 5°C for peptide-based standards).
4.  **LIMS Entry:** Log the material into the Google Life Sciences LIMS with a unique internal tracking ID (GHS-RS-XXXX).

##### **4.2 "Official Status" Monitoring Protocol**
The GHS Regulatory Compliance Team performs a monthly audit of the USP-NF and Ph. Eur. supplements.
*   **Action:** If a USP standard is replaced by a new lot, the previous lot is marked "Expired" in the LIMS.
*   **Grace Period:** Per USP General Chapter <11>, a 3-month grace period is observed unless the USP specifically mandates immediate discontinuation for safety or potency reasons.

---

#### **5.0 STEP-BY-STEP ANALYTICAL USE CASES**

##### **5.1 Case Study 1: Use of USP Glucagon for Peptide Map System Suitability**
While Glucogen-XR is a modified peptide, USP Glucagon (Cat #1292008) is utilized as a system suitability control for the Tryptic Mapping procedure (GHS-MET-GLUC-08) to ensure the LC-MS/MS sensitivity is optimized.

**Procedure:**
1.  **Preparation:** Reconstitute USP Glucagon to 1.0 mg/mL in 0.1% TFA.
2.  **Digestion:** Subject the USP standard to the same Trypsin-Gold digestion protocol (4 hours at 37°C) as the Glucogen-XR Batch (e.g., GLUC-2025-001).
3.  **Analysis:** Inject 10 µL onto the UHPLC-QTOF system.
4.  **Acceptance Criteria:**
    *   Recovery of the T1 fragment (HSQGTFTSDYSK) must be ≥ 92%.
    *   Mass accuracy must be ≤ 5 ppm.
    *   Chromatographic resolution between T2 and T3 fragments must be ≥ 1.8.

##### **5.2 Case Study 2: USP Endotoxin RS for LAL Kinetic Chromogenic Assay**
The safety of Glucogen-XR is verified using the USP Bacterial Endotoxins Test <85>.

**Calculations for Maximum Valid Dilution (MVD):**
The MVD for Glucogen-XR is calculated to ensure the compendial standard can detect the endotoxin limit.
$$MVD = \frac{Endotoxin Limit \times Concentration of Sample}{\lambda}$$
*   **Endotoxin Limit (L):** 5.0 EU/mg (for subcutaneous biologics).
*   **Concentration (C):** 10 mg/mL (Bulk Drug Substance).
*   **Sensitivity ($\lambda$):** 0.005 EU/mL (Kinetic sensitivity).
*   **Calculation:** $MVD = \frac{5.0 \times 10}{0.005} = 10,000$.
*   **Operational Setting:** GHS performs testing at a 1:1,000 dilution to ensure it remains well within the MVD while neutralizing potential inhibitory effects of the Glucogen-XR peptide.

---

#### **6.0 DATA COMPARISON: BATCH RELEASE VS. COMPENDIAL BENCHMARKS**
The following table summarizes the performance of recent Glucogen-XR clinical batches (GLUC-2025-001 through GLUC-2025-005) when analyzed using USP-compliant methodologies.

##### **Table 6.1: Compendial Integration Results for GLUC-2025 Series**

| Batch Number | USP Standard Reference | Parameter | Expected Result (Compendial) | Observed Result | Pass/Fail |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | USP 1013404 | Amino Acid Composition | ± 10% Theoretical | Met (98.2%) | Pass |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | USP 1235503 | Endotoxin Recovery | 50% - 200% Spike | 104% | Pass |
| **GLUC-2025-003** | EP I0300000 | SEC Retention Time | ± 2% vs. Standard | 0.4% Dev. | Pass |
| **GLUC-2025-004** | USP 1292008 | Peptide Map Identity | Consistent Fingerprint | Consistent | Pass |
| **GLUC-2025-005** | USP 1614008 | Chloride Content | 95% - 105% Target | 99.8% | Pass |

---

#### **7.0 JUSTIFICATION FOR NON-COMPENDIAL PRIMARY STANDARDS**
While USP/EP standards are used for ancillary components, GHS provides the following justification for the use of an In-House Primary Reference Standard (GHS-RS-GLUC-01) for the quantification of Glucogen-XR:

1.  **Unique Sequence:** Glucogen-XR contains a non-natural amino acid at position 8 (Aib) and a C16 fatty acid side chain attached via a glutamic acid spacer at Lys26. No USP monograph exists for this specific modification.
2.  **Extended Release Matrix:** The drug substance is formulated in a proprietary PEG-based hydrogel precursor. Compendial standards do not account for the interaction between the peptide and the extended-release polymer during SEC or RP-HPLC analysis.
3.  **Higher Purity Thresholds:** The GHS-RS-GLUC-01 is purified to >99.5% by preparative HPLC, exceeding the typical 97-98% purity found in general "Glucagon-like" USP standards, which is necessary for accurate potency determination in Type 2 Diabetes indications.

#### **8.0 STATISTICAL ANALYSIS OF REFERENCE STANDARD STABILITY**
To ensure the compendial standards remain valid throughout the testing cycle of GLUC-2025-XXX, GHS employs a Linear Regression analysis of the potency vs. time for the internal "Working Standard" as it relates to the USP primary benchmark.

**The Stability Equation:**
$$y = \beta_0 + \beta_1(t) + \epsilon$$
*   Where $y$ is the Relative Potency (%).
*   $\beta_0$ is the intercept (initial potency).
*   $\beta_1$ is the degradation rate.
*   $t$ is time in months.

**Statistical Significance:**
A p-value < 0.05 for $\beta_1$ would indicate a significant degradation trend, triggering an immediate re-qualification against a fresh USP/EP lot. As of the current filing, the degradation rate $\beta_1$ for GLUC-2025-001 is -0.002% per month (p = 0.45), indicating superior stability.

---

2.  **USP General Chapter <121>:** *Insulin Assays* (Applied by analogy for GLP-1).
3.  **Ph. Eur. Chapter 5.12:** *Reference Standards.*
4.  **ICH Q6B:** *Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.*
5.  **21 CFR 211.160:** *General Requirements for Laboratory Controls.*

#### **10.0 CONCLUSION**
Google Health Sciences ensures that every batch of **Glucogen-XR (GLUC-2025-XXX)** is anchored to internationally recognized compendial benchmarks. Where direct USP or EP standards for the molecule are unavailable, GHS utilizes compendial standards for amino acid analysis, purity components, and system suitability to maintain a state of high-quality control that meets or exceeds FDA and EMA expectations for peptide-based biologics.

## Suitability for Intended Use

### **3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **3.2.S.5.1 Compendial Reference Standards**
##### **3.2.S.5.1.1 Suitability for Intended Use**

---

### **1.0 Introduction and Scope**

The suitability for intended use of Compendial Reference Standards (CRS) employed in the analytical testing of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) Drug Substance (DS) is established through a rigorous verification framework. Google Health Sciences (GHS) adheres to the requirements set forth in **USP General Chapter <11> USP Reference Standards**, **ICH Q6B**, and **FDA Guidance for Industry: Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation**.

While CRS materials obtained from the United States Pharmacopeia (USP), European Pharmacopoeia (Ph. Eur.), or Japanese Pharmacopoeia (JP) are considered "primary" standards by regulatory definition, GHS performs an internal suitability assessment to ensure that the specific compendial lot is compatible with the extended-release glucapeptide matrix and the specialized analytical technologies employed at the South San Francisco (3000 Innovation Drive) facility.

### **2.0 Regulatory Framework and Compliance Matrix**

The suitability assessment is governed by the following regulatory and compendial standards:

| Regulation/Guideline | Description | Application to Glucogen-XR |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **USP <11>** | USP Reference Standards | Management, storage, and usage of USP RS. |
| **USP <1225>** | Validation of Compendial Procedures | Ensuring RS suitability during method transfer/validation. |
| **ICH Q6B** | Specifications: Test Procedures for Biotechnological/Biological Products | Requirement for characterizing reference materials for biologics. |
| **21 CFR 211.160** | General Requirements for Laboratory Controls | Requirement for scientifically sound and appropriate standards. |
| **21 CFR 211.194** | Laboratory Records | Documentation of RS purity, identity, and potency. |

---

### **3.0 Compendial Standards Utilized in Glucogen-XR DS Manufacture**

The following table lists the specific compendial standards utilized during the release and stability testing of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (Batch Series: GLUC-2025-XXX).

#### **Table 3.2.S.5.1.1-1: List of Compendial Reference Standards**

| RS Name | Source | Catalog No. | Intended Use |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **USP Glucagon RS** | USP | 1293008 | Secondary identification by HPLC-UV |
| **USP Insulin Human RS** | USP | 1342106 | System Suitability for impurities/related substances |
| **USP Endotoxin RS** | USP | 1235503 | Standard curve for LAL testing (Kinetic Turbidimetric) |
| **USP Dextrose RS** | USP | 1178001 | Content uniformity/Excipient verification |
| **USP Sodium Chloride RS** | USP | 1613802 | Osmolality calibration |

---

### **4.0 Detailed Suitability Assessment Protocol (SAP-GLUC-004)**

To ensure that the Compendial Reference Standard is fit for the purpose of testing Glucogen-XR, GHS executes a Suitability Assessment Protocol (SAP). This is critical because Glucogen-XR is an extended-release glucapeptide produced in the **GHS-CHO-001** cell line, which may present different impurity profiles than the original compendial source material.

#### **4.1 Identity Verification (Verification of Certificate of Analysis)**
Upon receipt of a new lot (e.g., USP Lot #L0M421), the Quality Control (QC) department verifies the C of A against the USP Daily Online update.
1.  **Lot Number Check:** Verify the lot is current and not "Valid Use Date" (VUD) expired.
2.  **Purity/Potency Assignment:** The assigned value (e.g., mg of peptide per mg of powder) is entered into the LIMS (LabVantage v8.4).

#### **4.2 Procedural Step-by-Step Suitability Testing**

For the USP Glucagon RS used in the Identity and Purity assays, the following procedure is followed:

**Step 1: Preparation of Standard Stock (SS)**
1.  Equilibrate the USP Glucagon RS vial to room temperature for 45 minutes in a desiccator.
2.  Accurately weigh 10.0 mg (±0.1 mg) using a Mettler Toledo XPR Microbalance (ID: GHS-EQ-092).
3.  Reconstitute in 10.0 mL of Diluent A (0.01 N HCl).
4.  Vortex for 30 seconds and sonicate for 5 minutes at 4°C.

**Step 2: Chromatographic Comparison (HPLC-UV)**
1.  Inject the USP RS and the Glucogen-XR Internal Primary Standard (Batch GLUC-2025-001-PS).
2.  **Criteria:** The retention time ($t_R$) of the main peak of the USP RS must be within $\pm$ 2.0% of the Glucogen-XR Internal Standard.
3.  **Resolution ($R_s$):** The resolution between the glucapeptide peak and the nearest deamidated degradant must be $> 1.5$.

#### **4.3 Statistical Analysis of Suitability**
The suitability is quantified using the Relative Response Factor (RRF) and the determination of System Suitability Testing (SST) parameters.

$$RSD = \frac{\sigma}{\bar{x}} \times 100$$

Where:
*   $\sigma$ = Standard deviation of 6 replicate injections of USP RS.
*   $\bar{x}$ = Mean peak area.
*   **Requirement:** $RSD \leq 0.73\%$ for assay suitability.

---

### **5.0 Analytical Data for Suitability (Representative Batch: GLUC-2025-401)**

The following table summarizes the suitability data obtained when comparing the USP Glucagon RS (Lot R087W0) against the Glucogen-XR Drug Substance.

#### **Table 3.2.S.5.1.1-2: Suitability Verification Results**

| Parameter | USP Requirement | Glucogen-XR Result (GLUC-2025-401) | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Identification (HPLC)** | Match Ret. Time | Match (Diff: 0.12 min) | PASS |
| **Peak Tailing ($T_f$)** | $\leq 2.0$ | 1.14 | PASS |
| **Theoretical Plates ($N$)** | $> 3000$ | 12,455 | PASS |
| **Mass Balance** | 98.0% - 102.0% | 99.8% | PASS |
| **Signal-to-Noise ($S/N$)** | $> 10$ (at LOQ) | 48.5 | PASS |

---

### **6.0 Storage and Handling (USP <11> Compliance)**

All Compendial Reference Standards are stored in the GHS Central Repository (Building 4, Room 202) under the following conditions:
*   **Temperature:** $-20^{\circ}C \pm 5^{\circ}C$ (Monitored by BlueMountain RAM System).
*   **Humidity:** Controlled via desiccated primary containers.
*   **Light:** Amber vials for light-sensitive materials.

**Re-evaluation Policy:** Unlike GHS-manufactured Reference Standards, Compendial Standards are not subjected to an independent shelf-life extension program. Once the USP declares a lot "Official Date Passed," the material is immediately decommissioned from the GLUC-2025-XXX production pipeline and replaced with the current official lot.

---

### **7.0 Handling of "Suitability Failures"**

In the event that a USP CRS fails to meet system suitability during a Glucogen-XR release run (e.g., peak splitting or unexpected baseline noise), the following OOS/OOT (Out of Specification/Trend) protocol is triggered:

1.  **Phase I Investigation:** Assessment of instrument (Waters ACQUITY UPLC) and analyst error.
2.  **Phase II Assessment:** Evaluation of the CRS lot integrity. If three independent preparations of the USP RS fail to meet the tailing factor requirement ($T_f < 2.0$), the lot is quarantined.
3.  **Cross-Verification:** The suspect USP lot is compared against a secondary compendial source (e.g., Ph. Eur. Glucagon CRS) to determine if the issue is lot-specific or matrix-specific.

---

### **8.0 Conclusion**

Based on the comparative analytical data and the rigorous adherence to USP <11> and ICH Q6B, the compendial reference standards listed herein are deemed **suitable for their intended use** in the qualification, release, and stability monitoring of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) Drug Substance. The use of these standards ensures the traceability of Glucogen-XR potency and purity to internationally recognized benchmarks.

---

## Comparison to In-House Standards

### **3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **3.2.S.5.1 Compendial Reference Standards**
##### **3.2.S.5.1.1 Comparison to In-House Standards**

---

### **1.0 Introduction and Purpose**
The qualification of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) necessitates a rigorous bridge between internationally recognized compendial standards (where applicable) and the Google Health Sciences (GHS) In-House Primary Reference Standard (IH-PRS). As Glucogen-XR is a novel, high-molecular-weight glucapeptide derivative expressed in the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line, no direct USP or EP monograph exists for the specific extended-release peptide sequence. However, comparison is mandated against USP Glucagon RS (Lot #R010V0) and USP Insulin Human RS (Lot #K0L231) for related substances, molecular weight profiling, and system suitability.

This section details the extensive analytical bridging studies performed at the GHS South San Francisco facility (Building 4, Analytical Sciences Lab) to calibrate the **GHS In-House Primary Reference Standard (Batch: GLUC-2025-001)** against established compendial benchmarks.

---

### **2.0 Reference Material Identification**

#### **2.1 Compendial Standards (External)**
| Standard Name | Source/Compendia | Lot Number | Potency/Purity | Expiry/Retest Date |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| USP Glucagon RS | USP | R010V0 | 0.98 mg/mg | 31-Dec-2026 |
| USP Insulin RS | USP | K0L231 | 28.7 USP units/mg | 30-Jun-2027 |
| USP Endotoxin RS | USP | H0K321 | 10,000 EU/vial | 15-Jan-2028 |

#### **2.2 In-House Primary Reference Standard (GHS)**
| Material | Batch Number | Date of Manufacture | Site of Manufacture | Purpose |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Glucogen-XR IH-PRS** | **GLUC-2025-001** | 12-Jan-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | Primary Calibration |
| **Glucogen-XR IH-WRS** | **GLUC-2025-002** | 04-Feb-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | Routine QC Testing |

---

### **3.0 Analytical Comparison Strategy**
In accordance with **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **USP <111> (Design and Analysis of Biological Assays)**, the comparison is divided into four critical pillars:
1. **Primary Structure and Identity Confirmation**
2. **Purity and Impurity Profile Bridging**
3. **Biological Potency Calibration**
4. **Physicochemical Property Alignment**

#### **3.1 Statistical Framework for Bridging**
The equivalence is determined using a Two One-Sided Test (TOST) approach with a predefined equivalence margin ($\theta$) of $\pm 5\%$ for potency and $\pm 2\%$ for purity.

**Formula for Equivalence Testing:**
$$90\% CI = (\bar{X}_1 - \bar{X}_2) \pm t_{0.05, df} \cdot SE \cdot \sqrt{\frac{1}{n_1} + \frac{1}{n_2}}$$
Where:
- $\bar{X}_1$ = Mean of Compendial Standard
- $\bar{X}_2$ = Mean of In-House Standard (GLUC-2025-001)

---

### **4.0 Detailed Analytical Protocols and Comparison Results**

#### **4.1 Protocol GHS-ANA-099: High-Resolution Mass Spectrometry (HRMS) Comparison**
**Objective:** To verify the molecular weight and glycosylation pattern of the In-House Standard against the predicted theoretical mass derived from the amino acid sequence, using USP Glucagon as a control for ionization efficiency.

**Step-by-Step Procedure:**
1.  **Preparation:** Reconstitute GLUC-2025-001 and USP Glucagon RS to 1.0 mg/mL in 0.1% Formic Acid.
2.  **Desalting:** Use a ZipTip C18 micro-column to remove residual salts from the CHO-K1 fermentation process.
3.  **Instrumentation:** Orbitrap Exploris 480 Mass Spectrometer; Electrospray Ionization (ESI) in positive mode.
4.  **Data Acquisition:** 400–2000 m/z range; Resolution 120,000 at m/z 200.
5.  **Deconvolution:** Use BioPharma Finder 4.1 software with the Xtract algorithm.

**Table 4.1-1: Mass Spectrometry Comparison Results**
| Attribute | USP Glucagon RS (Ref) | IH-PRS GLUC-2025-001 | Tolerance/Acceptance | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Theoretical Mass (Da) | 3482.75 | 42,345.82 (Peptide+Linker) | N/A | Pass |
| Observed Mass (Da) | 3482.74 ± 0.01 | 42,345.81 ± 0.05 | ± 0.5 Da | Pass |
| PTM: Deamidation (%) | 0.4% | 0.8% | < 2.0% | Pass |
| PTM: Oxidation (%) | 0.2% | 0.5% | < 1.5% | Pass |

---

#### **4.2 Protocol GHS-ANA-102: RP-HPLC Purity and Related Substances**
**Objective:** Compare the chromatographic profile of the IH-PRS against the compendial system suitability requirements for peptide purity.

**Chromatographic Conditions:**
- **Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC Protein BEH C4, 300Å, 1.7 µm, 2.1 x 150 mm.
- **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% TFA in Water.
- **Mobile Phase B:** 0.08% TFA in Acetonitrile.
- **Gradient:** 20% B to 45% B over 40 minutes.
- **Flow Rate:** 0.3 mL/min.
- **Detection:** UV at 214 nm and 280 nm.

**Table 4.2-1: Comparative Purity Analysis (n=6 replicates)**
| Parameter | USP Glucagon RS | GLUC-2025-001 (IH-PRS) | GLUC-2025-002 (WRS) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Main Peak (%) | 99.12 | 98.75 | 98.68 |
| Total Impurities (%) | 0.88 | 1.25 | 1.32 |
| RT of Main Peak (min) | 12.45 | 24.58* | 24.61* |
| RRT (Relative to USP) | 1.00 | 1.97 | 1.98 |

*\*Note: Increased retention time for GLUC-2025-001 is due to the extended-release lipophilic side-chain modification absent in standard glucagon.*

---

#### **4.3 Protocol GHS-BIO-005: In-Vitro Biological Activity (GLP-1R Agonism)**
**Objective:** To establish the biological potency of the GHS In-House Standard relative to the International Unit (IU) definition, using a Cell-Based Reporter Gene Assay.

**Cell Line:** HEK293 cells transfected with human GLP-1 receptor and a CRE-driven Luciferase reporter.

**Assay Procedure:**
1.  Seed cells at $5 \times 10^4$ cells/well in a 96-white-well plate.
2.  Incubate for 24 hours at 37°C, 5% CO2.
3.  Prepare serial dilutions (10-point) of GLUC-2025-001 and USP Glucagon RS (as a negative/low-affinity control) and a proprietary GLP-1 internal control.
4.  Add compounds to cells; incubate for 4 hours.
5.  Add Steady-Glo® Luciferase Reagent.
6.  Measure luminescence using a SpectraMax iD5 plate reader.

**Table 4.3-1: Potency Bridge Data**
| Sample ID | EC50 (pM) | Relative Potency (%) | 95% Confidence Interval |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLP-1 Control** | 12.5 | 100% (Assigned) | N/A |
| **GLUC-2025-001** | 14.2 | 88.0% | 84.5% - 91.5% |
| **GLUC-2025-002** | 14.4 | 86.8% | 83.1% - 90.5% |

---

### **5.0 Stability and Storage Conditions**
The IH-PRS (GLUC-2025-001) is stored in the GHS Central Repository under the following validated conditions:
- **Temperature:** -80°C ± 5°C (Ultra-Low Temperature Freezer, Asset ID: GHS-ULT-992).
- **Container:** 2.0 mL Type I Borosilicate glass vials with FluroTec® coated stoppers.
- **Monitoring:** Continuous temperature logging via Cloud-Linked sensors (Google Cloud IoT Core).

**Table 5.0-1: Real-Time Stability Data for IH-PRS (T=0 to T=24 Months)**
| Interval | Test Date | Batch | Purity (RP-HPLC) | Potency (%) | Appearance |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T=0 | 15-Jan-2025 | GLUC-2025-001 | 98.75% | 88.0% | Lyophilized White Cake |

| T=6m | 15-Jul-2025 | GLUC-2025-001 | 98.69% | 87.8% | Conforms |
| T=12m | 15-Jan-2026 | GLUC-2025-001 | [Pending] | [Pending] | [Pending] |

---

### **6.0 Compendial Alignment Summary**
While the Glucogen-XR molecule contains a unique 18-carbon fatty acid di-acid side chain linked via a γ-Glu spacer (not present in USP Glucagon), the fundamental glucapeptide backbone was compared against USP Glucagon RS for peptide mapping (via Trypsin Digestion).

**Protocol GHS-MAP-021: Tryptic Peptide Mapping**
1.  **Digestion:** IH-PRS GLUC-2025-001 treated with TPCK-treated Trypsin (1:20 ratio) for 16 hours.
2.  **Mapping:** C18 Reverse Phase separation.
3.  **Result:** All 4 expected fragments (T1, T2, T3, T4) matched the USP Glucagon fragmentation pattern, with the exception of the T2 fragment which contains the GLUC-XR specific modification, showing a predictable mass shift of +842.5 Da.

---

### **7.0 Conclusion**
The **In-House Primary Reference Standard GLUC-2025-001** has been comprehensively characterized and bridged against USP compendial standards. The data presented in this section confirms that the IH-PRS is fit for its intended use as the primary calibrator for all Glucogen-XR Release and Stability testing. The stability profile remains robust, and the biological activity is consistent with the pharmacological mechanism of action intended for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus treatment.

# Reference Standard Lifecycle Management

## Replacement Strategy

### **3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **3.2.S.5.1 Reference Standard Lifecycle Management**
#### **3.2.S.5.1.4 Replacement Strategy**

---

### **1.0 Introduction and Regulatory Rationale**

The replacement strategy for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) Drug Substance (DS) Primary and Working Reference Standards (PRS/WRS) is a multi-tiered, risk-based lifecycle management program. This strategy ensures the continuous availability of well-characterized, stable, and representative reference materials for the identity, purity, potency, and heterogenicity testing of Glucogen-XR. 

As per **ICH Q6B** (*Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products*), the replacement of reference standards must be supported by comprehensive analytical data demonstrating comparability between the "Old" (Current) and "New" (Candidate) lots. Google Health Sciences (GHS) employs a protocol-driven approach that integrates statistical equivalence testing, forced degradation comparisons, and orthogonal characterization to mitigate the risk of "drift" in the analytical baseline over the product lifecycle.

This document outlines the procedural requirements for the qualification of successor lots, the "bridging" protocols required for transition, and the inventory management triggers for initiating replacement.

---

### **2.0 Reference Standard Hierarchy and Replacement Triggers**

GHS maintains a two-tiered hierarchy to minimize the consumption of the Primary Reference Standard and to ensure long-term stability of the analytical baseline.

#### **2.1 Replacement Triggers**
The initiation of a replacement campaign for Glucogen-XR Reference Standards is triggered by one of the following conditions:

1.  **Inventory Depletion:** When the remaining inventory of a WRS or PRS reaches a "Critical Reorder Point" (CRP), defined as <18 months of projected use based on current testing volume (inclusive of stability program requirements).
2.  **Expiration/End of Retest Period:** Approaching the end of the validated shelf-life as determined by the Real-Time Stability Program (Section 3.2.S.5.1.5).
3.  **Stability Failure:** Any Out-of-Specification (OOS) or significant Out-of-Trend (OOT) result in the ongoing stability program that renders the current lot unsuitable.
4.  **Manufacturing Process Change:** Implementation of a "Moderate" or "Major" (CBE-30 or PAS) process change that results in a shift in the glycosylation profile or impurity profile such that the current RS no longer represents the commercial product.

#### **Table 2.1-1: Reference Standard Inventory and Trigger Specifications**

| Material Type | Identifier Series | Current Batch | Manufacturing Date | Current Inventory (Vials) | Reorder Trigger (Vials) | Retest Frequency |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary RS (PRS)** | GLUC-PRS-XXXX | GLUC-2025-001 | 14-JAN-2025 | 450 | 100 | Annually |
| **Working RS (WRS)** | GLUC-WRS-XXXX | GLUC-2025-002 | 12-FEB-2025 | 1,200 | 300 | Bi-annually |
| **Impurity RS** | GLUC-IMP-XXXX | GLUC-2025-009 | 05-MAR-2025 | 150 | 40 | Annually |

---

### **3.0 Candidate Lot Selection Criteria**

The selection of a candidate lot for replacement is a critical quality decision overseen by the **GHS Reference Standard Steering Committee (RSSC)**. 

#### **3.1 Technical Requirements for Candidate Lots**
1.  **Manufacturing Consistency:** The candidate lot must be manufactured using the validated commercial process (GHS-PRO-DS-01) at the 3000 Innovation Drive facility.
2.  **Purity Thresholds:** The candidate lot must meet all release specifications (Section 3.2.S.4.1) and exhibit purity levels (by RP-HPLC and SEC-HPLC) that are within ±0.5% of the current PRS.
3.  **Heterogeneity Profile:** The N-linked glycan profile (determined by HILIC-FLD/MS) must be representative of the historical mean (±2 SD) to ensure the potency assay remains calibrated to the average biological activity.
4.  **Formulation:** The candidate must be in the final DS formulation (10 mM Histidine, 5% Sucrose, 0.02% Polysorbate 20, pH 6.0) at the target concentration of 50.0 mg/mL.

---

### **4.0 Bridging Protocol: Qualification of Successor Lots**

The replacement of a reference standard requires a "Bridging Study" to assign values to the new lot and ensure continuity. This protocol follows the requirements of **USP <1226>** and **USP <1117>**.

#### **4.1 Statistical Approach for Bridging**
To ensure that the "New" RS (Candidate) does not introduce bias into the analytical methods, GHS utilizes a **Two One-Sided T-test (TOST)** approach for Equivalence Testing.

**Equation 1: Equivalence Calculation**
$$ \mu_{New} - \mu_{Old} < \theta $$
Where $\theta$ is the pre-defined equivalence margin (Acceptance Criterion) based on the Method Precision ($CV_{intermediate}$).

#### **4.2 Analytical Testing Matrix for Replacement**
Each candidate lot undergoes an exhaustive Characterization Matrix (CM).

#### **Table 4.2-1: Analytical Matrix for Successor Qualification**

| Category | Method ID | Parameter | Acceptance Criteria (vs. Current PRS) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Identity** | GHS-MET-ID-01 | Peptide Mapping (LC-MS/MS) | Equivalent Sequence Coverage (>98%) |
| **Potency** | GHS-MET-BIO-04 | In Vitro Cell-Based Bioassay | 90% - 110% Relative Potency |
| **Purity** | GHS-MET-PUR-02 | SEC-HPLC (Monomer %) | Difference $\le$ 0.3% |
| **Purity** | GHS-MET-PUR-05 | RP-HPLC (Main Peak %) | Difference $\le$ 0.5% |
| **Charge** | GHS-MET-CHG-01 | icIEF (Main Peak %) | Difference $\le$ 2.0% |
| **Glycan** | GHS-MET-GLY-08 | HILIC (Total Sialylation) | Difference $\le$ 1.5 mol/mol |
| **Physical** | USP <788> | Sub-visible Particles | Report Value |

---

### **5.0 Step-by-Step Procedure for Reference Standard Replacement**

The following procedure (SOP-QC-RS-099) must be followed for the transition from GLUC-2025-XXX to a successor lot.

#### **Step 1: Protocol Initiation**
- Generate a formal Qualification Protocol (e.g., **VAL-RS-202X-001**).
- Define the candidate lot (e.g., GLUC-2025-114).
- Verify the candidate lot has passed all Release Testing under GMP.

#### **Step 2: Dual-Testing Phase (The "Bridging Period")**
- Conduct a minimum of $n=10$ independent analytical runs where the "New" and "Old" RS are tested head-to-head.
- Operators: Minimum of three different analysts across different shifts.
- Equipment: Minimum of two different HPLC/UPLC systems (e.g., Waters ACQUITY H-Class).

#### **Step 3: Value Assignment (Calibration)**
- For quantitative attributes (e.g., Protein Concentration by $A_{280}$), the value for the New RS is assigned based on the mean of the $n=10$ bridging runs.
- **Formula for Adjusted Potency:**
  $$ Potency_{New\_Assigned} = Potency_{Candidate\_Measured} \times \left( \frac{Potency_{Old\_Declared}}{Potency_{Old\_Measured}} \right) $$

#### **Step 4: Forced Degradation Comparison**
- Subject both "Old" and "New" lots to thermal stress (40°C for 14 days) and photo-stress (1.2M lux hours).
- Compare degradation rates and species formation.
- **Requirement:** No new degradation species $\ge$ 0.05% in the New RS compared to the Old RS.

#### **Step 5: Documentation and Approval**
- Compile the **Reference Standard Qualification Report (RSQR)**.
- Quality Assurance (QA) reviews the statistical analysis.
- Update the **Certificate of Analysis (CoA)** for the new reference standard.

---

### **6.0 Inventory Phase-In/Phase-Out Strategy**

To prevent disruptions in the QC lab, a phased implementation is utilized.

1.  **Stage 1: Overlapping Use (Weeks 1-4):** The New RS is used for "Information Only" alongside the Old RS in routine testing.
2.  **Stage 2: Official Adoption (Week 5):** The New RS becomes the official standard for all GMP release and stability testing. The Old RS is relegated to "Backup" status.
3.  **Stage 3: Archiving:** 50 vials of the Old RS are moved to long-term "Retain" storage (-70°C) for historical "drift" investigations.

#### **Table 6.1-1: Example Replacement Timeline for GLUC-2025-114**

| Phase | Milestone | Responsible Party | Estimated Date |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Initiation** | CRP Trigger Reached (100 vials) | Inventory Control | 01-JUN-2026 |
| **Selection** | Candidate Lot GLUC-2025-114 Selected | RSSC | 15-JUN-2026 |
| **Testing** | Bridging Protocol Execution | QC Biologics | 01-JUL-2026 to 15-AUG-2026 |
| **Analysis** | Statistical Equivalence Report | Biostatistics | 01-SEP-2026 |
| **Approval** | QA Certification of GLUC-2025-114 | Quality Assurance | 15-SEP-2026 |
| **Go-Live** | Implementation in LIMS | IT/QC | 01-OCT-2026 |

---

### **7.0 Reference Standard Stability Program Replacement**

Upon qualification, the New RS is immediately entered into the **Reference Standard Stability Program (RSSP)**.

- **Storage Conditions:** -70°C ± 10°C (Primary), -20°C ± 5°C (Working).
- **Timepoints:** 0, 3, 6, 9, 12, 18, 24, 36, 48, 60 months.
- **Stability Protocol:** Refer to Section 3.2.S.5.1.5 for detailed method parameters and cumulative data analysis (CUSUM) to detect subtle degradation trends over the 5-year retest period.

---

### **8.0 Regulatory Commitments**

Google Health Sciences commits to the following:
1.  **Notification:** GHS will notify the FDA of Primary Reference Standard replacements via the **Annual Report** if the candidate lot meets all pre-defined specifications and equivalence margins.
2.  **Deviations:** Any failure to meet equivalence margins during the bridging of a PRS will be treated as a "Major Change" and submitted as a **Prior Approval Supplement (PAS)**.
3.  **Transparency:** All raw data from the bridging studies, including chromatograms and statistical worksheets, will be maintained at the 3000 Innovation Drive site for inspection.

---

### **9.0 Literature and Regulatory References**

1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures: Text and Methodology.
3.  **USP <1226>:** Verification of Compendial Procedures.
4.  **USP <1117>:** Best Practices for Microbiological Reference Material Management.
5.  **FDA Guidance (2015):** Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics.
6.  *Shimek, et al. (2019).* "Evolution of Reference Standards in Biopharmaceutical Development." *Journal of Pharmaceutical Sciences.*

---
**END OF SECTION**
