## Comparability Between Lots

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5: REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.3: REFERENCE STANDARD LIFECYCLE MANAGEMENT
#### PART 3.2.S.5.3.4: COMPARABILITY BETWEEN LOTS

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This subsection details the formal comparability assessment framework established by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)** for the qualification of new Primary and Working Reference Standard (RS) lots of **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**. In alignment with **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q5E** (Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products Subject to Changes in Their Manufacturing Process), this protocol ensures the continuity of the analytical link between historical clinical data and future commercial production.

The objective of the comparability program is to demonstrate that each new lot of Glucogen-XR reference material is analytically equivalent to the preceding lot (Master Reference Standard or current Working Reference Standard) within predefined statistical thresholds. This document covers the comprehensive testing matrix, statistical methodology, and the two-tiered bridge-study design employed by GHS.

---

### 2.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND GUIDANCE MATRIX

The comparability protocols for Glucogen-XR are designed to satisfy the rigorous requirements of the following regulatory bodies and pharmacopeial standards:

| Authority | Reference Number | Title/Description |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **FDA** | 21 CFR 211.160 | General Requirements for Laboratory Controls |
| **FDA** | 21 CFR 211.165 | Testing and Release for Distribution |
| **ICH** | ICH Q2(R1) | Validation of Analytical Procedures: Text and Methodology |
| **ICH** | ICH Q5E | Comparability of Biotechnological/Biological Products |
| **ICH** | ICH Q6B | Specifications: Test Procedures for Biological Products |
| **USP** | USP <1048> | Ancillary Materials for Cell, Gene, and Tissue-Engineered Products |
| **USP** | USP <1103> | Scanning Electron Microscopy |
| **USP** | USP <1225> | Validation of Compendial Procedures |

---

### 3.0 COMPARABILITY STRATEGY AND HIERARCHY

GHS employs a "Chain of Comparability" where each new lot is cross-referenced against the original **Clinical Master Reference Standard (C-MRS)**, lot **GLUC-2023-001**, to prevent "analytical drift" over the product lifecycle.

#### 3.1 Two-Tiered Bridge Study Design
1.  **Direct Comparison:** Simultaneous testing of the candidate lot against the current reference lot in the same analytical run (N=6 replicates per analyst).
2.  **Historical Trend Analysis:** Evaluation of the candidate lot data against the cumulative control charts (Levey-Jennings) of the current reference standard.

#### 3.2 Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs) for Comparability
The following attributes are deemed critical for establishing reference standard equivalence:
*   **Primary Structure:** Peptide mapping by LC-MS/MS.
*   **Higher Order Structure (HOS):** Circular Dichroism (CD) and FT-IR.
*   **Purity/Impurity Profile:** RP-HPLC, SE-HPLC, and CEX-HPLC.
*   **Biological Activity:** GLP-1 Receptor Activation Bioassay (In Vitro).
*   **Content:** UV-Vis Spectrophotometry ($\epsilon$ = 1.45 $L \cdot g^{-1} \cdot cm^{-1}$).

---

### 4.0 DETAILED COMPARABILITY DATA: BATCH GLUC-2025-RS04 VS. GLUC-2024-RS03

The following tables summarize the comparability data generated during the qualification of the most recent Working Reference Standard (WRS), **GLUC-2025-RS04**, compared to the previous standard, **GLUC-2024-RS03**.

#### Table 4.1: Physicochemical Characterization and Content Comparability

| Parameter | Method | Acceptance Criteria | Lot GLUC-2024-RS03 (Current) | Lot GLUC-2025-RS04 (Candidate) | Difference / P-Value |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual (GHS-SOP-55) | Clear, colorless | Conforms | Conforms | N/A |
| **Concentration** | UV ($A_{280}$) | $5.0 \pm 0.2$ mg/mL | 5.02 mg/mL | 4.98 mg/mL | 0.8% |
| **Purity (Monomer)** | SE-HPLC | $\geq 98.5\%$ | 99.4% | 99.3% | 0.1% |
| **Purity (Main Peak)** | RP-HPLC | $\geq 95.0\%$ | 97.2% | 97.5% | -0.3% |
| **Charge Heterogeneity** | CEX-HPLC | $75-85\%$ Main | 81.2% | 80.9% | 0.3% |
| **pH** | USP <791> | $6.5 \pm 0.2$ | 6.54 | 6.51 | 0.03 |
| **Endotoxin** | USP <85> | $\leq 0.5$ EU/mg | < 0.05 EU/mg | < 0.05 EU/mg | N/A |

#### Table 4.2: Biological Potency Comparability (GLP-1R Activation)
*Statistical analysis performed using Parallel Line Analysis (PLA) software.*

| Replicate | GLUC-2024-RS03 (Relative Potency %) | GLUC-2025-RS04 (Relative Potency %) | Difference (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1 | 102 | 98 | 4 |
| 2 | 98 | 101 | -3 |
| 3 | 105 | 103 | 2 |
| 4 | 97 | 99 | -2 |
| 5 | 100 | 102 | -2 |
| 6 | 101 | 97 | 4 |
| **Mean** | **100.5%** | **100.0%** | **0.5%** |
| **% RSD** | **2.8%** | **2.3%** | **N/A** |

---

### 5.0 ANALYITICAL PROTOCOL: PEPTIDE MAPPING BY LC-MS/MS

To ensure identity and primary sequence integrity between lots, GHS utilizes a high-resolution peptide mapping protocol.

#### 5.1 Reagents and Equipment
*   **Enzyme:** Tryptic Digestion (Promega Gold, Mass Spec Grade).
*   **LC System:** Agilent 1290 Infinity II UHPLC.
*   **Mass Spectrometer:** Thermo Scientific Orbitrap Exploris 480.
*   **Column:** Waters ACQUITY UPLC BEH C18, 1.7 $\mu$m, 2.1 x 150 mm.

#### 5.2 Step-by-Step Procedure
1.  **Denaturation:** Dilute 100 $\mu$g of Glucogen-XR into 6M Guanidine-HCl, 50 mM Tris-HCl (pH 8.0).
2.  **Reduction:** Add 10 mM Dithiothreitol (DTT); incubate at 56°C for 45 minutes.
3.  **Alkylation:** Add 25 mM Iodoacetamide (IAM); incubate in dark at RT for 30 minutes.
4.  **Desalting:** Utilize Zeba Spin Desalting Columns (7K MWCO).
5.  **Digestion:** Add Trypsin at a 1:20 (w/w) ratio; incubate at 37°C for 16 hours.
6.  **Quenching:** Add 1% Trifluoroacetic acid (TFA) to stop the reaction.
7.  **Analysis:** Inject 10 $\mu$L into the LC-MS/MS. Gradient 2-45% ACN over 60 minutes.

#### 5.3 Comparability Criteria for Peptide Mapping
*   **Retention Time ($t_R$):** The $t_R$ of all major peaks in the candidate lot must be within $\pm 0.2$ minutes of the reference lot.
*   **Mass Accuracy:** All identified peptides must show a mass error $< 5$ ppm.
*   **Sequence Coverage:** Must be $100\%$ for both lots.
*   **Mirror Plot Analysis:** Visual overlay of UV and TIC chromatograms must show no new peaks $> 0.05\%$ of total area.

---

### 6.0 STATISTICAL ANALYSIS OF COMPARABILITY

GHS applies the **Equivalence Testing (TOST - Two One-Sided Tests)** approach for quantitative CQAs.

#### 6.1 Calculation Formula
The null hypothesis ($H_0$) states that the difference between the mean of the candidate lot ($\mu_{can}$) and the reference lot ($\mu_{ref}$) exceeds the equivalence margin ($\theta$):

$$H_0: |\mu_{can} - \mu_{ref}| \geq \theta$$
$$H_a: |\mu_{can} - \mu_{ref}| < \theta$$

The margin $\theta$ is typically set at $1.5 \times SD_{hist}$ (historical standard deviation).

#### 6.2 Statistical Results for Batch GLUC-2025-RS04
| Parameter | $\theta$ (Margin) | Mean Diff | 90% CI Lower | 90% CI Upper | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Purity (RP) | 0.50% | 0.30% | 0.12% | 0.48% | **Equivalent** |
| Potency | 5.0% | 0.5% | -1.2% | 2.2% | **Equivalent** |
| Aggregation | 0.20% | 0.10% | 0.04% | 0.16% | **Equivalent** |

---

### 7.0 HIGHER ORDER STRUCTURE (HOS) ASSESSMENT

To confirm that the extended-release glucapeptide maintains its secondary and tertiary conformation, GHS performs Far-UV Circular Dichroism (CD).

#### 7.1 Circular Dichroism (CD) Parameters
*   **Instrument:** Jasco J-1500 Spectropolarometer.
*   **Pathlength:** 0.1 cm.
*   **Range:** 190 nm to 260 nm.
*   **Scan Speed:** 50 nm/min.
*   **Concentration:** 0.2 mg/mL in phosphate buffer.

#### 7.2 Results Summary
The Mean Residue Ellipticity $[\theta]$ at 208 nm and 222 nm (characteristic of $\alpha$-helical content) was calculated:
*   **GLUC-2024-RS03:** $[\theta]_{222} = -18,450$ $deg \cdot cm^2 \cdot dmol^{-1}$.
*   **GLUC-2025-RS04:** $[\theta]_{222} = -18,390$ $deg \cdot cm^2 \cdot dmol^{-1}$.
*   **Concordance:** Spectral correlation coefficient ($r$) = 0.9992.

---

### 8.0 STABILITY PROTOCOL DURING TRANSITION

When a new reference standard is introduced, a 6-month "co-stability" period is initiated where both the old and new lots are tested concurrently at the 0, 3, and 6-month intervals.

#### Table 8.1: Co-Stability Testing Matrix (Real-Time Storage: -70°C)

| Interval | Purpose | Testing Suite |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Month 0** | Baseline Establishment | Full Release + Characterization |
| **Month 3** | Trend Monitoring | HPLC (RP, SE, CEX), Potency |
| **Month 6** | Final Handover | HPLC (RP, SE, CEX), Potency, CD |

---

### 9.0 HANDLING OF OUT-OF-SPECIFICATION (OOS) IN COMPARABILITY

If the candidate lot fails the statistical equivalence test (TOST) or falls outside the predefined $3\sigma$ historical range, the following GHS protocol is triggered:

1.  **Phase I Investigation:** Laboratory assessment to identify analytical error or equipment drift.
2.  **Phase II Investigation:** Manufacturing review of batch **GLUC-2025-XXX** to identify process deviations in the CHO-K1 GS knockout line or purification steps.
3.  **Impact Assessment:** If the difference is "analytical but not biological," a formal Risk Assessment (GHS-RA-2025-09) is conducted to determine if the lot can be used with a corrected "Assigned Value" or if the lot must be rejected.

---

### 10.0 CONCLUSION

Based on the extensive physicochemical, structural, and biological data presented, lot **GLUC-2025-RS04** is demonstrated to be highly comparable to the preceding lot **GLUC-2024-RS03**. All statistical equivalence margins were met, and no significant differences in impurity profiles or higher-order structures were observed. Lot **GLUC-2025-RS04** is hereby qualified as the active Working Reference Standard for Glucogen-XR commercial release and stability testing, effective [Current Date].

---

*   *Head of Quality Control:* [Signature]
*   *Head of Regulatory Affairs:* [Signature]
*   *Manufacturing Lead (Google Health Sciences):* [Signature]

## Documentation and Record Keeping

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.5.4 REFERENCE STANDARD LIFECYCLE MANAGEMENT
### SUBSECTION: DOCUMENTATION AND RECORD KEEPING

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection details the comprehensive documentation and record-keeping framework established by Google Health Sciences (GHS) for the lifecycle management of Reference Standards (RS) associated with Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). In accordance with **ICH Q7 (Section 11.1)**, **21 CFR Part 211.194**, and **USP <1226>**, the integrity of the analytical data for Glucogen-XR is fundamentally dependent on the traceability, authenticity, and stability of the Primary (PRS) and Working Reference Standards (WRS).

The documentation system is hosted on the **Google Cloud Life Sciences (GCLS) Quality Document Management System (QDMS)**, a validated 21 CFR Part 11 compliant platform. This system ensures that every phase of the RS lifecycle—from initial synthesis/purification of the GLUC-2025 series batches to terminal decommissioning—is captured with high fidelity and metadata-rich audit trails.

---

#### 2.0 REGULATORY HIERARCHY AND COMPLIANCE STANDARDS
The documentation protocols described herein are designed to meet or exceed the following international regulatory requirements:

*   **FDA 21 CFR Part 211.160(b):** General requirements for the establishment of scientifically sound and appropriate specifications, standards, and sampling plans.
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **ICH Q2(R2):** Validation of Analytical Procedures.
*   **USP <1117>:** Best Storage and Shipping Practices.
*   **ISO 17034:2016:** General requirements for the competence of reference material producers.

---

#### 3.0 CORE DOCUMENTATION CATEGORIES
The lifecycle of Glucogen-XR Reference Standards is documented across five primary categories. Each category contains specific forms, logs, and reports required for a complete CMC (Chemistry, Manufacturing, and Controls) dossier.

##### 3.1 Characterization and Qualification Dossier (CQD)
The CQD is the foundational document for each new batch (e.g., Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01). It must contain:
1.  **Certificate of Analysis (CoA):** Comprehensive result set.
2.  **Structural Elucidation Report:** Including High-Resolution Mass Spectrometry (HRMS), 2D-NMR (COSY, HSQC, HMBC), and N-terminal sequencing.
3.  **Purity Profile:** RP-HPLC, SEC-HPLC, and CEX-HPLC chromatograms.
4.  **Potency Assignment:** Derived from the *in vitro* GLP-1 receptor activation bioassay.

##### 3.2 Chain of Custody and Inventory Logs
The "Physical Life" of the vial is tracked through:
1.  **The Master Inventory Ledger (MIL):** Real-time tracking of vial locations across GHS facilities.
2.  **Usage Logs:** Recording the exact mass (mg) withdrawn, the analyst ID, and the specific Project Code (e.g., GHS-GLUC-PH3-002).

##### 3.3 Stability Monitoring Records
Documentation of the degradation profile over time, including:
1.  **Stability Protocols:** Pre-defined testing intervals (0, 3, 6, 12, 24, 36 months).
2.  **Statistical Trend Analysis:** Calculations of degradation rates (k) using Arrhenius kinetics for accelerated studies.

---

#### 4.0 DETAILED BATCH RECORD DATA TABLES
The following tables represent the actualized data structure for the Glucogen-XR Reference Standard program.

##### Table 4.1: Master Reference Standard Batch Genealogy
| Batch Number | Type | Date of Manufacture | Site of Manufacture | Scale (Grams) | Purity (HPLC %) | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** | Primary | 12-JAN-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | 250.0g | 99.82% | Active |
| **GLUC-2025-WRS-01** | Working | 05-FEB-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | 1000.0g | 99.75% | Active |
| **GLUC-2025-WRS-02** | Working | 14-MAY-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | 1000.0g | 99.78% | Pending Qual |
| **GLUC-2025-EXT-01** | External | 20-MAR-2025 | Contract Site A (Boston) | 50.0g | 99.60% | Evaluation |

##### Table 4.2: Analytical Qualification Metadata Structure
For each batch, the following parameters are logged into the GCLS Cloud SQL database for GLP/GMP compliance:

| Parameter ID | Test Method | Equipment ID | Acceptance Criteria | Result (GLUC-2025-PRS-01) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **ID-001** | ESI-TOF MS | MS-GHS-09 | 4321.5 ± 0.5 Da | 4321.48 Da |
| **PUR-001** | RP-HPLC | HPLC-044 | ≥ 99.0% | 99.82% |
| **POT-001** | Cell Bioassay | BIA-021 | 95-105% of Target | 101.2% |
| **H2O-001** | Karl Fischer | KF-003 | ≤ 1.0% w/w | 0.42% w/w |
| **SOL-001** | GC-Headspace | GC-112 | ≤ 500 ppm | 112 ppm (Ethanol) |

---

#### 5.0 PROTOCOL: INITIAL QUALIFICATION DOCUMENTATION (SOP-GHS-RS-001)
*This protocol outlines the mandatory steps for documenting the birth of a new Reference Standard batch.*

**Step 1: Batch Nomination**
*   The Quality Control (QC) Director nominates a high-purity drug substance (DS) batch (e.g., GLUC-2025-DS-010) for RS conversion.
*   **Documentation Required:** Batch Nomination Form (Form GHS-77).

**Step 2: Aliquoting and Labeling**
*   RS is sub-aliquoted into 10mg lyophilized vials.
*   Each vial receives a unique 2D Matrix Barcode containing: Batch No, Vial No, Date of Fill, and Storage Requirement (-80°C).
*   **Documentation Required:** Aliquoting Logbook (Form GHS-82).

**Step 3: Multi-Laboratory Characterization**
*   Samples are sent to three independent GHS-qualified labs for orthogonal testing.
*   **Calculation of Assigned Value:**
    $$ Purity_{assigned} = \frac{\sum_{i=1}^{n} (Purity_{Lab-i})}{n} $$
    *Where n = number of labs.*
*   **Documentation Required:** Inter-laboratory Comparison Report (Report GHS-R-2025-01).

**Step 4: Quality Assurance (QA) Release**
*   QA reviews the "Reference Standard Summary Folder."
*   Final sign-off in the GCLS QDMS.

---

#### 6.0 CALCULATION METHODOLOGIES FOR POTENCY ASSIGNMENT
The Glucogen-XR RS documentation must include the raw data and the mathematical models used for potency assignment. For glucapeptides, we utilize a **Four-Parameter Logistic (4PL) Model** for bioassay documentation.

**Formula 4.1: 4PL Model for Bioassay**
$$ y = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B} $$

Where:
*   **A** = Minimum asymptote (zero signal)
*   **B** = Hill slope (steepness of the curve)
*   **C** = $EC_{50}$ (Potency)
*   **D** = Maximum asymptote (saturated signal)

Documentation must include the $R^2$ value (Requirement: $R^2 \geq 0.995$) and the Residual Sum of Squares (RSS).

---

#### 7.0 STORAGE AND DISTRIBUTION RECORDS (USP <659> COMPLIANCE)
Glucogen-XR is highly sensitive to thermal fluctuations. Record keeping for storage involves:

1.  **Continuous Temperature Monitoring (CTM):** Data from the GHS Cloud-linked sensors (Model: G-Temp-2025) are archived every 60 seconds.
2.  **Mean Kinetic Temperature (MKT) Calculation:**
    $$ T_{k} = \frac{\Delta H / R}{-\ln \left( \frac{e^{-\Delta H / RT_1} + e^{-\Delta H / RT_2} + \dots + e^{-\Delta H / RT_n}}{n} \right)} $$
    *This value is recorded in the Annual Reference Standard Review (ARSR).*

##### Table 7.1: Excursion Log Example (Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01)
| Date | Duration | Temp Max | Impact Assessment | Deviation Ref # |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 14-MAR-2025 | 12 mins | -65°C | Negligible; within T90 | DEV-GLUC-0045 |
| 22-JUN-2025 | 2 mins | -72°C | Door open for inventory | N/A |

---

#### 8.0 PERIODIC RE-QUALIFICATION AND EXTENSION DOCUMENTATION
Working Reference Standards (WRS) for Glucogen-XR expire every 12 months unless extension data is provided.

**Protocol for Extension:**
1.  **Pull Date:** 30 days prior to expiry.
2.  **Testing:** Full suite as per Table 4.2.
3.  **Comparison:** New data compared to "Time Zero" ($T_0$) using a t-test ($\alpha = 0.05$).
4.  **Reporting:** If $P > 0.05$, a **Shelf-Life Extension Memo** is generated and appended to the CoA.

---

#### 9.0 RETENTION AND ARCHIVING
In accordance with **21 CFR 211.180**, all records pertaining to the Glucogen-XR Reference Standards shall be maintained for:
*   At least 5 years after the date of manufacture of the last batch of drug product manufactured using the RS.
*   At least 1 year after the expiration date of the last batch of drug product.

All digital records are backed up across three geographically distinct Google Cloud regions (us-central1, us-east1, and europe-west1) with immutable storage buckets to prevent unauthorized deletion or alteration.

#### 10.0 REFERENCES
1.  *Google Health Sciences Quality Manual (GHS-QM-2024).*
2.  *United States Pharmacopeia (USP) Chapter <11> Reference Standards.*
3.  *European Pharmacopoeia (Ph. Eur.) 5.12 Reference Standards.*
4.  *ICH Q1A(R2) Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.*

**End of Subsection**

# Reference Materials for Impurity Testing

## Aggregate Standards

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.5.2 REFERENCE MATERIALS FOR IMPURITY TESTING
### SUBSECTION: 3.2.S.5.2.1 AGGREGATE STANDARDS (HIGH MOLECULAR WEIGHT SPECIES)

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This section delineates the characterization, qualification, and maintenance of Reference Standards specifically designated for the identification and quantification of High Molecular Weight Species (HMWS), including dimers, trimers, and higher-order oligomeric aggregates of Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). 

Glucogen-XR is a 31-amino acid peptide analog produced in a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout cell line (GHS-CHO-001). Due to the hydrophobic nature of the GLP-1 receptor agonist peptide and the extended-release formulation kinetics, the monitoring of covalent and non-covalent aggregation is critical to ensuring clinical safety (mitigating immunogenicity risks) and maintaining pharmacological potency.

The establishment of the **Primary Aggregate Reference Standard (PARS)** and the **Working Aggregate Reference Standard (WARS)** follows ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and ICH Q3D.

---

#### 2.0 PHYSICAL-CHEMICAL DEFINITION OF GLUCOGEN-XR AGGREGATES

Aggregates in Glucogen-XR are categorized into three distinct classes for which reference materials are maintained:

1.  **Covalent Dimers/Oligomers:** Irreversible species formed via disulfide shuffling or dityrosine cross-linking.
2.  **Non-Covalent Reversible Aggregates:** Concentration-dependent assemblies held by hydrophobic interactions.
3.  **Sub-visible Particulates:** Species in the 2 µm to 100 µm range, governed by USP <787> and USP <788>.

**Table 1: Target Specifications for Glucogen-XR Aggregate Reference Standards**

| Attribute | Methodology | Primary Standard (PARS) Target | Working Standard (WARS) Target |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Purity (Monomer %)** | SEC-HPLC/MALS | > 99.0% (Enriched for impurity ID) | < 5.0% (System Suitability) |
| **Dimer Content** | SEC-HPLC | 45.0% - 55.0% (Forced Degradation) | 2.0% - 5.0% |
| **Higher Order Aggregates** | AUC (Analytical Ultracentrifugation) | > 10.0% | Report Results |
| **Secondary Structure** | Circular Dichroism (CD) | Distorted Alpha-helix | Match Reference |
| **Particulate Matter** | MFI (Micro-flow Imaging) | > 10,000 particles/mL (>10µm) | < 2,000 particles/mL |

---

#### 3.0 BATCH GENEALOGY AND MANUFACTURING OF AGGREGATE STANDARDS

Unlike the Primary Drug Substance Reference Standard, which represents the highest purity material, the Aggregate Standards are intentionally generated to represent specific impurity profiles.

##### 3.1 Batch GLUC-2025-AG-001 (Primary Aggregate Standard)
Manufactured at Google Health Sciences Facility (3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco). This batch was generated via thermal stress of the Clinical Batch GLUC-2024-012.

**Manufacturing Protocol for GLUC-2025-AG-001:**
1.  **Starting Material:** 500 mL of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (20 mg/mL in 20mM Citrate Buffer, pH 5.5).
2.  **Thermal Stress:** Incubation at 45°C ± 0.5°C for 72 hours in a calibrated ICH Q1A stability chamber (ID: GHS-STAB-09).
3.  **Mechanical Stress:** Orbital shaking at 300 RPM for 12 hours to induce sub-visible particulate formation.
4.  **Concentration:** Ultrafiltration/Diafiltration (UF/DF) using a 3kDa Pellicon 3 membrane to reach 50 mg/mL.
5.  **Aliquotting:** 0.5 mL per Type I Borosilicate Glass vial; nitrogen overlay; stoppered with FluroTec® coated chlorobutyl stoppers.

---

#### 4.0 ANALYTICAL CHARACTERIZATION PROTOCOLS

The following procedures are utilized to qualify the Aggregate Standards against established Google Health Sciences (GHS) internal specifications and USP/ICH requirements.

##### 4.1 Size Exclusion Chromatography with Multi-Angle Light Scattering (SEC-MALS)
SEC-MALS is the primary tool for determining the absolute molecular mass of the aggregates in the reference standard, independent of elution volume.

*   **Column:** TSKgel G2000SWxl, 7.8 mm ID x 30 cm, 5 µm.
*   **Mobile Phase:** 50 mM Phosphate, 150 mM NaCl, pH 7.0.
*   **Flow Rate:** 0.5 mL/min.
*   **Detector 1:** UV at 214 nm and 280 nm.
*   **Detector 2:** Wyatt DAWN HELEOS II (18-angle light scattering).
*   **Calculation:** Zimm plot analysis using ASTRA 7.3 software.

**Table 2: SEC-MALS Results for Batch GLUC-2025-AG-001**

| Peak ID | Retention Time (min) | Calculated Mol. Weight (kDa) | Mass Fraction (%) | Assignment |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Peak 1 | 12.45 | 72.4 ± 2.1 | 12.4% | HMW Oligomer |
| Peak 2 | 14.82 | 14.2 ± 0.4 | 48.2% | Dimer |
| Peak 3 | 18.90 | 7.1 ± 0.2 | 39.4% | Monomer |

##### 4.2 Analytical Ultracentrifugation (AUC-SEDPHAT)
AUC is utilized as an orthogonal, matrix-free method to validate SEC results, specifically to detect aggregates that might be filtered out or dissociated by the SEC column matrix.

*   **Equipment:** Beckman Coulter Optima AUC.
*   **Rotor:** AN-60 Ti.
*   **Parameters:** 45,000 RPM, 20°C, 8 hours.
*   **Data Analysis:** Sedimentation velocity c(s) distribution using SEDFIT software version 16.1.

**Table 3: AUC Sedimentation Coefficient Distribution**

| S-value ($S_{20,w}$) | Identification | Frictional Ratio (f/f0) | Integration % |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 1.2S | Monomer | 1.25 | 38.5% |
| 2.1S | Dimer | 1.38 | 49.1% |
| 3.5S+ | Higher Aggregates | 1.62 | 12.4% |

---

#### 5.0 ESTABLISHMENT OF WORKING AGGREGATE REFERENCE STANDARD (WARS)

The Working Aggregate Reference Standard (WARS), Batch **GLUC-2025-WAG-005**, is derived by spike-incorporation of the Primary Standard (PARS) into the current GMP Drug Substance. This creates a "system suitability" standard used for daily SEC-HPLC runs.

##### 5.1 Formulation Protocol for WARS
1.  Calculate volume of PARS (GLUC-2025-AG-001) required to achieve a 5.0% Dimer content.
2.  **Formula:** $V_{spike} = \frac{C_{target} \times V_{total}}{C_{stock}}$
3.  Perform aseptic blending in a Class 100 Laminar Flow Hood.
4.  Verification of final concentration via $A_{280}$ extinction coefficient ($\epsilon = 1.45 \text{ L g}^{-1} \text{ cm}^{-1}$).

---

#### 6.0 STABILITY AND RE-QUALIFICATION PROGRAM

To ensure the integrity of the Aggregate Standards, GHS maintains a rigorous stability monitoring program according to ICH Q1B.

**Table 4: Re-qualification Schedule for GLUC-2025 Series Standards**

| Storage Condition | Frequency | Required Tests | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **-80°C (Primary)** | Annual | SEC-HPLC, MFI, Potency | No significant change (>5%) in monomer % |
| **2-8°C (Working)** | Quarterly | SEC-HPLC, Visual | Dimer content within 4.5% - 5.5% |

##### 6.1 Statistical Evaluation of Drift
GHS utilizes a Bayesian linear regression model to predict the degradation rate of the Dimer species within the reference standard. If the 95% Confidence Interval (CI) of the Monomer % falls below 98.0% for the PARS, a new standard batch must be initiated.

$$y_t = \beta_0 + \beta_1 t + \epsilon$$
Where:
*   $y_t$ = Monomer percentage at time $t$.
*   $\beta_1$ = Degradation rate constant.
*   $\epsilon$ = Analytical variance ($s^2 \leq 0.05$).

---

#### 7.0 PROCEDURAL PROTOCOL: USE OF AGGREGATE STANDARDS IN RELEASE TESTING

**SOP-GHS-QC-4402: Calibration of SEC-HPLC for Glucogen-XR**

1.  **Thawing:** Remove one vial of GLUC-2025-WAG-005 from -80°C storage. Thaw at room temperature for 30 minutes. Do not vortex.
2.  **Dilution:** Dilute to 1.0 mg/mL using Mobile Phase.
3.  **Injection Volume:** 20 µL.
4.  **System Suitability Requirement:**
    *   Resolution ($R_s$) between Monomer and Dimer $\geq 1.5$.
    *   Symmetry Factor (As) for Monomer peak: 0.8 - 1.2.
    *   Relative Standard Deviation (RSD) of Peak Area (n=5) $\leq 2.0\%$.
5.  **Integration:** Use a "valley-to-valley" integration method for the HMW region to ensure conservative estimation of impurities.

---

#### 8.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND DOCUMENTATION

All Aggregate Reference Standards described herein comply with:
*   **21 CFR Part 211.160:** General requirements for laboratory controls.
*   **USP <1226>:** Verification of Analytical Procedures.
*   **EP 2.2.46:** Chromatographic Separation Techniques.

**Reference IDs for Supporting Data:**
*   Characterization Report: **GHS-RPT-AGG-2025-001**
*   MALS Validation Study: **GHS-VAL-MALS-099**
*   Container Closure Integrity Test: **GHS-CCIT-2025-04**

---
*End of Subsection 3.2.S.5.2.1*

## Process-Related Impurity Standards

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.5)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: 3.2.S.5.1 PROCESS-RELATED IMPURITY STANDARDS

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.1 Introduction and Scope
This section details the characterization, qualification, and lifecycle management of the reference standards utilized for the detection, identification, and quantification of process-related impurities in Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) drug substance. 

In accordance with **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **ICH Q3A(R2) (Impurities in New Drug Substances)**, Google Health Sciences (GHS) has established a comprehensive suite of reference materials to ensure the removal of manufacturing residuals to levels deemed safe for chronic administration in Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus patients.

The manufacturing process for Glucogen-XR, utilizing the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 (CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative) cell line and a sophisticated fed-batch bioreactor system followed by an extended-release PEGylation/encapsulation matrix, necessitates rigorous control over three primary categories of process-related impurities:
1. **Cell-Derived Impurities:** Host Cell Proteins (HCPs) and Host Cell DNA (hcDNA).
2. **Process-Derived Impurities:** Protein A leachates, Cell Culture Media Components (Insulin, Methotrexate, Pluronic F-68), and Anti-foam residuals.
3. **Downstream/Modification Impurities:** Unreacted PEG (Polyethylene Glycol) species, catalysts, and organic solvents used during the extended-release formulation phase.

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.2 Host Cell Protein (HCP) Reference Standard
The quantification of HCPs in Glucogen-XR is performed using a multi-product, high-sensitivity Enzyme-Linked Immunosorbent Assay (ELISA). The reference standard for this assay is the **GHS-CHO-HCP-Standard-05**, derived from a mock fermentation of the GHS-CHO-001 cell line lacking the Glucogen-XR expression vector.

##### 3.2.S.5.1.2.1 Preparation of HCP Standard (Batch: GLUC-2025-HCP-001)
The HCP reference material was generated following a "null cell" fermentation protocol to ensure the protein profile accurately reflects the endogenous proteins encountered during the actual purification process.

**Protocol HCP-PREP-09:**
1.  **Inoculation:** GHS-CHO-001 (Null) cells were thawed from WCB-002 and expanded in CD-CHO medium until a density of $5.0 \times 10^6$ cells/mL was achieved.
2.  **Bioreactor Phase:** A 50L SUB (Single-Use Bioreactor) was operated for 14 days under identical parameters to the Glucogen-XR production run (pH 7.0, DO 40%, Temp 36.5°C).
3.  **Harvest:** Cells were removed via depth filtration (Millistak+® HC Pod).
4.  **Concentration:** The harvest was concentrated 20-fold via Tangential Flow Filtration (TFF) using a 10 kDa MWCO membrane.
5.  **Dialysis:** Buffer exchanged into Phosphate Buffered Saline (PBS) pH 7.2.

##### 3.2.S.5.1.2.2 HCP Standard Characterization and Qualification Data
Table 1 summarizes the results for the current primary HCP reference standard.

**Table 1: Qualification of HCP Reference Standard (Batch: GLUC-2025-HCP-001)**

| Parameter | Test Method | Specification | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | Visual Inspection | Clear to slightly opalescent | Conforms |
| **Total Protein** | BCA Assay (USP <1057>) | 1.0 - 2.0 mg/mL | 1.48 mg/mL |
| **Purity/Profile** | SDS-PAGE (Silver Stain) | Multi-band distribution (10-150 kDa) | Conforms (Figure 1) |
| **Purity/Profile** | 2D-PAGE / Silver Stain | > 800 distinct spots | 942 spots |
| **Identity** | LC-MS/MS (Proteomics) | Match to CHO-K1 Proteome | 98.4% Match |
| **Antibody Coverage**| 2D-Western Blot | > 70% coverage | 84.5% Coverage |
| **Endotoxin** | LAL (USP <85>) | < 50 EU/mg | 12 EU/mg |
| **Bioburden** | USP <61> | < 10 CFU/mL | 0 CFU/mL |

*Footnote 1: Coverage calculation formula: $(\text{Number of Western Blot Spots} / \text{Number of Silver Stain Spots}) \times 100$.*

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.3 Host Cell DNA (hcDNA) Reference Standard
The detection of residual DNA is performed via Quantitative Polymerase Chain Reaction (qPCR) targeting a highly conserved 120-bp sequence of the CHO-K1 genome.

##### 3.2.S.5.1.3.1 Specification of hcDNA Reference Material (Batch: GLUC-2025-DNA-04)
The reference standard consists of highly purified genomic DNA extracted directly from the GHS-CHO-001 master cell bank.

**Table 2: Genomic DNA Reference Standard Specifications**

| Attribute | Method | Requirement | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Concentration** | NanoDrop $A_{260}$ | 100 - 150 $\mu$g/mL | 124.2 $\mu$g/mL |
| **Purity ($A_{260}/A_{280}$)** | Spectrophotometry | 1.7 - 2.0 | 1.88 |
| **Integrity** | Agarose Gel (0.8%) | High molecular weight (> 20 kb) | Conforms |
| **Residual Protein** | BCA Assay | < 0.1% (w/w) | 0.04% |
| **Standard Curve $R^2$** | qPCR | $\geq 0.990$ | 0.998 |
| **PCR Efficiency** | qPCR | 90 - 110% | 102.4% |

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.4 Process-Derived Chemical Impurity Standards
Glucogen-XR utilizes specific chemical reagents in its manufacturing that require tracking via reference standards.

##### 3.2.S.5.1.4.1 Protein A Leachate Standard
Because the first purification step utilizes Protein A affinity chromatography (MabSelect Sure), leaching of the Protein A ligand is a potential impurity. 

*   **Reference Material:** Ligand-specific recombinant Protein A (rPrA).
*   **Batch Number:** GLUC-2025-PRA-002.
*   **Source:** Repligen Corp (Secondary Qualification by GHS).
*   **Storage:** $-80^\circ C$.

##### 3.2.S.5.1.4.2 PEG-Carbonate Reference Standard
As Glucogen-XR is a PEGylated peptide for extended release, residual unactivated 40kDa-PEG-Carbonate must be monitored.

**Table 3: PEG-Carbonate Standard (Batch: GLUC-2025-PEG-012)**

| Analysis | Method | Limit | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Molecular Weight** | MALDI-TOF | 38,000 - 42,000 Da | 40,150 Da |
| **Polydispersity** | SEC-MALS | $\leq 1.05$ | 1.02 |
| **Active Species** | NMR ($^1$H-NMR) | $\geq 98\%$ active | 99.2% |
| **Residual Solvent** | GC-Headspace | < 500 ppm (DCM) | 120 ppm |

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.5 Analytical Procedures for Impurity Standard Qualification

##### 3.2.S.5.1.5.1 Determination of HCP Antibody Coverage (2D-Western Blot)
This protocol is critical for ensuring the HCP reference standard provides a representative profile of the potential impurities in the drug substance.

1.  **Isoelectric Focusing (IEF):** 100 $\mu$g of HCP Standard (GLUC-2025-HCP-001) is loaded onto a pH 3-10 IPG strip.
2.  **SDS-PAGE:** The strip is transferred to a 4-12% Bis-Tris gel for second-dimension separation.
3.  **Transfer:** Duplicate gels are run; one is stained with Silver Stain (Total Protein), the other is transferred to a PVDF membrane.
4.  **Immunoblotting:** The membrane is blocked with 5% non-fat milk and incubated with the anti-CHO HCP polyclonal antibody (GHS-Ab-009) at a 1:2000 dilution.
5.  **Detection:** Chemiluminescence detection using HRP-conjugated secondary antibody.
6.  **Image Analysis:** Alignment of the Silver Stained gel image and the Western Blot image using **GHS-BioImage-Pro Software**. 
    *   *Calculation:* % Coverage = $(\text{Spots identified on Blot} / \text{Spots identified on Silver Stain}) \times 100$.

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.6 Maintenance and Stability of Impurity Standards

##### 3.2.S.5.1.6.1 Stability Program for Process-Related Standards
Reference standards are subject to a formal stability program (GHS-SOP-QA-442) to ensure the integrity of the data throughout the product lifecycle.

**Table 4: Stability Schedule for Impurity Standards**

| Standard ID | Storage | Frequency | Key Stability Indication |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **HCP Std** | $-80^\circ C$ | Annual | 2D-PAGE Profile Stability |
| **hcDNA Std** | $-20^\circ C$ | Every 2 Years | PCR Amplification Efficiency |
| **Protein A** | $-80^\circ C$ | Annual | ELISA Reactivity |
| **PEG Std** | $-20^\circ C$ | Every 3 Years | $M_w$ via SEC |

##### 3.2.S.5.1.6.2 Re-qualification Protocol
Upon reaching the expiration date or if a trend is observed in stability data, the following protocol is initiated:
1.  **Visual comparison** against a retained "gold-standard" aliquot.
2.  **Functional assay:** Run a standard curve in the relevant impurity assay (ELISA or qPCR).
3.  **Statistical Assessment:** The Slope and Intercept of the new curve must be within $\pm 10\%$ of the original qualification data.

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.7 Traceability and Documentation
All process-related impurity standards are tracked using the Google Cloud Life Sciences **LIMS (Laboratory Information Management System)**. Each vial is assigned a unique Global Trade Item Number (GTIN) and a QR code linked to the Certificate of Analysis (CoA) and the specific manufacturing batch record (e.g., BR-GLUC-HCP-2025-001).

**Reference Documentation Cross-Index:**
*   *Validation of HCP ELISA:* Report VAL-2025-ELISA-HCP
*   *Validation of hcDNA qPCR:* Report VAL-2025-PCR-DNA
*   *Characterization of GHS-CHO-001 Cell Line:* Section 3.2.S.2.3

---

#### 3.2.S.5.1.8 Statistical Analysis of Reference Standard Performance
To ensure the robustness of the Glucogen-XR impurity testing, Google Health Sciences employs a Bayesian approach to monitor the performance of reference standards across multiple testing sites (South San Francisco, CA and Google Cloud Life Sciences Node, Dublin).

The following formula is used to calculate the **Relative Bias ($B_r$)** of a new impurity standard batch compared to the previous lot:

$$B_r = \left( \frac{\bar{X}_{new} - \bar{X}_{old}}{\bar{X}_{old}} \right) \times 100$$

Where:
*   $\bar{X}_{new}$ is the mean recovery of a known spiked sample using the new standard.
*   $\bar{X}_{old}$ is the mean recovery using the current standard.

An acceptance criterion of $B_r \leq 15\%$ is applied for HCP standards, and $B_r \leq 20\%$ for hcDNA standards, reflecting the inherent variability of biological matrices.

---

### [END OF SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.1]

---

## Forced Degradation Samples

### **3.2.S.5.3 Reference Materials for Impurity Testing: Forced Degradation Samples**

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.1 Introduction and Regulatory Scope**
In accordance with **ICH Q1A(R2)** (*Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products*), **ICH Q1B** (*Photostability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products*), and **ICH Q3A(R2)** (*Impurities in New Drug Substances*), Google Health Sciences (GHS) has established a comprehensive library of Forced Degradation Samples (FDS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release). 

The primary objective of this section is to document the generation, characterization, and utilization of degradation materials used as reference markers for the validation of stability-indicating analytical procedures. These samples serve as the "ground truth" for ensuring that the analytical methods—specifically Reversed-Phase High-Performance Liquid Chromatography (RP-HPLC), Size-Exclusion Chromatography (SEC-HPLC), and Hydrophilic Interaction Liquid Chromatography (HILIC)—are capable of resolving the parent Glucogen-XR molecule from its potential degradants, including deamidated, oxidized, truncated, and aggregated species.

#### **3.2.S.5.3.2 Manufacturing Site and Quality Oversight**
All forced degradation studies were conducted at the Google Health Sciences primary development facility:
*   **Site Address:** 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080, USA.
*   **Quality Management System (QMS):** All studies adhered to GHS-SOP-6621 (*Stress Testing of Biologics*) and GHS-SOP-9980 (*Reference Standard Qualification*).

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.3 Protocol for Generation of Stress Samples**
The generation of forced degradation samples for Glucogen-XR utilized Drug Substance Batch **GLUC-2025-001-A** (Purity: 99.4% by RP-HPLC). The goal of the stress program was to achieve a target degradation of 10% to 20% of the main peak to ensure sufficient signal-to-noise ratios for the identification of secondary and tertiary degradants without causing total molecular destruction.

##### **Table 1: Summary of Stress Conditions and Target Degradation Pathways**

| Stress Category | Specific Condition | Reagents/Equipment | Target Degradation Pathway | Protocol ID |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Acid Hydrolysis** | 0.1M HCl, 40°C, 24h | Thermo-Scientific Incubator (ID: INC-099) | Deamidation, Asp-Pro Cleavage | GHS-PRO-01A |
| **Base Hydrolysis** | 0.1M NaOH, 25°C, 6h | Mettler Toledo pH Control (ID: PH-442) | Racemization, Deamidation | GHS-PRO-01B |
| **Oxidation** | 3.0% H₂O₂, 25°C, 4h | Darkened Quartz Vessel | Met-Sulfoxide, Trp-Oxidation | GHS-PRO-01C |
| **Thermal (Dry)** | 60°C, 7 Days | Binder Vacuum Oven (ID: VO-221) | Aggregation, Pyroglutamate | GHS-PRO-01D |
| **Thermal (Liquid)** | 50°C, 48h (pH 7.4) | Circulating Water Bath | High Molecular Weight Species | GHS-PRO-01E |
| **Photolysis** | 1.2M Lux-hr / 200 W/m² | Caron Photostability Chamber | Tyr-Crosslinking, His-Oxid | GHS-PRO-01F |
| **Freeze/Thaw** | 5 Cycles (-80°C to RT) | Stirling Ultra-Low Freezer | Denaturation/Aggregation | GHS-PRO-01G |

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.4 Step-by-Step Stress Procedures**

##### **Subsection 3.2.S.5.3.4.1: Protocol GHS-PRO-01A (Acidic Stress)**
1.  **Preparation:** Aliquot 10 mL of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (10 mg/mL) into a 20 mL Type I Borosilicate glass vial.
2.  **Acidification:** Slowly add 1.0M Hydrochloric Acid (Trace Metal Grade) to reach a final concentration of 0.1M HCl.
3.  **Incubation:** Seal vial with a Teflon-lined cap. Place in a calibrated incubator at 40.0°C ± 0.5°C for exactly 24 hours.
4.  **Neutralization:** Remove from heat. Place on ice for 5 minutes. Neutralize to pH 7.0 using 1.0M Sodium Hydroxide.
5.  **Storage:** Immediate dilution for HPLC analysis; remaining sample stored at -80°C as **Reference Batch GLUC-2025-FDS-ACID**.

##### **Subsection 3.2.S.5.3.4.2: Protocol GHS-PRO-01C (Oxidative Stress)**
1.  **Preparation:** Dilute Glucogen-XR to 5 mg/mL in Phosphate Buffered Saline (PBS).
2.  **Oxidant Addition:** Add Hydrogen Peroxide (H₂O₂) to a final concentration of 3.0% (v/v).
3.  **Incubation:** Incubate at 25°C in the dark for 4 hours.
4.  **Quenching:** Add 100 mM L-Methionine (free amino acid) to quench residual peroxide.
5.  **Purification:** Desalt using a PD-10 column into formulation buffer to prevent long-term radical damage.
6.  **Storage:** Labeled as **Reference Batch GLUC-2025-FDS-OXID**.

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.5 Analytical Characterization of Forced Degradation Samples**

To qualify these samples as reference materials, they underwent extensive characterization via Mass Spectrometry (LC-MS/MS) to map the exact sites of degradation.

##### **Table 2: Characterization Data for FDS Reference Batches**

| Reference ID | Primary Degradant Identified | Site of Modification | Method | Observed Mass Delta (Da) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2025-FDS-ACID** | [Asp15]-Glucapeptide | Aspartic Acid Hydrolysis | LC-MS | +0.98 |
| **GLUC-2025-FDS-OXID** | [Met(O)27]-Glucapeptide | Methionine 27 Sulfoxide | LC-MS | +15.99 |
| **GLUC-2025-FDS-BASE** | [isoAsp9]-Glucapeptide | Succinimide Intermediate | Peptide Map | +0.00 (Isobaric) |
| **GLUC-2025-FDS-PHOTO** | Dityrosine Dimer | Tyr13-Tyr13 Crosslink | SEC-UV | +Parent Mass |
| **GLUC-2025-FDS-HEAT** | C-terminal Truncation | Loss of Gly-Arg | Orbitrap MS | -213.22 |

##### **Calculation of Degradation Recovery (Mass Balance)**
Mass balance was calculated for each stress condition using the following formula:
$$Mass Balance (\%) = \frac{Area_{Main} + \sum Area_{Degradants}}{Area_{Control}} \times 100$$
The criteria for an acceptable stress study for reference standard qualification is a mass balance of $95\% - 105\%$.

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.6 Chromatographic Resolution Requirements**
The Forced Degradation Samples are used during system suitability testing for the **GHS-METH-331 (Stability-Indicating RP-HPLC)**. 

##### **Table 3: System Suitability Criteria using FDS Reference Standards**

| Parameter | Required Performance | Reference Standard Used | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Resolution (Rs)** | Rs ≥ 1.5 between Main Peak and Impurity 1 | GLUC-2025-FDS-ACID | Ensures separation of deamidated species |
| **Relative Retention Time (RRT)** | 0.92 ± 0.02 | GLUC-2025-FDS-OXID | Identifies Met-Oxidized marker |
| **Peak Purity Angle** | Angle < Threshold | All FDS Samples | Ensures no co-eluting degradants |
| **Signal-to-Noise (S/N)** | S/N > 10 for 0.05% spike | GLUC-2025-FDS-LOW | Sensitivity check for trace impurities |

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.7 Storage and Stability of FDS Reference Materials**
Unlike the primary reference standard (GLUC-2025-PRS), forced degradation samples are intrinsically unstable. 
*   **Storage Temperature:** Frozen at -80°C ± 5°C.
*   **Re-qualification Period:** 12 months.
*   **Usage Policy:** Single-use aliquots to prevent freeze-thaw induced artifacts.

Each aliquot is tracked via the **Google LIMS (Laboratory Information Management System)** with a unique barcode (e.g., `GHS-LIMS-FDS-88712`).

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.8 Detailed Mass Spectrometry Mapping (Exemplary Case: Oxidative Stress)**
To confirm the utility of **GLUC-2025-FDS-OXID** as a reference for impurity testing, the sample was subjected to Tryptic Digestion followed by LC-MS/MS.

**1. Tryptic Digestion Protocol:**
*   Buffer: 50 mM Ammonium Bicarbonate, pH 8.0.
*   Reduction: 5 mM DTT at 56°C for 45 min.
*   Alkylation: 15 mM Iodoacetamide at RT in dark for 30 min.
*   Enzyme: Trypsin (Sequence Grade) at 1:20 ratio.
*   Duration: 16 hours at 37°C.

**2. MS Parameters:**
*   Instrument: Thermo Fisher Orbitrap Exploris 480.
*   Resolution: 120,000 at m/z 200.
*   Fragmentation: HCD (Higher-energy Collisional Dissociation) at 28% NCE.

**3. Results:**
The peptide fragment `T-15 (G-L-U-C-A-P-E-P-T-I-D-E-M-V-R)` showed a mass shift from $m/z$ 845.41 (2+) to $m/z$ 853.41 (2+), corresponding to the addition of one oxygen atom (+16 Da) at the Methionine residue. This peak corresponds to **Impurity RRT 0.92** in the standard release method, thereby validating the reference sample's utility for impurity tracking.

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.9 Statistical Evaluation of Forced Degradation Precision**
To ensure the reproducibility of the degradation markers, five independent preparations of **GLUC-2025-FDS-ACID** were performed.

| Preparation ID | % Main Peak | % Deamidation 1 | % Deamidation 2 | Total Degradation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Prep 1 | 82.1 | 12.4 | 5.5 | 17.9 |
| Prep 2 | 81.8 | 12.6 | 5.6 | 18.2 |
| Prep 3 | 82.5 | 12.2 | 5.3 | 17.5 |
| Prep 4 | 82.0 | 12.5 | 5.5 | 18.0 |
| Prep 5 | 82.3 | 12.3 | 5.4 | 17.7 |
| **Mean** | **82.14** | **12.40** | **5.46** | **17.86** |
| **% RSD** | **0.32%** | **1.25%** | **2.01%** | **1.45%** |

The low %RSD (<5.0%) across five preparations demonstrates the robustness of the Google Health Sciences forced degradation protocol, ensuring that these reference materials are consistent for use across global testing sites.

---

#### **3.2.S.5.3.10 Conclusion**
The established Forced Degradation Samples for Glucogen-XR provide a scientifically rigorous basis for the identification and quantification of product-related impurities. By aligning with **ICH Q2(R1)** validation requirements, these materials ensure that the life-cycle management of the Glucogen-XR drug substance is supported by high-resolution, stability-indicating analytical technology. All FDS batches are maintained under stringent environmental controls and are subject to the same Google Cloud Life Sciences data integrity standards as clinical-grade materials.

---

# Reference Panels for Biological Assays

## Dose-Response Standards

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.5.2 REFERENCE PANELS FOR BIOLOGICAL ASSAYS
### SUBSECTION: DOSE-RESPONSE STANDARDS (DRS)

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
The establishment of Dose-Response Standards (DRS) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) is a critical component of the potency assessment strategy. As a GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via a proprietary CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative (GHS-CHO-001), Glucogen-XR exhibits complex pharmacodynamics characterized by sustained receptor activation. 

The Dose-Response Standards defined herein are utilized to calibrate the Primary Biological Reference Standard (PBRS) and the Working Biological Reference Standard (WBRS) against the International Standard (if applicable) or to maintain internal consistency across the product lifecycle. These standards ensure that the relative potency ($RP$) of clinical and commercial lots is determined with a precision and accuracy compliant with ICH Q6B and USP <1032>, <1033>, and <1034>.

---

### 2.0 REGULATORY FRAMEWORK AND COMPLIANCE
The development, qualification, and maintenance of the Dose-Response Standards for Glucogen-XR adhere to the following regulatory guidelines:
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **ICH Q2(R2):** Validation of Analytical Procedures.
*   **USP <1032>:** Design and Development of Biological Assays.
*   **USP <1033>:** Biological Assay Methods Validation.
*   **USP <1034>:** Analysis of Biological Assays.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** Bioanalytical Method Validation (2018).
*   **21 CFR Part 211.160:** General Requirements for Laboratory Controls.

---

### 3.0 PREPARATION OF DOSE-RESPONSE REFERENCE PANELS
The Dose-Response Standards are prepared from high-purity Drug Substance (DS) batches characterized by Google Health Sciences (GHS) Quality Control (QC). 

#### 3.1 Selection of Batches for DRS Calibration
Batches selected for the Dose-Response Panel must meet stringent purity requirements (HPLC-SEC > 99.0%, RP-HPLC > 98.5%). 

**Table 1: Source Materials for Dose-Response Standard Panel (Batch Series GLUC-2025-DRS)**

| Component ID | Manufacturing Batch | Date of Manufacture | Storage Temp | Initial Potency (IU/mg) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **DRS-LEVEL-1** | GLUC-2025-012 | 14-JAN-2025 | -80°C ± 5°C | 1.02 ± 0.05 |
| **DRS-LEVEL-2** | GLUC-2025-015 | 22-JAN-2025 | -80°C ± 5°C | 0.98 ± 0.04 |
| **DRS-LEVEL-3** | GLUC-2025-018 | 05-FEB-2025 | -80°C ± 5°C | 1.05 ± 0.03 |
| **DRS-LEVEL-4** | GLUC-2025-021 | 18-FEB-2025 | -80°C ± 5°C | 1.01 ± 0.02 |

#### 3.2 Aliquoting and Storage
Reference panels are aliquoted into 0.5 mL medical-grade cyclic olefin polymer (COP) vials (Equipment ID: GHS-FILL-09) at a concentration of 2.0 mg/mL in a formulation buffer (20 mM Histidine, 100 mM NaCl, 0.02% Polysorbate 80, pH 6.5).

---

### 4.0 BIOLOGICAL ACTIVITY ASSAY (GLP-1R cAMP ACTIVATION)
The primary bioassay for Glucogen-XR is a cell-based reporter gene assay or a direct cAMP measurement using a HEK293 cell line stably transfected with the human GLP-1 receptor (GLP-1R).

#### 4.1 Assay Principle
Glucogen-XR binds to the GLP-1 receptor, a G-protein coupled receptor (GPCR), stimulating adenylate cyclase and increasing intracellular cyclic adenosine monophosphate (cAMP). The DRS ensures the sigmoidal dose-response curve (4-Parameter Logistic Fit) remains within specified asymptotes ($A$ and $D$) and slope ($B$) parameters.

#### 4.2 Step-by-Step Calibration Protocol (Protocol GHS-BIO-772)
1.  **Cell Seeding:** Seed GLP-1R HEK293 cells at a density of $5.0 \times 10^4$ cells/well in 96-well plates. Incubate for 24 hours at 37°C, 5% $CO_2$.
2.  **Serial Dilution:** Prepare an 8-point serial dilution of the DRS-Level-3 (Batch GLUC-2025-018) in Assay Medium (DMEM + 0.1% BSA).
    *   *Dilution Factor:* 1:3.
    *   *Concentration Range:* 0.001 nM to 100 nM.
3.  **Stimulation:** Add diluted DRS to the cell plate. Incubate for 45 minutes at 37°C.
4.  **Lysis and Detection:** Lyse cells using proprietary lysis buffer (GHS-LB-001) and add cAMP detection reagents (HTRF or equivalent).
5.  **Signal Measurement:** Measure fluorescence at 665nm/620nm using the PHERAstar FSX (Equipment ID: GHS-READ-22).

---

### 5.0 STATISTICAL ANALYSIS AND CURVE FITTING
The data generated from the Dose-Response Standards are analyzed using a 4-Parameter Logistic (4PL) model according to the equation:

$$y = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B}$$

Where:
*   $y$ = Response (Fluorescence Ratio)
*   $x$ = Concentration of Glucogen-XR (nM)
*   $A$ = Minimum Asymptote (Baseline)
*   $B$ = Hill Slope (Sensitivity)
*   $C$ = $EC_{50}$ (Potency)
*   $D$ = Maximum Asymptote (Efficacy)

#### 5.1 Acceptance Criteria for DRS Validity
The DRS must meet the following statistical thresholds to be considered valid for lot release testing:

**Table 2: Validity Criteria for DRS Curves**

| Parameter | Acceptance Limit | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Coefficient of Determination ($R^2$)** | $\geq 0.99$ | Ensures goodness of fit |
| **Slope (B)** | $0.85 - 1.25$ | Consistency of receptor binding kinetics |
| **Signal-to-Noise Ratio** | $\geq 5.0$ | Assay sensitivity and robustness |
| **Relative Bias (Accuracy)** | $\pm 15\%$ | Accuracy across the linear range |
| **Parallelism (Prob > F)** | $> 0.05$ | Similarity between standard and sample |

---

### 6.0 CALIBRATION DATA AND BATCH ANALYSIS
The following table provides the historical performance data for the current Dose-Response Reference Panel (Batch Series GLUC-2025-XXX).

**Table 3: Potency Analysis of DRS Panel (Batch GLUC-2025-018)**

| Run ID | Date | $EC_{50}$ (nM) | Hill Slope | Max Signal (RFU) | Min Signal (RFU) | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| R-202501 | 01-MAR-2025 | 1.22 | 1.05 | 14,500 | 420 | PASS |
| R-202502 | 02-MAR-2025 | 1.18 | 1.10 | 14,200 | 415 | PASS |
| R-202503 | 03-MAR-2025 | 1.25 | 0.98 | 14,800 | 430 | PASS |
| R-202504 | 04-MAR-2025 | 1.21 | 1.02 | 14,650 | 425 | PASS |
| **Mean** | -- | **1.215** | **1.038** | **14,538** | **422.5** | -- |
| **%CV** | -- | **2.4%** | **4.9%** | **1.7%** | **1.5%** | -- |

---

### 7.0 STABILITY PROGRAM FOR DOSE-RESPONSE STANDARDS
DRS vials are subjected to an ongoing stability program (Protocol GHS-STAB-99) to ensure that the biological activity remains constant over the intended shelf life.

#### 7.1 Stability Monitoring Schedule
*   **Long-Term:** -80°C ± 5°C (Tested at 0, 3, 6, 12, 18, 24, 36 months).
*   **Accelerated:** -20°C ± 5°C (Tested at 0, 1, 3, 6 months).
*   **Stress:** 5°C ± 3°C (Tested at 0, 7, 14, 30 days).

**Table 4: Stability Data for Batch GLUC-2025-018 (3-Month Data)**

| Time Point | Storage Temp | Assay | Result (% of T0) | Specification |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T0 (Initial) | -80°C | Potency | 100% | 80% - 125% |
| T3 (3 Months)| -80°C | Potency | 99.2% | 80% - 125% |
| T3 (3 Months)| -20°C | Potency | 97.5% | 80% - 125% |

---

### 8.0 DILUTION LINEARITY AND PARALLELISM
To ensure the DRS is suitable for the calculation of Relative Potency ($RP$), parallelism must be demonstrated between the DRS and several "Mock" samples representing 50%, 75%, 100%, 125%, and 150% of the nominal potency.

#### 8.1 Formula for Relative Potency ($RP$)
The $RP$ is calculated by comparing the $EC_{50}$ of the Sample ($S$) to the $EC_{50}$ of the Reference Standard ($RS$):

$$RP = \frac{EC_{50, RS}}{EC_{50, S}}$$

For the Glucogen-XR Dose-Response Standard, the $EC_{50, RS}$ is fixed based on the consensus mean of 20 independent assay runs (N=20) conducted during qualification.

---

### 9.0 EQUIPMENT AND INSTRUMENTATION
All bioassay procedures involving the Dose-Response Standards utilize qualified equipment listed in the GHS Quality Management System (QMS).

*   **Liquid Handler:** Hamilton STARlet (Asset ID: GHS-HAM-04).
*   **Incubator:** Thermo Heracell VIOS 160i (Asset ID: GHS-INC-12).
*   **Microplate Reader:** BMG LABTECH PHERAstar FSX (Asset ID: GHS-READ-22).
*   **Analysis Software:** SoftMax Pro GxP v7.1.

---

### 10.0 CONCLUSION
The Dose-Response Standards (DRS) established for Glucogen-XR (GLUC-2025 series) provide a robust and reproducible benchmark for biological potency. Through rigorous qualification, statistical modeling via USP <1034>, and continuous stability monitoring, Google Health Sciences ensures that every lot of Glucogen-XR maintains the therapeutic efficacy required for the treatment of Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus.

---
**Footnotes:**
1. GHS-CHO-001 is a proprietary cell line derivative of CHO-K1 GS-/-.
2. Batch GLUC-2025-018 serves as the current master calibration lot for bioassay drift monitoring.
3. All calculations performed using Google Cloud Life Sciences AI-Assisted Statistical Suite (v4.2).

## System Suitability Standards

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (DATA SUMMARY)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5: REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.2: REFERENCE PANELS FOR BIOLOGICAL ASSAYS
#### PART B: SYSTEM SUITABILITY STANDARDS (SSS)

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND REGULATORY RATIONALE

The System Suitability Standards (SSS) for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** are designed to ensure that the analytical performance of the biological potency assays, specifically the GLP-1 Receptor Activation Assay (Cell-Based Bioassay), remains consistent, reproducible, and compliant with regulatory expectations as outlined in **ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products)** and **USP <111> (Design and Analysis of Biological Assays)**.

Given the complex molecular architecture of Glucogen-XR—a recombinant glucapeptide fusion protein produced in the **GHS-CHO-001 (CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative)** cell line—the biological activity is sensitive to conformational changes, post-translational modifications (PTMs), and aggregation states. Therefore, the SSS serves as the gatekeeper for assay validity, ensuring that the cellular environment, reagent potency, and instrumentation are operating within established control limits before any reportable value is generated for a GMP batch release (e.g., Batch **GLUC-2025-001** through **GLUC-2025-500**).

#### 1.1 Scope
This document details the preparation, qualification, and maintenance of the System Suitability Standards used in the following assays:
1.  **GLP-1R In Vitro Potency Assay (cAMP-based Reporter Gene Assay)**
2.  **Competitive Binding Affinity Assay (Surface Plasmon Resonance - SPR)**
3.  **Extended Release Kinetic Profile Bioassay (Simulated Physiological Release)**

---

### 2.0 HIERARCHY OF REFERENCE MATERIALS

System suitability is maintained through a tiered hierarchy of materials. All materials are manufactured at the **Google Health Sciences (GHS) facility at 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA**.

| Material Tier | Designation | Batch ID Format | Purpose |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Primary Reference Standard (PRS)** | GHS-GLUC-PRS-01 | GLUC-2025-PRS-01 | Calibration of Secondary Standards; defined as 100% potency. |
| **Working Reference Standard (WRS)** | GHS-GLUC-WRS-XX | GLUC-2025-WRS-02 | Day-to-day assay comparison and dose-response curve generation. |
| **System Suitability Standard (SSS)** | GHS-GLUC-SSS-XX | GLUC-2025-SSS-01 | Internal "control" to verify assay sensitivity and precision. |
| **Negative Control (NC)** | GHS-NC-001 | N/A | Non-specific protein (Albumin) to verify assay specificity. |

---

### 3.0 SYSTEM SUITABILITY PARAMETERS AND ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA

The biological assay for Glucogen-XR utilizes a 4-parameter logistic (4-PL) regression model. For an assay run to be considered "Suitable," the following criteria must be met using the System Suitability Standard (Batch **GLUC-2025-SSS-01**).

#### 3.1 Statistical Model: 4-Parameter Logistic (4-PL) Equation
The potency of Glucogen-XR is calculated using the following sigmoid function:

$$y = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B}$$

Where:
*   **$y$**: Bioassay Response (Relative Luminescence Units, RLU)
*   **$x$**: Concentration of Glucogen-XR (ng/mL)
*   **$A$**: Minimum response (Bottom Asymptote)
*   **$B$**: Hill Slope (Slope Factor)
*   **$C$**: $EC_{50}$ (Concentration at half-maximal response)
*   **$D$**: Maximum response (Top Asymptote)

#### 3.2 Table of Suitability Requirements (Method: GHS-BIO-009)

| Parameter | Identifier | Acceptable Range | Rationale |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Coefficient of Determination** | $R^2$ | $\ge 0.985$ | Verifies goodness of fit for the 4-PL model. |
| **Slope Ratio** | $B_{SSS} / B_{WRS}$ | $0.80 - 1.25$ | Ensures parallelism between SSS and Reference Standard. |
| **Relative Potency (RP)** | $RP_{SSS}$ | $0.90 - 1.10$ | Verifies the SSS performs within 10% of expected activity. |
| **Signal-to-Noise Ratio** | $D / A$ | $\ge 15.0$ | Ensures sufficient window for detection of GLP-1R activation. |
| **Precision (Intra-assay)** | $\%CV$ (triplicates) | $\le 15.0\%$ | Ensures minimal pipetting/technical error. |
| **EC50 Absolute Value** | $C$ | $12.5 - 24.8$ ng/mL | Verifies cell line sensitivity (GHS-CHO-001). |

---

### 4.0 DETAILED PREPARATION PROTOCOL FOR SSS (GLUC-2025-SSS-01)

The SSS is prepared by diluting the formulated Drug Substance (DS) into a stabilized Bioassay Matrix (BAM-001).

#### 4.1 Reagents and Equipment
*   **Reference Item:** Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (Batch GLUC-2025-004)
*   **Diluent:** GHS-BAM-001 (HEPES buffered saline, 0.1% Human Serum Albumin, 0.05% Polysorbate 80)
*   **Equipment:** Automated Liquid Handling System (Hamilton Microlab STAR - Asset ID: GHS-EQ-112)
*   **Storage:** Cryogenic Vials (Nunc, 1.8 mL)

#### 4.2 Step-by-Step Procedure
1.  **Thawing:** Thaw one vial of Glucogen-XR DS at $25^{\circ}C$ in a water bath for 15 minutes.
2.  **Primary Dilution:** Perform a 1:100 dilution in GHS-BAM-001 to reach a nominal concentration of $100 \mu g/mL$.
3.  **Intermediate Dilution:** Perform serial dilutions to reach the assay starting concentration of $2000 ng/mL$.
4.  **Aliquotting:** Aliquot $150 \mu L$ into 500 pre-labeled vials (Batch **GLUC-2025-SSS-01-A** through **GLUC-2025-SSS-01-Z**).
5.  **Storage:** Rapidly freeze in liquid nitrogen vapor phase and transfer to $-80^{\circ}C$ storage.

---

### 5.0 QUALIFICATION DATA FOR BATCH GLUC-2025-SSS-01

The following table summarizes the validation of the System Suitability Standard against the Primary Reference Standard.

**Table 5.1: Qualification Results for SSS Batch GLUC-2025-SSS-01**
*Tested on: 14-JAN-2025 | Analyst: GHS-QA-992*

| Run ID | Parameter | Result | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **RUN-001** | $R^2$ | 0.9992 | PASS |

| **RUN-002** | $R^2$ | 0.9987 | PASS |
| **RUN-002** | Relative Potency | 0.98 | PASS |
| **RUN-002** | $EC_{50}$ | 19.1 ng/mL | PASS |
| **RUN-003** | $R^2$ | 0.9995 | PASS |
| **RUN-003** | Relative Potency | 1.01 | PASS |
| **RUN-003** | $EC_{50}$ | 17.9 ng/mL | PASS |
| **MEAN** | **-** | **RP: 1.003** | **MEETS SPEC** |

---

### 6.0 CELL LINE SUITABILITY (GHS-CHO-001)

The SSS is inextricably linked to the performance of the **GHS-CHO-001** cell line. System suitability fails if the cell line drift exceeds established limits.

#### 6.1 Cell Passage Limits
*   **Minimum Passage:** 5 (Recovery period after thaw)
*   **Maximum Passage:** 25 (End of validated growth phase)
*   **Cell Viability at Seeding:** $\ge 95\%$ (Measured via Vi-CELL BLU, GHS-EQ-442)

#### 6.2 Cell Density Requirements
The SSS must be analyzed when the cell density in the 96-well assay plate is $4.0 \times 10^4$ cells/well. Deviations $>10\%$ in cell density require a systemic review of the suitability data.

---

### 7.0 MAINTENANCE AND TRENDING

Google Health Sciences employs a "Rolling Suitability Trend Analysis" using JMP Statistical Software (Version 17.0).

#### 7.1 Control Charting
For every GMP release assay conducted for Glucogen-XR, the $EC_{50}$ and Hill Slope ($B$) of the SSS (Batch **GLUC-2025-SSS-01**) are plotted on a Shewhart Control Chart.

*   **Warning Limit:** $\pm 2$ Standard Deviations (SD)
*   **Action Limit:** $\pm 3$ Standard Deviations (SD)

#### 7.2 Protocol for Suitability Failure
In the event that the SSS fails to meet the criteria in Section 3.2:
1.  The entire assay run is invalidated.
2.  A Laboratory Investigation Report (LIR) is initiated under SOP-GHS-QA-004.
3.  Equipment (e.g., Plate Reader GHS-EQ-881) is inspected for calibration drift.
4.  Reagents (e.g., cAMP Detection Kit, Batch #GHS-CAMP-2025) are checked for degradation.
5.  If three consecutive SSS failures occur, the cell bank (GHS-CHO-001-MCB) must be re-evaluated for phenotypic stability.

---

### 8.0 REFERENCES
1.  **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures: Text and Methodology.
2.  **USP <1032>:** Design and Development of Biological Assays.
3.  **USP <1033>:** Biological Assay Validation.
4.  **USP <1034>:** Analysis of Biological Assays.
5.  **GHS-SOP-552:** Manufacturing Procedure for Glucogen-XR Reference Panels.

## Assay Control Materials

# SECTION 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
## SUBSECTION: Assay Control Materials for Biological and Physicochemical Characterization

### 3.2.S.5.1 Introduction and Scope of Assay Control Materials
The characterization and lifecycle management of Assay Control Materials (ACM) for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) are governed by the rigorous standards established under ICH Q6B (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and ICH Q2(R1) (Validation of Analytical Procedures). 

Google Health Sciences (GHS) employs a hierarchical approach to control materials to ensure the longitudinal consistency of the GLP-1 receptor agonist potency, molecular integrity, and extended-release kinetics. Unlike the Primary Reference Standard (PRS), which is used for absolute quantification, the Assay Control Materials (ACMs) are utilized as "system suitability monitors" and "internal drift indicators" across the analytical landscape.

### 3.2.S.5.2 Categorization of Control Materials
Assay Control Materials for Glucogen-XR are stratified into three distinct functional tiers:

1.  **Bioassay Positive Controls (BPC):** Used in the GLP-1 Receptor Activation Assay (Cell-based cAMP induction).
2.  **Physicochemical Performance Controls (PPC):** Used for SEC-HPLC (Aggregates), RP-HPLC (Purity), and CE-SDS (Purity/Impurity profile).
3.  **Process-Specific Controls (PSC):** Used for Host Cell Protein (HCP) ELISAs and Residual DNA (rDNA) qPCR assays.

---

### 3.2.S.5.3 Detailed Inventory of Assay Control Materials (Batch GLUC-2025-XXX)

The following table details the current active inventory of control materials utilized at the South San Francisco manufacturing facility (3000 Innovation Drive).

#### Table 1: Current Inventory of Glucogen-XR Assay Control Materials
| Control ID | Batch Number | Functional Category | Date of Manufacture | Retest Date | Storage Conditions |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **AC-GLP1-001** | GLUC-2025-01A | Bioassay Control | 12-JAN-2025 | 12-JAN-2027 | -80°C ± 5°C |
| **AC-SEC-042** | GLUC-2025-04B | SEC Aggregate Control | 15-FEB-2025 | 15-FEB-2026 | 2°C - 8°C |
| **AC-RPH-019** | GLUC-2025-09C | Purity/Isoform Control | 03-MAR-2025 | 03-MAR-2026 | -20°C ± 2°C |
| **AC-HCP-112** | GLUC-2025-12K | Process Impurity | 20-MAR-2025 | 20-MAR-2027 | -80°C ± 5°C |
| **AC-IVR-005** | GLUC-2025-05R | In Vitro Release | 10-FEB-2025 | 10-AUG-2025 | 2°C - 8°C |

---

### 3.2.S.5.4 Bioassay Control Materials (BPC): Protocols and Characterization

#### 3.2.S.5.4.1 Role in GLP-1 Receptor Activation Assay
The BPC (Batch GLUC-2025-01A) is a qualified aliquot of the drug substance used to ensure that the CHO-K1 cells expressing the human GLP-1 receptor are responding within the validated linear range. The BPC is evaluated for its $EC_{50}$ (half-maximal effective concentration).

#### 3.2.S.5.4.2 Protocol for BPC Qualification (SOP-GHS-BIO-492)
1.  **Cell Culture Preparation:** Thaw CHO-K1 GS knockout cells (GHS-CHO-001) in DMEM/F12 medium supplemented with 10% Dialyzed FBS.
2.  **Seeding:** Seed cells at $2.5 \times 10^4$ cells/well in a 96-well white-walled plate.
3.  **Sample Preparation:** Dilute GLUC-2025-01A in Assay Buffer (HBSS + 0.1% BSA + 0.5 mM IBMX) to a starting concentration of 100 nM.
4.  **Serial Dilution:** Perform 1:3 serial dilutions across 10 points.
5.  **Detection:** Add LANCE Ultra cAMP detection reagents. Measure TR-FRET signal (665nm/615nm ratio).
6.  **Data Analysis:** Fit data to a 4-parameter logistic (4PL) regression model.

#### 3.2.S.5.4.3 Acceptance Criteria for Bioassay Control
The following statistical parameters must be met for the BPC to validate the run:
*   **Asymptotic Maximum ($Top$):** $12,000 \pm 1,500$ RFU
*   **Asymptotic Minimum ($Bottom$):** $400 \pm 100$ RFU
*   **Hill Slope:** $1.0 \pm 0.2$
*   **$EC_{50}$:** $4.2 \pm 0.8$ pM
*   **$R^2$ Value:** $> 0.985$

---

### 3.2.S.5.5 Physicochemical Control Materials (PPC)

#### 3.2.S.5.5.1 Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC) Control (GLUC-2025-04B)
To monitor the formation of high molecular weight species (HMWS) and low molecular weight species (LMWS), a "System Suitability Standard" (SSS) is prepared by inducing controlled stress (thermal incubation at 40°C for 72 hours) on a subset of Batch GLUC-2025-04B.

#### Table 2: SEC Control Material Specification and Historical Performance
| Parameter | Batch GLUC-2025-04B Result | Specification | Method Reference |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Main Peak (%)** | 97.42% | $\geq 96.0\%$ | USP <129> / GHS-SEC-01 |
| **HMWS (%)** | 2.15% | $\leq 3.0\%$ | USP <129> / GHS-SEC-01 |
| **LMWS (%)** | 0.43% | $\leq 1.0\%$ | USP <129> / GHS-SEC-01 |
| **Retention Time** | 14.21 min | $14.2 \pm 0.3$ min | N/A |

#### 3.2.S.5.5.2 Reverse Phase HPLC (RP-HPLC) Purity Control (GLUC-2025-09C)
The RP-HPLC control is utilized to ensure the separation efficiency of deamidated and oxidized forms of the glucapeptide.

**Protocol for Purity Control Monitoring:**
1.  **Column:** C18, $2.1 \times 150$ mm, 1.7 $\mu$m.
2.  **Mobile Phase A:** 0.1% TFA in Water.
3.  **Mobile Phase B:** 0.08% TFA in Acetonitrile.
4.  **Gradient:** 25% B to 45% B over 30 minutes.
5.  **Flow Rate:** 0.3 mL/min.

---

### 3.2.S.5.6 Process-Specific Impurity Controls (PSC)

#### 3.2.S.5.6.1 Host Cell Protein (HCP) Control (GLUC-2025-12K)
The HCP control material consists of a clarified lysate from a non-transfected GHS-CHO-001 cell line, intended to serve as a high-concentration positive control for the Sandwich ELISA.

**Calculation for Recovery:**
$$ \% \text{Recovery} = \frac{\text{Measured Concentration} - \text{Endogenous Concentration}}{\text{Spiked Concentration}} \times 100 $$

*   **Target Recovery:** 80% - 120%
*   **Linearity of Dilution:** $R^2 \geq 0.99$

---

### 3.2.S.5.7 Stability and Storage Strategy for Control Materials

Stability is monitored via the "Continuous Control Monitoring Program" (CCMP). All ACMs are stored in USP Type I Borosilicate glass vials with FluroTec® coated stoppers to minimize leachables.

#### Table 3: Stability Monitoring Schedule for GLUC-2025-XXX Series
| Timepoint | Bioassay ($EC_{50}$) | SEC (% HMWS) | RP-HPLC (Purity) | Appearance |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **T=0** | Pass | 2.15% | 98.2% | Clear, Colorless |
| **T=3M** | Pass | 2.18% | 98.1% | Clear, Colorless |
| **T=6M** | Pass | 2.22% | 97.9% | Clear, Colorless |
| **T=12M** | Pass | 2.30% | 97.7% | Clear, Colorless |

---

The preparation and qualification of these materials adhere to:
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures: Text and Methodology.

*   **USP <1034>:** Analysis of Biological Assays.

The Assay Control Materials for Glucogen-XR, specifically the GLUC-2025-XXX series, provide a robust framework for maintaining the analytical lifecycle. By utilizing cell-line specific controls and stress-induced physicochemical standards, Google Health Sciences ensures the highest degree of confidence in the potency and safety profile of Glucogen-XR throughout its shelf-life and clinical application.

# Traceability to International Standards

## WHO International Standards if Available

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS

### 3.2.S.5.1 TRACEABILITY TO INTERNATIONAL STANDARDS
#### SUBSECTION: WHO INTERNATIONAL STANDARDS IF AVAILABLE

---

### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection details the alignment, traceability, and calibration of the **Google Health Sciences (GHS)** Internal Primary Reference Standard (iPRS) and Working Reference Standard (WRS) for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)** against the established World Health Organization (WHO) International Standards (IS). 

As Glucogen-XR is a novel, long-acting GLP-1 receptor agonist produced via recombinant DNA technology in the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line, direct molecular identity with historical standards (such as porcine or bovine glucagon) is not applicable. However, for the assessment of biological potency, receptor binding affinity, and specific immunoreactivity, GHS has established a comprehensive traceability chain to the **WHO International Standard for Glucagon, Human, Recombinant (NIBSC code: 12/168)** and relevant GLP-1 reference materials where applicable for bioassay validation.

The objective of this traceability program is to ensure that the potency units (IU) assigned to Glucogen-XR are consistent with international biological activity definitions, thereby ensuring patient safety and therapeutic efficacy across clinical sites and commercial batches.

---

### 2.0 IDENTIFICATION OF PRIMARY INTERNATIONAL REFERENCE MATERIALS

Google Health Sciences has identified the following International Standards (IS) as the foundational benchmarks for the characterization and potency assignment of Glucogen-XR. These materials are procured from the National Institute for Biological Standards and Control (NIBSC), a WHO Collaborating Center.

#### Table 1: Primary International Reference Standards Utilized
| Standard Name | NIBSC Code | Source/Origin | Assigned Potency/Content | Primary Use Case |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **WHO International Standard for Glucagon (Human, Recombinant)** | 12/168 | E. coli derived | 1.07 mg/ampoule | HPLC Identity; Bioassay Calibration |
| **WHO International Standard for GLP-1 (7-36) Amide** | 08/236 | Synthetic | 1.15 IU/ampoule | Potency Benchmark (cAMP Induction) |
| **1st WHO IS for Insulin-like Growth Factor-1** | 02/254 | Recombinant | N/A (Control) | Specificity testing for cross-reactivity |

---

### 3.0 TRACEABILITY HIERARCHY AND CALIBRATION CHAIN

The traceability of Glucogen-XR follows a tiered hierarchical structure to minimize the consumption of the WHO International Standard while maintaining a direct link to the international unitage.

#### 3.1 The Calibration Pyramid
1.  **Level 1: WHO International Standard (NIBSC 12/168)** – The "Gold Standard" held by NIBSC. Used only for the initial qualification of the GHS Primary Reference Standard.
2.  **Level 2: GHS Internal Primary Reference Standard (iPRS) (Batch: GLUC-2025-PRS-01)** – Extensively characterized against Level 1. This material is stored in the vapor phase of liquid nitrogen (-196°C) at the GHS South San Francisco repository.
3.  **Level 3: GHS Working Reference Standard (WRS) (Batch: GLUC-2025-WRS-01)** – Calibrated against Level 2. Used for routine release and stability testing of Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (DS) and Drug Product (DP).
4.  **Level 4: Routine Control Samples/Calibration Curves** – Derived from Level 3 for daily laboratory use.

---

### 4.0 DETAILED COMPARATIVE CHARACTERIZATION PROTOCOLS

To ensure absolute traceability, GHS conducted a multi-modal bridging study comparing Glucogen-XR (Batch: GLUC-2025-001) against WHO IS 12/168.

#### 4.1 Protocol GHS-RE-00982: Potency Alignment by Cell-Based Bioassay
The potency of Glucogen-XR is defined by its ability to activate the GLP-1 receptor (GLP-1R), resulting in the intracellular accumulation of cyclic Adenosine Monophosphate (cAMP).

**Step-by-Step Procedure:**
1.  **Cell Preparation:** HEK293 cells stably transfected with the human GLP-1 receptor (GHS-HEK-GLP1R) are seeded at $5 \times 10^4$ cells/well in 96-well plates.
2.  **Standard Reconstitution:** One ampoule of WHO IS 12/168 (1.07 mg) is reconstituted in 1.07 mL of assay buffer (HBSS + 0.1% BSA + 0.5 mM IBMX) to achieve a stock concentration of 1 mg/mL.
3.  **Serial Dilution:** 12-point serial dilutions (1:3 ratio) are prepared for both WHO IS and GHS iPRS (GLUC-2025-PRS-01).
4.  **Incubation:** Cells are incubated with the standards for 30 minutes at 37°C.
5.  **Detection:** cAMP levels are measured using a Time-Resolved Fluorescence Resonance Energy Transfer (TR-FRET) kit (Lance® Ultra).
6.  **Data Analysis:** Data is fitted using a 4-Parameter Logistic (4-PL) model.

**Statistical Calculation for Potency Ratio:**
The relative potency ($R$) is calculated as:
$$R = \frac{EC_{50}(\text{WHO IS})}{EC_{50}(\text{GHS iPRS})}$$
Where $EC_{50}$ represents the half-maximal effective concentration.

#### Table 2: Comparative Potency Data (WHO IS vs. GHS iPRS)
| Test Parameter | WHO IS (12/168) | GHS iPRS (GLUC-2025-PRS-01) | Acceptance Criteria | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **$EC_{50}$ (pM)** | $42.5 \pm 3.2$ | $41.8 \pm 2.9$ | Ratio 0.80 - 1.25 | 0.98 (Pass) |
| **Max Signal (RFU)** | $124,500$ | $126,200$ | $\pm 10\%$ Difference | 1.3% (Pass) |
| **Slope Factor** | $1.12$ | $1.15$ | Parallelism $p > 0.05$ | $p=0.42$ (Pass) |

---

### 5.0 ANALYTICAL TRACEABILITY BY HIGH-RESOLUTION MASS SPECTROMETRY (HRMS)

To bridge the chemical identity of Glucogen-XR to the WHO International Standard, intact mass analysis and peptide mapping were performed using an Orbitrap Exploris 480 Mass Spectrometer.

#### 5.1 Protocol GHS-MS-2025-11: Intact Mass Comparison
1.  **Sample Prep:** WHO IS 12/168 and GHS-2025-PRS-01 are desalted using ZipTip C18.
2.  **LC-MS Settings:**
    *   Column: Waters ACQUITY UPLC Protein BEH C4, 300Å.
    *   Mobile Phase A: 0.1% Formic Acid in $H_2O$.
    *   Mobile Phase B: 0.1% Formic Acid in ACN.
3.  **Deconvolution:** Data processed via BioPharma Finder™ software using the Xtract algorithm.

#### Table 3: Mass Spectrometric Identification vs. WHO Standard
| Attribute | WHO IS 12/168 (Expected) | GHS iPRS (Measured) | Delta (Da) | Interpretation |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Monoisotopic Mass** | 3480.52 Da | 3480.53 Da | 0.01 | Direct Identity |
| **De-amidation (%)** | < 2.0% | 1.4% | N/A | High Purity |
| **Oxidation (%)** | < 1.0% | 0.6% | N/A | High Purity |

---

The Working Reference Standard (GLUC-2025-WRS-01) is the material used for the release of commercial batches. Its traceability to the WHO IS is maintained through the iPRS.

#### 6.1 WRS Qualification Batch Record

### 7.0 STORAGE AND STABILITY OF TRACEABLE STANDARDS

To maintain the integrity of the traceability chain, GHS follows ICH Q1A(R2) and ICH Q5C guidelines for the storage of reference materials.

#### 7.1 Stability Program for iPRS (GLUC-2025-PRS-01)
*   **Primary Storage:** Liquid Nitrogen (Vapor Phase) at GHS Facility 3000 Innovation Drive.

*   **Monitoring:** Continuous NIST-traceable temperature monitoring with redundant alarm systems.

| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
