| **GHS WRS** | Semi-Annual | Potency, Purity | 18-JAN-2025 | 18-JUL-2025 |

---

### 8.0 JUSTIFICATION FOR MODIFICATIONS TO WHO PROCEDURES

While Google Health Sciences adheres to the principles of WHO/NIBSC standards, certain modifications were necessary to accommodate the "Extended Release" (XR) properties of Glucogen-XR.

1.  **Extended Incubation in Bioassay:** Unlike the 5-minute incubation typical for native glucagon, Glucogen-XR requires 30 minutes to reach steady-state cAMP levels due to the proprietary glucapeptide extension. This has been validated as a "fit-for-purpose" modification under USP <1033>.
2.  **Dilution Buffers:** To prevent non-specific adsorption of the hydrophobic GLP-1 moiety, 0.1% polysorbate-20 is added to all dilution buffers, a deviation from the standard PBS recommended in NIBSC 12/168 instructions.

---

### 9.0 STATISTICAL ANALYSIS AND UNCERTAINTY

In accordance with ISO 17025 and ICH Q2(R1), GHS has calculated the expanded uncertainty ($U$) for the potency assignment of the Reference Standard.

**The Uncertainty Equation:**
$$u_c = \sqrt{u_{WHO}^2 + u_{rep}^2 + u_{dil}^2 + u_{inst}^2}$$
*   $u_{WHO}$: Uncertainty of the WHO IS (provided by NIBSC = 2.1%)
*   $u_{rep}$: Repeatability (0.8%)
*   $u_{dil}$: Dilution error (0.5%)
*   $u_{inst}$: Instrumental precision (1.2%)

**Calculated Expanded Uncertainty ($k=2$):**
$$U = 2 \times \sqrt{2.1^2 + 0.8^2 + 0.5^2 + 1.2^2} = 5.2\%$$

This indicates that the assigned potency of the GHS iPRS is $1.00 \pm 0.052$ units relative to the WHO International Standard.

---

2.  **USP <1032>:** Design and Development of Biological Assays.
3.  **USP <1034>:** Analysis of Biological Assays.
4.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
5.  **FDA Guidance for Industry (2019):** Development of Therapeutic Protein Biosimilars: Comparative Analytical Assessment and Other Quality-Related Considerations (Applied for bridging principles).

### 11.0 CONCLUSION
The Glucogen-XR reference standard program is fully traceable to the **WHO International Standard for Glucagon (12/168)**. Through a rigorous hierarchy of primary and working standards, Google Health Sciences ensures that every commercial batch of Glucogen-XR (GLUC-2025-XXX) maintains a consistent biological potency that is globally aligned with international pharmaceutical requirements. All characterization data confirm that the internal standards are of high purity, stable, and suitable for their intended regulatory purpose.

## Calibration Hierarchy

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5: REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.1.4: TRACEABILITY TO INTERNATIONAL STANDARDS – CALIBRATION HIERARCHY

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE

This subsection delineates the comprehensive calibration hierarchy and metrological traceability framework established by Google Health Sciences (GHS) for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) program. The traceability of reference materials for Glucogen-XR is designed to comply with **ICH Q6B**, **ICH Q2(R2)**, and **USP <1024>** regarding the characterization and qualification of biological products.

As there is currently no International Standard (IS) established by the World Health Organization (WHO) or the National Institute for Biological Standards and Control (NIBSC) specifically for synthetic/recombinant long-acting GLP-1 receptor agonists of this specific peptide sequence, Google Health Sciences has established a robust internal hierarchy. This hierarchy ensures that all analytical measurements—ranging from potency assays to high-resolution mass spectrometry—are linked to fundamental SI units or internally validated primary reference anchors.

---

#### 2.0 METROLOGICAL TRACEABILITY MAP

The calibration hierarchy for Glucogen-XR follows a tiered pyramid structure to ensure the highest degree of certainty and minimal cumulative bias.

##### 2.1 The Four-Tiered Hierarchy Model

| Tier | Designation | Description | Retention Site |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Tier I** | **Primary Reference Standard (PRS)** | The "Gold Standard" batch, characterized by absolute methods (qNMR, Amino Acid Analysis). | GHS Deep Freeze Vault (-80°C) |
| **Tier II** | **Working Reference Standard (WRS)** | Calibrated directly against the PRS. Used for routine release and stability testing. | QC Laboratory (-20°C) |
| **Tier III** | **Secondary/Control Standards** | Used for specific assay system suitability or trend monitoring. | Local Satellite Labs |
| **Tier IV** | **Instrumental Calibration Standards** | NIST-traceable weights, thermometers, and chemical precursors. | External Metrology |

---

#### 3.0 TIER I: PRIMARY REFERENCE STANDARD (PRS) CALIBRATION PROTOCOL

The Primary Reference Standard (Batch: **GLUC-2025-PRS-001**) serves as the ultimate metrological anchor for the Glucogen-XR program. 

##### 3.1 Traceability to SI Units via Absolute Methods
Because no WHO international standard exists, Tier I traceability is established via **Primary Methodologies** where the results are directly derived from physical constants or SI-traceable chemical properties.

**3.1.1 Quantitative Nuclear Magnetic Resonance (qNMR)**
*   **Traceability:** Linked to NIST SRM 350b (Benzoic Acid) or SRM 192a (Potassium Hydrogen Phthalate).
*   **Calculation for Absolute Purity ($P_{abs}$):**
    $$P_{abs} = \frac{I_{sample}}{I_{std}} \cdot \frac{N_{std}}{N_{sample}} \cdot \frac{M_{sample}}{M_{std}} \cdot \frac{W_{std}}{W_{sample}} \cdot P_{std}$$
    *Where:*
    *   $I$ = Integrated signal area
    *   $N$ = Number of protons
    *   $M$ = Molar mass
    *   $W$ = Weight

**3.1.2 Amino Acid Analysis (AAA)**
*   **Traceability:** Linked to NIST SRM 2389a (Amino Acids in 0.1 mol/L HCl).
*   **Procedure:** 24, 48, and 72-hour acid hydrolysis followed by ion-exchange chromatography with post-column ninhydrin derivatization.

##### 3.2 Tier I Characterization Data (Batch: GLUC-2025-PRS-001)

| Parameter | Method | Traceability Anchor | Result | Confidence Interval (95%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Absolute Peptide Content** | AAA | NIST SRM 2389a | 98.4% (w/w) | ± 0.3% |
| **Molar Mass** | Orbitrap MS | External NIST Calibrant | 4,203.54 Da | ± 0.02 Da |
| **Specific Activity** | In Vitro Bioassay | Internal Bio-Anchor | 1.25 x 10^7 IU/mg | ± 0.15 |
| **Residual Moisture** | Karl Fischer | NIST SRM 2890 | 1.12% (w/w) | ± 0.05% |

---

#### 4.0 TIER II: WORKING REFERENCE STANDARD (WRS) QUALIFICATION

The Working Reference Standard (WRS) is calibrated against the PRS. The current active WRS is **Batch: GLUC-2025-WRS-002**.

##### 4.1 Transfer of Value (PRS to WRS)
The "Value Assignment" process involves a multi-day, multi-analyst campaign to minimize intermediate precision error.

**Protocol GHS-QC-PRO-099: Calibration Transfer**
1.  **Preparation:** Reconstitute 5 vials of PRS and 10 vials of candidate WRS.
2.  **Analysis:** Perform 18 independent HPLC runs (RP-HPLC and SEC-HPLC).
3.  **Statistical Calculation:**
    The assigned potency of the WRS ($Pot_{WRS}$) is calculated as:
    $$Pot_{WRS} = \bar{X}_{obs} \times \frac{Pot_{PRS}}{100}$$
    where $\bar{X}_{obs}$ is the mean relative purity observed during the crossover study.

##### 4.2 Cross-Linkage Table: PRS vs. WRS

| Analysis Date | PRS Batch ID | WRS Candidate ID | Instrument ID | Assigned Purity (%) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 12-JAN-2025 | GLUC-2025-PRS-001 | GLUC-2025-WRS-002 | HPLC-GHS-04 | 98.2 |
| 13-JAN-2025 | GLUC-2025-PRS-001 | GLUC-2025-WRS-002 | HPLC-GHS-09 | 98.3 |
| 14-JAN-2025 | GLUC-2025-PRS-001 | GLUC-2025-WRS-002 | HPLC-GHS-04 | 98.1 |
| **Mean Value** | | | | **98.2%** |

---

#### 5.0 CALIBRATION OF AUXILIARY CRITICAL REAGENTS

Traceability for Glucogen-XR is not limited to the peptide itself but extends to the critical reagents used in the extended-release matrix (Proprietary GHS-Polymer-01).

##### 5.1 Traceability of Molecular Weight Standards
For the GPC/SEC analysis of the extended-release polymer, the following hierarchy is maintained:
1.  **Primary:** NIST SRM 1475a (Linear Polyethylene).
2.  **Secondary:** Narrow-distribution Polystyrene standards (ISO 9001 certified).

---

#### 6.0 PROCEDURAL CONTROLS FOR HIERARCHY MAINTENANCE

To ensure the "Chain of Comparison" is never broken, Google Health Sciences implements the following lifecycle controls:

##### 6.1 Recalibration Schedule (The "Drift" Control)
*   **PRS Re-qualification:** Every 24 months via full characterization.
*   **WRS Re-qualification:** Every 12 months against the PRS.
*   **Instrument Metrology:** Every 6 months (NIST-traceable service).

##### 6.2 Step-by-Step Procedure for Annual Traceability Verification
1.  **Step 1:** Retrieve 3 aliquots of PRS (GLUC-2025-PRS-001) from -80°C.
2.  **Step 2:** Prepare a 5-point calibration curve (0.5 mg/mL to 2.5 mg/mL).
3.  **Step 3:** Perform 6 replicate injections of the current WRS.
4.  **Step 4:** Calculate the **Bias Factor (B)**:
    $$B = \frac{Response_{WRS(Measured)}}{Response_{WRS(Assigned)}}$$
5.  **Step 5:** If $0.98 \le B \le 1.02$, the hierarchy is maintained. If $B$ is outside this range, a Root Cause Analysis (RCA) is triggered per **SOP-GHS-QA-004**.

---

#### 7.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND CITATIONS

The calibration hierarchy described herein adheres to the following regulatory frameworks:

1.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (2015).*
2.  **USP Chapter <1024>:** *Measurement of Viral Antibody Titers.*
3.  **ISO/IEC 17025:2017:** *General requirements for the competence of testing and calibration laboratories.*
4.  **ICH Q2(R2):** *Validation of Analytical Procedures.*

---

#### 8.0 UNCERTAINTY BUDGET ANALYSIS

Each step in the calibration hierarchy introduces a component of uncertainty. The expanded uncertainty ($U$) for the Glucogen-XR traceability chain is calculated using the Root Sum Square (RSS) method.

| Uncertainty Component | Symbol | Value (Rel %) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| Weighing (NIST Traceable) | $u_{weight}$ | 0.02% |
| Volumetric Dilution | $u_{vol}$ | 0.05% |
| PRS Value Assignment | $u_{PRS}$ | 0.30% |
| Intermediate Precision (WRS) | $u_{ip}$ | 0.45% |
| **Combined Standard Uncertainty** | $u_c$ | **0.54%** |
| **Expanded Uncertainty (k=2)** | $U$ | **1.08%** |

*Conclusion: The Glucogen-XR calibration hierarchy ensures that the final reported value of any clinical batch is accurate within an expanded uncertainty of ±1.08% relative to the Primary Reference Standard.*

## Uncertainty Analysis

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5: REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.3: TRACEABILITY TO INTERNATIONAL STANDARDS
#### 3.2.S.5.3.1: UNCERTAINTY ANALYSIS

---

### 1.0 Executive Summary of Uncertainty Framework
Google Health Sciences (GHS) has implemented a comprehensive metrological traceability and uncertainty quantification framework for **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**. In accordance with **ICH Q6B**, **ICH Q2(R2)**, and **ISO/IEC 17025:2017**, this section details the rigorous statistical derivation of the "Combined Standard Uncertainty" ($u_c$) and the "Expanded Uncertainty" ($U$) associated with the Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standard (WRS).

The uncertainty analysis for Glucogen-XR is not merely a statement of precision but a complete budget of all potential error sources throughout the value chain—from the international SI unit (via NIST-traceable materials) to the final released batch (e.g., **Batch GLUC-2025-001**).

---

### 2.0 Metrological Hierarchy and Traceability Chain
The traceability of Glucogen-XR is established through a multi-tier hierarchy. Each tier introduces a component of uncertainty which is mathematically aggregated.

| Tier | Material Level | Identification | Traceability Source |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Tier 1** | SI Units / Primary Calibrants | NIST SRM 927f (Bovine Serum Albumin) | NIST / BIPM |
| **Tier 2** | Secondary Reference Standard | USP Glucagon RS (Lot L12345) | United States Pharmacopeia |
| **Tier 3** | GHS Primary Reference Standard | **GLUC-2025-PRS-01** | Internal Characterization |
| **Tier 4** | GHS Working Reference Standard | **GLUC-2025-WRS-01** | Characterization vs. PRS |
| **Tier 5** | Clinical/Commercial Batches | **GLUC-2025-XXX** | Potency/Purity vs. WRS |

---

### 3.0 Mathematical Model for Uncertainty Quantification
The uncertainty of the assigned value ($x_{RS}$) for Glucogen-XR is calculated using the GUM (Guide to the Expression of Uncertainty in Measurement) methodology.

#### 3.1 The Fundamental Equation
The combined uncertainty ($u_c$) is defined as the square root of the sum of the squares of individual uncertainty components:

$$u_c = \sqrt{u_{char}^2 + u_{bb}^2 + u_{lts}^2 + u_{sts}^2}$$

Where:
*   **$u_{char}$**: Uncertainty derived from the primary characterization (Assay/Purity).
*   **$u_{bb}$**: Uncertainty due to between-bottle (inter-vial) heterogeneity.
*   **$u_{lts}$**: Uncertainty from long-term stability studies.
*   **$u_{sts}$**: Uncertainty from short-term (transportation) stability.

#### 3.2 Coverage Factor ($k$)
To provide a 95% confidence interval, the expanded uncertainty ($U$) is calculated:
$$U = k \cdot u_c$$
For Glucogen-XR, $k = 2.0$, assuming a normal distribution of values.

---

### 4.0 Detailed Component Analysis for Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01

#### 4.1 $u_{char}$ - Uncertainty in Characterization
The characterization of Glucogen-XR involves orthogonal techniques: RP-HPLC (Purity), SEC-HPLC (Aggregation), and Bioassay (Potency).

##### Table 4.1.1: Characterization Data for PRS-01
| Parameter | Method ID | Mean Value | SD ($n=12$) | RSD (%) | $u_{char}$ (unit) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Purity (RP-HPLC)** | GHS-AN-RP-001 | 99.45% | 0.042 | 0.042 | 0.0121 |
| **Assay (Mass)** | GHS-AN-UV-005 | 1.02 mg/mL | 0.008 | 0.78 | 0.0023 |
| **Potency (In-Vitro)**| GHS-BIO-012 | 104.2% | 3.15 | 3.02 | 0.909 |

**Calculation Example (Purity):**
The $u_{char}$ for purity is derived from the standard error of the mean:
$$u_{char} = \frac{SD}{\sqrt{n}} = \frac{0.042}{\sqrt{12}} = 0.0121$$

#### 4.2 $u_{bb}$ - Between-Bottle Heterogeneity
To ensure the reference standard is uniform across the entire fill (500 vials), GHS performed a stratified sampling plan. Ten (10) vials were selected across the fill sequence (start, middle, end) for **Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01**.

##### Table 4.2.1: Heterogeneity Testing Results
| Vial ID | Fill Position | Assay (mg/vial) | Deviation from Mean |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| PRS-01-001 | Start | 5.01 | -0.01 |
| PRS-01-050 | Start | 5.02 | 0.00 |
| PRS-01-125 | Middle | 5.03 | +0.01 |
| PRS-01-250 | Middle | 5.02 | 0.00 |
| PRS-01-375 | Middle | 5.01 | -0.01 |
| PRS-01-500 | End | 5.03 | +0.01 |

**ANOVA Analysis for $u_{bb}$:**
Using ANOVA, the variance within-bottle ($s_w$) and between-bottle ($s_{bb}$) is calculated.
If $MS_{between} < MS_{within}$, the $u_{bb}$ is calculated using the formula:
$$u_{bb} = \sqrt{\frac{MS_{between} - MS_{within}}{n}} \cdot \text{Correction Factor}$$
For Batch GLUC-2025-PRS-01, the calculated **$u_{bb} = 0.0045$**.

#### 4.3 $u_{lts}$ - Long-Term Stability Uncertainty
Stability uncertainty is derived from the slope of the stability curve at the recommended storage temperature (-80°C).

**Protocol for $u_{lts}$:**
1.  Analyze data points over 24 months.
2.  Calculate the standard error of the slope ($s_b$).
3.  Calculate $u_{lts} = s_b \times \text{Shelf-life (t)}$.

| Timepoint | Result (Purity %) | Condition |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| T=0 | 99.45 | -80°C |
| T=6M | 99.42 | -80°C |
| T=12M | 99.46 | -80°C |
| T=24M | 99.38 | -80°C |

**Calculated $u_{lts} = 0.024$** (based on 24-month regression analysis).

---

### 5.0 Step-by-Step Uncertainty Calculation Protocol (SOP-GHS-QA-550)

To ensure consistency across the Google Health Sciences network, the following protocol is applied to all **Glucogen-XR** reference materials:

1.  **Selection of Measurand:** Define the property (e.g., protein concentration by UV-Vis A280).
2.  **Identification of Error Sources:** Map the process using a Fishbone (Ishikawa) diagram (Pipetting, Temperature, Instrument Calibration, Analyst, Extinction Coefficient).
3.  **Quantification of Type A Uncertainties:** Derived from statistical analysis of series of observations (Standard Deviation of the Mean).
4.  **Quantification of Type B Uncertainties:** Derived from external sources:
    *   *Pipette Calibration Certificate:* $u_{pipette} = \frac{\text{Uncertainty on Cert}}{\text{Coverage Factor}}$.
    *   *Balance Calibration:* $u_{bal} = 0.0001$ mg.
    *   *Molecular Weight Accuracy:* $u_{MW} = 0.002$ Da.
5.  **Conversion to Relative Standard Uncertainty ($w_i$):**
    $$w_i = \frac{u_i}{x_i}$$
6.  **Combining Uncertainties:** Sum the squares of relative uncertainties.
7.  **Expansion:** Multiply by $k=2$.

---

### 6.0 Comparative Uncertainty: PRS vs. WRS (Batch GLUC-2025-WRS-01)

The Working Reference Standard (WRS) inherently contains higher uncertainty because it is calibrated *against* the PRS.

| Component | PRS-01 Uncertainty | WRS-01 Uncertainty |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Characterization** | 0.0121 | 0.0185 (includes PRS error) |
| **Heterogeneity** | 0.0045 | 0.0062 |
| **Stability** | 0.0240 | 0.0280 |
| **Combined ($u_c$)** | **0.0272** | **0.0341** |
| **Expanded ($U, k=2$)** | **0.0544** | **0.0682** |

---

### 7.0 Statistical Impact on Product Specifications
The uncertainty in the Reference Standard directly impacts the "Guard-banding" of clinical release specifications for Glucogen-XR.

#### 7.1 Calculation of Decision Rules
Following **ASME B89.7.3.1**, GHS applies a guard-band to ensure that the probability of a false acceptance (PFA) is $<0.1\%$.
$$\text{Acceptance Limit} = \text{Specification Limit} - U$$

For Assay (95.0% - 105.0%):
*   Lower Acceptance Limit = $95.0 + 0.068 = 95.07\%$
*   Upper Acceptance Limit = $105.0 - 0.068 = 104.93\%$

This ensures that even with the maximum estimated uncertainty in the **GLUC-2025-WRS-01**, the patient receives a dose within the therapeutic window.

---

**Batch Number:** GLUC-2025-WRS-01
**Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences
**Storage:** -80°C ± 5°C
**Assigned Purity:** 99.41%
**Expanded Uncertainty ($k=2$):** ± 0.07%

**Traceability Statement:**

# Documentation and Certificates

## Standard Operating Procedures

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION: STANDARD OPERATING PROCEDURES (SOP) FOR DOCUMENTATION AND CERTIFICATES

**Document ID:** GHS-GLUC-SOP-RS-009  
**Version:** 4.2.0  
**Effective Date:** 15-OCT-2024  
**Supersedes:** 3.1.0 (12-JAN-2023)  
**Author:** Quality Regulatory Affairs Department, Google Health Sciences  
**Manufacturing Site:** 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080, USA  

---

#### 1.0 PURPOSE AND SCOPE

This Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) defines the mandatory requirements for the generation, management, archival, and lifecycle control of Documentation and Certificates of Analysis (CoA) for the Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) reference standards. 

This SOP applies to all Reference Standard tiers, including:
1.  **Primary Reference Standard (PRS):** Derived from Batch GLUC-2025-001 (Characterized by orthogonal analytical methods against international standards).
2.  **Working Reference Standard (WRS):** Derived from subsequent clinical or commercial scale batches (e.g., GLUC-2025-014, GLUC-2025-088).
3.  **Impurity Reference Standards:** Isolated or synthesized degradation products and process-related impurities.

The objective is to ensure full compliance with **21 CFR Part 211.165**, **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products), and **ICH Q7** (Good Manufacturing Practice Guidance for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients).

---

#### 2.0 REGULATORY HIERARCHY AND COMPLIANCE FRAMEWORK

All documentation generated under this SOP must adhere to the following regulatory benchmarks:

*   **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures.
*   **ICH Q5C:** Stability Testing of Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **USP <11>:** Reference Standards.
*   **USP <1029>:** Good Documentation Guidelines.
*   **21 CFR Part 11:** Electronic Records; Electronic Signatures (specifically regarding the Google Cloud Life Sciences Electronic Quality Management System - EQMS).

---

#### 3.0 PROCEDURE FOR THE GENERATION OF THE CERTIFICATE OF ANALYSIS (CoA)

The CoA is the definitive document certifying the quality, identity, purity, and potency of the Glucogen-XR Reference Standard.

##### 3.1 Data Aggregation and Verification Protocol
Prior to CoA generation, the Quality Control (QC) Lead must compile the "Reference Standard Characterization Package" (RSCP). This package consists of raw data from the following instruments integrated into the Google Cloud Life Sciences Data Lake:

1.  **Mass Spectrometry (ESI-Q-TOF):** Intact mass and peptide mapping (LC-MS/MS).
2.  **Chromatography (UPLC-SEC/RP-HPLC):** Purity and related substances.
3.  **Capillary Electrophoresis (cIEF/CE-SDS):** Charge heterogeneity and purity.
4.  **Bioassay:** Potency (GLP-1 Receptor Activation via cAMP response element).

##### 3.2 Step-by-Step Procedure for CoA Issuance

1.  **Initiation:** Trigger a "Document Request" in the EQMS using Workflow ID `GHS-WF-RS-COA`.
2.  **Batch Identification:** Enter the specific Batch ID (e.g., **GLUC-2025-RS05**).
3.  **Attribute Mapping:** Map the analytical results against the pre-defined Specification Limits (Refer to Section 5.0, Table 2).
4.  **Statistical Integration:** For PRS qualification, calculate the Mean and Relative Standard Deviation (RSD) from $n=12$ independent replicates across three different analysts.
5.  **Calculations for Potency (Standardization):**
    Use the following formula for assigning potency to a WRS relative to the PRS:
    $$P_{WRS} = \frac{\sum_{i=1}^{n} (Activity_{i} / Weight_{i})}{P_{PRS\_Constant}}$$
    *Where $P$ is Potency in International Units (IU) per mg.*
6.  **Approval Workflow:**
    *   *Analyst:* Uploads raw data/chromatograms.
    *   *QC Manager:* Reviews for technical accuracy.
    *   *QA Regulatory:* Final signature and seal.

---

#### 4.0 DOCUMENTATION STRUCTURE: THE REFERENCE STANDARD DOSSIER

Every batch of Glucogen-XR Reference Standard must have a physical and electronic dossier containing the following documents:

| Document Code | Document Title | Description |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GHS-RSD-01** | Certificate of Analysis (CoA) | Final certified results and shelf-life. |
| **GHS-RSD-02** | Characterization Report | Full structural elucidation (NMR, MS/MS, CD). |
| **GHS-RSD-03** | Stability Summary Report | Real-time stability data at $-80^\circ C$ and $-20^\circ C$. |
| **GHS-RSD-04** | Vial Log & Chain of Custody | Track of movement from Vault to QC Labs. |
| **GHS-RSD-05** | Recertification Protocol | Schedule for next qualification event. |

---

#### 5.0 TECHNICAL SPECIFICATIONS AND ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA (TABLE 2)

The following table outlines the mandatory fields and acceptance criteria for the Glucogen-XR Working Reference Standard (Batch Category: GLUC-2025-XXX).

**Table 2: Glucogen-XR WRS Specification Framework**

| Test Parameter | Method ID | Acceptance Criteria | Example Result (Batch GLUC-2025-022) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Appearance** | GHS-VIS-01 | White to off-white lyophilized cake | Conforms |
| **Identity (Mass Spec)** | GHS-MS-04 | $4242.5 \pm 0.5$ Da | 4242.48 Da |
| **Purity (RP-UPLC)** | GHS-HPLC-02 | $\ge 98.5\%$ | 99.42% |
| **Total Impurities** | GHS-HPLC-02 | $\le 1.5\%$ | 0.58% |
| **Deamidated Forms** | GHS-cIEF-09 | $\le 2.0\%$ | 0.8% |
| **Potency (In-Vitro)** | GHS-BIO-01 | 90% - 110% of PRS | 102.5% |
| **Water Content** | GHS-KF-03 | $\le 3.0\% w/w$ | 1.45% |
| **Bacterial Endotoxins** | GHS-LAL-01 | $\le 5$ EU/mg | < 0.1 EU/mg |

---

#### 6.0 RECERTIFICATION AND LIFECYCLE MANAGEMENT PROTOCOL

Glucogen-XR is a peptide therapeutic sensitive to oxidative degradation and deamidation. Therefore, the Reference Standard documentation must be updated via a "Rolling Qualification" system.

##### 6.1 Recertification Frequency
*   **Primary Reference Standard:** Every 24 months.
*   **Working Reference Standard:** Every 12 months.

##### 6.2 Procedure for Extension of Expiry
1.  **Sampling:** Withdraw 5 vials of Batch **GLUC-2025-XXX** from the GHS Biovault ($T = -80^\circ C$).
2.  **Analysis:** Perform "Abbreviated Stability Testing" focusing on Purity (RP-UPLC) and Bioassay.
3.  **Statistical Comparison:** Apply a Student’s t-test ($p < 0.05$) to compare the current purity against the Time-Zero ($T_0$) data.
4.  **Documentation Update:** If results are within 0.5% of $T_0$, issue an **Amendment to the CoA** extending the "Retest Date" by 12 months.

---

#### 7.0 STORAGE AND LOGISTICAL DOCUMENTATION

Reference standards are stored in the Google Health Sciences "Deep-Freeze" (Equipment ID: GHS-FRZ-9902).

**Protocol for Inventory Log (SOP-RS-LOG):**
*   **Entry 1:** Date of Deposition.
*   **Entry 2:** Inventory Count (Vial Level).
*   **Entry 3:** NIST-Traceable Temperature Log (Continuous monitoring via Google Cloud IoT Core).
*   **Entry 4:** Deviation Flags (Any excursion above $-60^\circ C$ for $>30$ minutes requires a formal Quality Investigation Report - QIR).

---

#### 8.0 ARCHIVAL AND RETENTION

1.  **Retention Period:** Documentation must be retained for **15 years** after the discontinuation of the Glucogen-XR product line, or as per local regulatory requirements.
2.  **Electronic Backup:** All CoAs are cryptographically signed and mirrored across three Google Cloud regions (us-central1, us-east1, and europe-west1) to ensure "Five Nines" (99.999%) availability and data integrity as per **ALCOA+** principles.

---

#### 9.0 APPENDICES AND FORMS

*   **Form RS-001A:** Template for Primary Reference Standard CoA.
*   **Form RS-001B:** Template for Working Reference Standard CoA.
*   **Form RS-LOG:** Daily Temperature and Access Log.

---
**END OF DOCUMENT**  
*Confidential - Property of Google Health Sciences*

## Certificate of Analysis Format

### **3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS**
#### **3.2.S.5.3 Documentation and Certificates**
##### **3.2.S.5.3.1 Certificate of Analysis (CoA) Format and Data Hierarchy**

---

#### **1. SCOPE AND PURPOSE**
This subsection delineates the standardized format, structural hierarchy, and data integrity requirements for the Certificate of Analysis (CoA) pertaining to Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) reference standards. As Glucogen-XR is a recombinant GLP-1 receptor agonist fusion protein produced via the proprietary GHS-CHO-001 cell line, the CoA must encompass multifaceted analytical characterization spanning primary structure, post-translational modifications (PTMs), higher-order structure (HOS), and biological potency.

All CoAs generated by Google Health Sciences (GHS) comply with **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **21 CFR Part 11** (Electronic Records; Electronic Signatures).

---

#### **2. ARCHITECTURAL HIERARCHY OF THE COA**
The CoA for Glucogen-XR Reference Standards (Primary, Working, and Interim) is divided into twelve distinct modules. This ensures that regulatory reviewers from the FDA Office of Biotechnology Products (OBP) can navigate complex mass spectrometry and bioassay data with maximum transparency.

| Module | Section Title | Content Description |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **I** | **Administrative Metadata** | Manufacturer details, Batch ID (GLUC-2025-XXX), Date of Manufacture. |
| **II** | **Product Identification** | INN Name, IUPAC chemical name, Molecular Formula, Theoretical Mass. |
| **III** | **Physical Description** | State, color, pH of reconstituted solution, container closure system. |
| **IV** | **Identity Confirmation** | N-terminal sequencing, Peptide Mapping (LC-MS/MS), Intact Mass. |
| **V** | **Purity - Process Related** | Host Cell Protein (HCP), Host Cell DNA (hcDNA), Protein A leachates. |
| **VI** | **Purity - Product Related** | SE-HPLC (Aggregates), CEX-HPLC (Charge variants), HIC (Hydrophobicity). |
| **VII** | **Potency / Biological Activity** | In vitro GLP-1 Receptor Activation (cAMP), Binding Affinity (SPR). |
| **VIII** | **Quantity and Concentration** | UV280 extinction coefficient analysis, Amino Acid Analysis (AAA). |
| **IX** | **Glycan Characterization** | Sialic acid content, N-linked glycan profiling (HILIC-FLD). |
| **X** | **Compendial Requirements** | USP <788> Sub-visible particles, USP <85> Endotoxin, USP <71> Sterility. |
| **XI** | **Stability Data Summary** | Cumulative stability duration, storage conditions (-80°C). |
| **XII** | **Authorization** | Quality Control (QC) and Quality Assurance (QA) signatures. |

---

#### **3. DETAILED TECHNICAL SPECIFICATIONS & TABLE FORMATS**

##### **3.1 Administrative Metadata Section (Module I)**
The header of every CoA for Glucogen-XR must include the Google Cloud Life Sciences cryptographic digital signature and the following tracking parameters:

*   **Manufacturer:** Google Health Sciences, 3000 Innovation Drive, South San Francisco, CA 94080.
*   **Batch Number Format:** `GLUC-2025-[YYY]` (where YYY is a sequential three-digit code).
*   **Standard Type:** [Primary Reference Standard / Working Reference Standard].
*   **Retest Date:** Set at 24 months from the date of qualification based on real-time stability (Section 3.2.S.5.4).

##### **3.2 Primary Structural Characterization and Identity (Module IV)**
Identity is confirmed using an orthogonal approach. The following table represents the standard CoA reporting format for Identity:

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-1: Identity Test Requirements for GLUC-2025-001 (Primary RS)**

| Test Method | Procedure ID | Specification / Acceptance Criteria | Observed Result (Batch GLUC-2025-001) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Intact Mass (ESI-TOF MS)** | SOP-GHS-MS-012 | 68,452.12 Da ± 2.0 Da (Deconvoluted) | 68,452.18 Da |
| **Reduced Peptide Mapping** | SOP-GHS-MS-015 | >98% Sequence Coverage; Matches Reference Map | 100% Coverage; Conforms |
| **N-Terminal Sequencing** | SOP-GHS-SQ-002 | Confirms: H-G-E-G-T-F-T-S-D-V... | Confirms Sequence |
| **C-Terminal Sequencing** | SOP-GHS-SQ-003 | Confirms: ...G-G-S-S-G-A-P-P-P-S | Confirms Sequence |
| **Isoelectric Point (icIEF)** | SOP-GHS-CE-088 | pI Range: 4.85 - 5.15 | 4.98 |

---

##### **3.3 Detailed Purity and Heterogeneity Metrics (Modules V & VI)**
Due to the extended-release nature of Glucogen-XR, control of aggregates (dimers/multimers) and charge variants (deamidation/oxidation) is critical for PK/PD consistency.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-2: Product-Related Impurities (Detailed Quantitative Format)**

| Analytical Parameter | Specification Limit | Result (GLUC-2025-001) | Statistical Confidence (95% CI) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Monomer Content (SE-HPLC)** | ≥ 99.0% | 99.78% | ± 0.04% |
| **High Molecular Weight (HMW)** | ≤ 0.5% | 0.12% | ± 0.01% |
| **Low Molecular Weight (LMW)** | ≤ 0.5% | 0.10% | ± 0.01% |
| **Main Peak (CEX-HPLC)** | 65.0% - 75.0% | 71.22% | ± 0.35% |
| **Acidic Variants (Deamidation)** | ≤ 25.0% | 19.45% | ± 0.22% |
| **Basic Variants (C-term Lys)** | ≤ 10.0% | 9.33% | ± 0.18% |

---

#### **4. STEP-BY-STEP CALCULATION PROTOCOLS FOR COA VALUES**

To ensure reproducibility across Google Cloud Life Sciences nodes, the CoA must document the specific formulas used for purity and potency calculations.

##### **4.1 Potency Calculation (GLP-1 Receptor Activation)**
The biological activity of Glucogen-XR is determined via a cell-based cAMP reporter gene assay using the HEK-293 cell line overexpressing the human GLP-1 receptor.

**Formula for Relative Potency (RP):**
$$RP = \frac{EC_{50} (\text{Standard})}{EC_{50} (\text{Test})} \times 100\%$$

**Protocol for Potency Determination:**
1.  **Preparation:** Dilute GLUC-2025-XXX to a starting concentration of 100 nM in Assay Buffer (DMEM/F12).
2.  **Serial Dilution:** Perform an 11-point, 1:3 serial dilution.
3.  **Incubation:** Incubate cells with the peptide for 4 hours at 37°C, 5% $CO_2$.
4.  **Detection:** Add Lysis/Detection buffer and measure luminescence using a microplate reader (ID: GHS-PL-99).
5.  **Statistical Analysis:** Fit data to a 4-parameter logistic (4-PL) model. Parallelism must be confirmed ($\chi^2 < 0.05$) before RP calculation.

---

##### **4.2 Glycan Molar Ratio Calculation**
Sialylation is a Critical Quality Attribute (CQA) for Glucogen-XR as it dictates the serum half-life.

**Molar Ratio Calculation (moles sialic acid / mole protein):**
$$M_{sialic} = \frac{C_{sialic} \times V}{MW_{sialic} \times n_{protein}}$$

Where:
*   $C_{sialic}$ = Concentration determined by HPAEC-PAD.
*   $MW_{sialic}$ = 309.3 g/mol.
*   $n_{protein}$ = Moles of Glucogen-XR based on AAA.

**Acceptance Criteria for Reference Standard:**
*   **Total Sialylation:** 6.0 - 8.5 mol/mol.
*   **Galactosylation (G0/G1/G2 ratio):** Reported for information (RFI).

---

#### **5. PROCESS-RELATED IMPURITIES (EXTENSIVE QUANTITATION)**

The reference standard serves as the "Gold Standard" for impurity benchmarking. Google Health Sciences utilizes high-sensitivity Google-engineered ELISA platforms for these measurements.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-3: Process-Related Impurities for Reference Standard Qualification**

| Contaminant | Method | LOD / LOQ | Result (Batch GLUC-2025-001) |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Host Cell Protein (HCP)** | GHS-Proprietary ELISA | 0.5 ppm / 1.5 ppm | 2.2 ppm |
| **Host Cell DNA (hcDNA)** | qPCR (Alu-like sequences) | 1 pg/mg | < 1 pg/mg |
| **Protein A Leachate** | ELISA | 0.1 ng/mg | 0.32 ng/mg |
| **Residual Solvents** | GC-FID (USP <467>) | Class 2 & 3 Limits | Not Detected |
| **Heavy Metals** | ICP-MS (USP <232>) | PPB Levels | Complies |

---

#### **6. COMPENDIAL AND MICROBIOLOGICAL ATTRIBUTES**

To ensure the safety and stability of the reference material during long-term storage and global distribution via Google Cloud Logistics, the following USP/EP tests are integrated into the CoA:

1.  **Bacterial Endotoxins (USP <85>):** Measured using the Limulus Amebocyte Lysate (LAL) Kinetic Chromogenic Method.
    *   *Limit:* $\leq 5.0$ EU/mg.
2.  **Particulate Matter (USP <788>):** Light Obscuration Method.
    *   *Limit:* $\geq 10 \mu m: \leq 6000$/container; $\geq 25 \mu m: \leq 600$/container.
3.  **Sterility (USP <71>):** Membrane Filtration Method.
    *   *Limit:* No growth after 14 days.

---

#### **7. DATA INTEGRITY AND CLOUD TRACEABILITY**

Each CoA generated for Glucogen-XR includes a **Blockchain-Verified QR Code**. Scanning this code links the reviewer directly to the raw analytical data stored on the Google Cloud Healthcare API (Protected Health Information/PHI-compliant layer).

*   **Audit Trail ID:** GHS-AUDIT-2025-99812-B
*   **Electronic Signature Hash:** SHA-256 (e7f1...a92d)
*   **Reviewer:** Senior Director, Regulatory CMC (Experience: 30+ years)

---

#### **8. REFERENCES (REGULATORY AND SCIENTIFIC)**

1.  **ICH Q6B:** Specifications for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
2.  **ICH Q2(R1):** Validation of Analytical Procedures: Text and Methodology.
3.  **USP <1225>:** Validation of Compendial Procedures.
4.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** "Characterization and Qualification of Cell Substrates and Biological Materials Used in the Production of Viral Vaccines and Biologics."

## Archive Samples

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (CHEMISTRY, MANUFACTURING, AND CONTROLS)
## SECTION 3.2.S.5: REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS
### SUBSECTION 3.2.S.5.3: ARCHIVE SAMPLES AND RETENTION PROTOCOLS

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.1 Introduction and Scope
The establishment of a robust archive sample system for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) reference standards is fundamental to the Google Health Sciences (GHS) Quality Management System (QMS). This subsection delineates the policies, procedures, and technical specifications for the retention of primary, secondary, and working reference standards.

The primary objective of the Archive Sample Program (ASP) is to ensure that a continuous, verifiable, and analytically stable history of the drug substance reference material is maintained throughout the product lifecycle. This program complies with 21 CFR §211.170 (Retention of Samples) and ICH Q7 (Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients).

#### 3.2.S.5.3.2 Regulatory Compliance Framework
The Archive Sample strategy for Glucogen-XR is designed to meet or exceed the following regulatory benchmarks:
*   **USP <1029>:** Good Documentation Guidelines for Reference Materials.
*   **ICH Q1A(R2):** Stability Testing of New Drug Substances and Products.
*   **ICH Q6B:** Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products.
*   **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics.*

#### 3.2.S.5.3.3 Archive Sample Inventory Matrix
The following table provides the comprehensive inventory of current and historical archive samples for Glucogen-XR Drug Substance (DS) reference standards.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-1: Reference Standard Archive Inventory (Batch Series GLUC-2025)**

| Archive ID | Reference Material Type | Parent Batch Number | Quantity Retained | Container Closure System | Storage Temp | Purpose |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **ARC-GLUC-001** | Primary Reference | GLUC-2025-001 | 500 x 2.0 mL | Cryovial, Type I Borosilicate | -70°C ± 10°C | Bridging Studies |
| **ARC-GLUC-002** | Secondary Reference | GLUC-2025-004 | 1,200 x 2.0 mL | Cryovial, Type I Borosilicate | -70°C ± 10°C | Routine Release |
| **ARC-GLUC-003** | Working Standard | GLUC-2025-012 | 2,500 x 1.0 mL | Polypropylene Vented Cap | -20°C ± 5°C | In-process Control |
| **ARC-GLUC-004** | Qualification Standard | GLUC-2025-018 | 300 x 2.0 mL | Cryovial, Type I Borosilicate | -70°C ± 10°C | Method Transfer |
| **ARC-GLUC-005** | Stability Standard | GLUC-2025-022 | 800 x 2.0 mL | Cryovial, Type I Borosilicate | -70°C ± 10°C | Forced Degradation |

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.4 Detailed Protocol for Archive Sample Management

##### 3.2.S.5.3.4.1 Sample Selection and Aliquoting Procedure
The selection of archive samples for Glucogen-XR follows a randomized, statistically significant sampling plan (ISO 2859-1).

1.  **Selection Criteria:** Archive samples must be drawn from a batch that has passed all release specifications (Table 3.2.S.1.3).
2.  **Environmental Controls:** Aliquoting is performed under Grade A (ISO 5) laminar flow conditions within the GHS South San Francisco facility (Room 402-B).
3.  **Aliquoting Volume Calculation:**
    *   $V_{total} = (N_{years} \times n_{tests}) + S_{reserve}$
    *   Where $N_{years} = 15$ (Retention period)
    *   $n_{tests} = 3$ (Number of full monographs per year)
    *   $S_{reserve} = 25\%$ safety margin.
4.  **Labeling Requirements:** Labels must be cryogenic-stable and include:
    *   Drug Name: Glucogen-XR
    *   Archive ID: ARC-GLUC-XXX
    *   Batch No: GLUC-2025-XXX
    *   Storage: -70°C
    *   Expiry: [Date]

##### 3.2.S.5.3.4.2 Storage Conditions and Monitoring
Archive samples are stored in specialized ultra-low temperature (ULT) freezers (Equipment ID: GHS-ULT-9942 and GHS-ULT-9943).

*   **Temperature Set Point:** -70°C.
*   **Operational Range:** -60°C to -80°C.
*   **Monitoring System:** Google Cloud Life Sciences Remote Telemetry (GCLSRT) providing 24/7 real-time monitoring with SMS/Email alerts for deviations exceeding 5 minutes.
*   **Back-up Power:** Redundant Liquid Nitrogen (LN2) backup systems capable of maintaining temperature for 72 hours in the event of total power failure.

##### 3.2.S.5.3.4.3 Periodic Re-qualification Schedule
To ensure the integrity of the archive samples, a rolling re-qualification program is implemented.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-2: Re-qualification Testing Matrix for Archive Samples**

| Test Parameter | Methodology | Frequency | Acceptance Criteria |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Identity (RT)** | RP-HPLC (GHS-METH-042) | Annual | Matches Reference Chromatogram |
| **Purity (SEC)** | SE-HPLC (GHS-METH-055) | Bi-annual | $\geq 98.5\%$ Monomer |
| **Potency (Bioassay)** | cAMP Induction (GHS-BIO-001) | Annual | 80% - 120% of Target |
| **Aggregate Content** | DLS (GHS-METH-089) | Every 3 Years | < 0.5% High Molecular Weight |
| **Deamidation** | LC-MS/MS (GHS-METH-112) | Annual | Report Result (% Change < 1%) |

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.5 Statistical Analysis of Archive Stability
Google Health Sciences utilizes a Bayesian stability model to predict the shelf-life of the archive samples based on real-time data from the GLUC-2025 series.

The degradation rate ($k$) is calculated using the Arrhenius Equation:
$$k = A \cdot e^{\frac{-E_a}{RT}}$$
Where:
*   $A$ = Pre-exponential factor
*   $E_a$ = Activation energy for glucapeptide degradation (determined as 84.3 kJ/mol)
*   $R$ = Gas constant (8.314 J/mol·K)
*   $T$ = Storage temperature in Kelvin (203.15 K)

Calculations indicate that at -70°C, the chemical stability of Glucogen-XR exceeds 25 years with less than 0.1% degradation in primary sequence integrity.

#### 3.2.S.5.3.6 Chain of Custody and Access Control
Access to the Reference Standard Archive is strictly restricted to authorized Quality Control (QC) personnel.

1.  **Biometric Access:** Entry to the storage vault requires multi-factor authentication (MFA) via Google Titan Security Keys and biometric retinal scans.
2.  **Electronic Logbook:** Every sample withdrawal is recorded in the GHS-LIMS (Laboratory Information Management System).
3.  **Audit Trail:** The system generates an immutable audit trail (compliant with 21 CFR Part 11) for every interaction with the archive.

**Table 3.2.S.5.3-3: Example Withdrawal Log (Audit Trail Fragment)**

| Transaction Date | Sample ID | Quantity | Authorized Personnel | Reason for Withdrawal |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 2025-JAN-14 | ARC-GLUC-001-V042 | 1 Vial | Dr. S. Pichai | Annual Re-qualification |
| 2025-FEB-02 | ARC-GLUC-002-V112 | 2 Vials | J. Doe, Senior QC | Method Validation Study |
| 2025-MAR-12 | ARC-GLUC-001-V043 | 1 Vial | A. Zhang, QA | Investigator Site Inspection |

---

#### 3.2.S.5.3.7 Protocol for Disposition of Expired Archive Samples
Archive samples that reach the end of their designated retention period (typically 1 year after the expiration of the last commercial batch associated with the standard) undergo a formal decommissioning process.

1.  **Final Assessment:** A "Terminal Stability Test" is performed to gather longitudinal data.
2.  **Documentation:** A Disposition Report (Form GHS-QC-DR-88) is generated.
3.  **Destruction:** Samples are incinerated as Biohazardous Level 2 waste in accordance with EPA regulations.
4.  **Archiving of Records:** All analytical data and certificates of analysis (CoAs) are moved to permanent digital storage in the Google Cloud Life Sciences Archive (Region: us-central1).

#### 3.2.S.5.3.8 Handling of Deviations and OOS Results
In the event that an archive sample fails a re-qualification test (Out-of-Specification - OOS):
*   **Phase I Investigation:** Immediate check of storage temperature logs and equipment calibration (GHS-SOP-QC-009).
*   **Phase II Investigation:** Assessment of the entire GLUC-2025 batch series to determine if the instability is inherent to the batch or isolated to the archive storage vial.
*   **Impact Assessment:** Determine if commercial products released using this standard are compromised.

#### 3.2.S.5.3.9 References
1.  *US Food and Drug Administration.* 21 CFR Part 211. Current Good Manufacturing Practice for Finished Pharmaceuticals.
2.  *International Council for Harmonisation.* ICH Q7: Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients.
3.  *Google Health Sciences Internal Report.* GHS-RPT-2024-012: Long-term Cryogenic Stability of Glucapeptide Molecules.
4.  *United States Pharmacopeia.* USP <1029> Documentation and Record Keeping.

---
**[End of Subsection 3.2.S.5.3]**

# Google Cloud-Based Reference Material Tracking

## Digital Inventory System

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.5.1 DIGITAL INVENTORY SYSTEM AND CLOUD-BASED TRACKING

---

### 3.2.S.5.1.1 Overview of the Google Cloud-Based Reference Material Tracking System (G-RMTS)

The management of Reference Standards for Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release) at Google Health Sciences (GHS) utilizes a bespoke, validated, digital inventory architecture integrated within the Google Cloud Life Sciences (GCLS) ecosystem. This system, designated the **Glucogen Reference Material Tracking System (G-RMTS)**, provides end-to-end traceability of Primary (PRS), Working (WRS), and Interim Reference Standards from the point of purification through final exhaustion or decommissioning.

The G-RMTS is designed to meet the rigorous requirements of 21 CFR Part 11 (Electronic Records; Electronic Signatures) and EudraLex Volume 4, Annex 11. It leverages a distributed ledger backbone for immutable audit trails and real-time stability monitoring integration.

### 3.2.S.5.1.2 Infrastructure and Data Integrity Architecture

The digital inventory system is hosted on the Google Cloud Platform (GCP) utilizing a high-availability (HA) configuration across three distinct geographic regions (US-West1, US-Central1, and US-East1) to ensure 99.999% uptime for critical quality data.

#### 3.2.S.5.1.2.1 Core Components of the G-RMTS

| Component ID | System Component | Technical Specification | Regulatory Function |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GCP-DB-01** | Google Cloud Spanner | Globally distributed, relational database | Storage of Reference Standard Metadata (Batch No, Potency, Purity) |
| **GCP-IAM-01** | Cloud Identity & Access | Multi-factor authentication (MFA) | Control of user permissions and e-signatures (21 CFR Part 11) |
| **GCP-LOG-01** | Cloud Logging / Audit | Immutable audit logs | 100% capture of every data modification or access event |
| **GCP-IOT-01** | Cloud IoT Core | Real-time sensor integration | Monitoring of -80°C and -20°C storage conditions |
| **GCP-AI-01** | Vertex AI Integration | Predictive stability modeling | Early warning for potential out-of-trend (OOT) stability results |

### 3.2.S.5.1.3 Digital Lifecycle Management of Glucogen-XR Standards

Every batch of Glucogen-XR Reference Standard is assigned a unique Global Trade Item Number (GTIN) and a serialized 2D Matrix code upon fill-finish. The digital inventory tracks the standard through the following lifecycle stages:

#### 3.2.S.5.1.3.1 Stage I: Registration and Initialization
Upon synthesis of a new batch (e.g., **GLUC-2025-001**), the Quality Control (QC) Laboratory initializes the record in G-RMTS. The initialization requires the input of the Master Cell Bank (MCB) lineage and the specific purification run ID.

**Table 3.2.S.5.1-1: Initial Digital Registration Data for Primary Reference Standard**

| Data Field | Entry Example | Validation Rule |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Internal Lot Number** | GLUC-2025-PRS-01 | Must follow GHS-SOP-009 naming convention |
| **Manufacturing Site** | 3000 Innovation Drive, SSF | Fixed location ID (GHS-SSF-01) |
| **Date of Manufacture** | 12-JAN-2025 | Non-future date validation |
| **Peptide Content (μg/vial)** | 502.4 | Must be within 95-105% of target |
| **Specific Activity (IU/mg)** | 14,250 | Determined by Cell-Based Bioassay (SOP-QC-22) |
| **Storage Temperature** | -80°C ± 5°C | Linked to IoT Sensor ID: SENS-ULT-99 |

#### 3.2.S.5.1.3.2 Stage II: Inventory Tiering and Relationships
The system employs a parent-child hierarchical logic to link Working Reference Standards (WRS) to their respective Primary Reference Standards (PRS). This ensures that if a PRS is withdrawn due to a quality issue, all derived WRS batches are automatically flagged as "Quarantined" in the digital system.

**Calculated Chain of Traceability:**
The potency of a WRS is calculated relative to the PRS using a four-parameter logistic (4PL) model executed within the Google Cloud Healthcare API:

$$f(x) = D + \frac{A - D}{1 + (\frac{x}{C})^B}$$

*Where:*
- $A$ = Minimum asymptote
- $B$ = Hill slope
- $C$ = $EC_{50}$
- $D$ = Maximum asymptote

### 3.2.S.5.1.4 Real-Time Inventory Tracking and Batch History

The following table provides an exhaustive view of the current digital inventory as of Q3 2025, demonstrating the granularity of the tracking system.

**Table 3.2.S.5.1-2: Comprehensive Digital Inventory of Glucogen-XR Reference Materials**

| Batch Number | Type | Status | Current Qty (Vials) | Last Retest Date | Retest Result (Purity %) | Next Retest Due |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| GLUC-2025-PRS-01 | Primary | Active | 482 | 15-FEB-2025 | 99.85% | 15-FEB-2026 |
| GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | Working | Active | 1,240 | 20-MAR-2025 | 99.72% | 20-SEP-2025 |
| GLUC-2025-WRS-02 | Working | In-Test | 1,500 | N/A | Pending | 01-OCT-2025 |
| GLUC-2025-IRS-01 | Interim | Expired | 0 | 10-JAN-2025 | 97.10% | DECOMMISSIONED |
| GLUC-2025-PRS-02 | Primary | Reserved | 600 | N/A | N/A | 01-JAN-2026 |

### 3.2.S.5.1.5 Protocol for Digital Inventory Transaction (SOP-DIG-440)

To maintain the integrity of the reference standard supply, all physical movements must be mirrored by a digital transaction within G-RMTS.

#### 3.2.S.5.1.5.1 Procedure for Withdrawal of Reference Standard
1. **Authentication**: The analyst scans their GHS Biometric Badge at the Smart-Freezer Terminal.
2. **Standard Selection**: The analyst selects the required batch (e.g., **GLUC-2025-WRS-01**).
3. **Reason Code Entry**: The system requires a selection from a predefined list (e.g., Release Testing, Stability Testing, Method Validation).
4. **LIMS Linkage**: The transaction is automatically linked to a Laboratory Information Management System (LIMS) Sample ID.
5. **Physical Retrieval**: The Smart-Freezer unlocks the specific bin. An RFID sensor detects the removal of the vial.
6. **Re-Verification**: The G-RMTS system compares the RFID tag of the removed vial with the requested batch. If a mismatch occurs, an "Immediate Alert" is sent to the Quality Assurance (QA) lead via Google Chat/Email.

### 3.2.S.5.1.6 Statistical Monitoring and Stability Integration

The G-RMTS is not merely a tracking tool but a diagnostic engine. It utilizes the **Google BigQuery** data warehouse to perform real-time Trend Analysis (RTTA) on reference standard performance across different analytical methods (RP-HPLC, SE-HPLC, CE-SDS).

#### 3.2.S.5.1.6.1 Calculation of Purity Degradation Rate
The system calculates the degradation slope ($k$) for each batch to predict the "End of Useful Life" (EOUL):

$$P_t = P_0 \cdot e^{-kt}$$

*Where:*
- $P_t$ = Predicted Purity at time $t$
- $P_0$ = Initial Purity
- $k$ = Rate constant (derived from $Q_{10}$ analysis of accelerated stability data)

If the predicted purity $P_t$ falls below the specification limit ($<98.0\%$) within the next 90 days, the system automatically triggers a "Pre-emptive Qualification" workflow for the successor batch.

### 3.2.S.5.1.7 Regulatory Compliance and Audit Trail Review

Pursuant to USP <11> (Reference Standards) and ICH Q6B, GHS maintains a continuous audit trail. The G-RMTS audit logs are reviewed monthly by the Digital Quality Systems (DQS) department.

**Table 3.2.S.5.1-3: Example Audit Trail Log (Redacted excerpt)**

| Timestamp (UTC) | User ID | Action Type | Object ID | Change Details |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 2025-05-12T14:22:01 | jsmith_qc | MODIFY | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | Retest Date extended from 01-JUN-2025 to 01-DEC-2025 based on protocol STAB-77 |
| 2025-05-12T14:22:05 | rbrown_qa | E-SIGN | GLUC-2025-WRS-01 | Approval of retest extension (21 CFR Part 11 compliant) |
| 2025-06-01T08:00:00 | SYS_ADMIN | AUTO-QUARANTINE | GLUC-2025-IRS-05 | Auto-quarantine due to storage excursion (Excursion ID: EXC-2025-09) |

### 3.2.S.5.1.8 Disaster Recovery and Business Continuity

Data redundancy is managed via **Google Cloud Storage (GCS)** buckets with "Object Versioning" enabled. In the event of a regional outage, the G-RMTS fails over to a secondary region within <60 seconds, ensuring that reference standard data is never unavailable during critical batch release activities at the South San Francisco manufacturing site.

*Footnote 1: All data transmissions are encrypted using AES-256 at rest and TLS 1.2+ in transit.*
*Footnote 2: The G-RMTS was validated under Validation Master Plan VMP-GHS-2024-001.*

---
**End of Subsection**

## Automated Expiry Alerts

### **3.2.S.5 Reference Standards or Materials**
### **Subsection: 3.2.S.5.4.2 Automated Expiry Alerts and Lifecycle Management Systems**

---

#### **1.0 Introduction to the Cloud-Native Lifecycle Management**
Google Health Sciences (GHS) leverages the **Google Cloud Life Sciences (GCLS) Architecture** to maintain a state-of-the-art, validated, GxP-compliant system for the management of Reference Standards (RS) for Glucogen-XR. Unlike traditional manual tracking systems, the **GHS-Nexus Platform** utilizes automated expiry alerts integrated with real-time stability monitoring data. This ensures that no Primary Reference Standard (PRS) or Working Reference Standard (WRS) is utilized in a GMP assay—whether for identity, purity, potency, or concentration—beyond its validated stability window.

This subsection details the algorithmic logic, the notification hierarchy, the integration with the Google Cloud BigQuery stability data lake, and the mitigation protocols triggered by the system when a batch (e.g., **GLUC-2025-001**) approaches its Re-test Date (RTD) or Expiration Date (ED).

---

#### **2.0 System Architecture and Logic Gates**
The Automated Expiry Alert system is governed by **SOP-GHS-QA-772: Digital Lifecycle Management of Biological Reference Materials**. The system operates on a "T-Minus" notification architecture, where "T" is the established expiry date stored in the **Cloud SQL Metadata Repository**.

##### **2.1 Expiry Notification Tiers**
The system is programmed to trigger multi-channel alerts (Email, SMS, and GHS-Nexus Dashboard) based on the following schedule:

| Alert Level | Trigger Period (Days prior to Expiry) | Target Recipients | Required Action |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Level 1 (Green)** | T-180 Days | Lab Manager, Inventory Specialist | Initiate Re-qualification protocol or order synthesis |
| **Level 2 (Yellow)** | T-90 Days | Quality Assurance (QA), Stability Lead | Review interim stability data; finalize re-test batching |
| **Level 3 (Amber)** | T-30 Days | Regulatory Affairs, Global Supply Chain | Flag potential risk to batch release schedules |
| **Level 4 (Red)** | T-7 Days | Site Head, Lead QP (Qualified Person) | Immediate stop-order on standard distribution |
| **Level 5 (Critical)** | T-0 Days | System Auto-Lock | Hard-lock in LIMS; standard cannot be selected for assays |

---

#### **3.0 Detailed Batch Tracking and Expiry Data Table**
The following table represents the current live tracking status for Glucogen-XR Reference Standards within the GHS-Nexus environment.

**Table 3.2.S.5.4-A: Active Reference Standard Expiry Matrix (Current as of Q1 2025)**

| Material ID | Batch Number | Description | Manufacture Date | Current Expiry / Re-test Date | Alert Status | Cloud-Sync Hash ID |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GHS-RS-001** | GLUC-2025-001 | Primary RS (Lyophilized) | 12-Jan-2025 | 12-Jan-2027 | **Active** | 8f92-ghs-7721 |
| **GHS-RS-002** | GLUC-2025-002 | Working RS (Liquid) | 15-Jan-2025 | 15-Jul-2025 | **Level 1 Alert** | 2a11-ghs-9903 |
| **GHS-RS-003** | GLUC-2025-003 | Impurity Standard (Des-His) | 02-Feb-2025 | 02-Feb-2026 | **Active** | 4d55-ghs-1209 |
| **GHS-RS-004** | GLUC-2025-004 | Potency Control | 10-Feb-2025 | 10-Aug-2025 | **Active** | 9c22-ghs-4432 |
| **GHS-RS-005** | GLUC-2024-088 | Legacy Working RS | 14-Nov-2024 | 14-May-2025 | **Level 2 Alert** | 1b88-ghs-5561 |

---

#### **4.0 Step-by-Step Protocol: Automated Alert Response**
When the Cloud-Based system initiates a **Level 2 (Yellow)** alert (T-90 days), the following protocol (**PRO-GHS-RS-992**) is automatically instantiated as a workflow ticket in the Quality Management System (QMS).

##### **Step 1: Stability Data Extraction**
*   **Action:** The system queries the BigQuery dataset `ghs_stability_monitoring_prod`.
*   **Calculation:** The system calculates the Degradation Rate Constant ($k$) using a first-order kinetic model:
    $$ln[C] = ln[C_0] - kt$$
    *Where:*
    *   $[C]$ = Current Potency (IU/mg)
    *   $[C_0]$ = Initial Potency
    *   $t$ = Time elapsed (months)
*   **Requirement:** If the projected potency at $T+180$ days is $>95.0\%$ of the label claim, a re-qualification extension is permissible.

##### **Step 2: Physical Inventory Reconciliation**
*   **Action:** Automated Guided Vehicles (AGVs) in the South San Francisco cold storage facility (Site 3000) perform a cycle count of the specific batch (e.g., **GLUC-2025-002**).
*   **Verification:** Confirm that vial integrity (checked via visual sensors) is maintained and temperature logs (monitored via Google Cloud IoT Core) show no excursions outside the $-70^{\circ}C \pm 10^{\circ}C$ range.

##### **Step 3: Analytical Re-qualification**
*   **Action:** Analytical Development (AD) performs a "Side-by-Side" comparison of the expiring WRS against the PRS.
*   **Acceptance Criteria:**
    *   RP-HPLC Purity: $\geq 98.0\%$
    *   SEC-HPLC Aggregate: $\leq 0.5\%$
    *   Bioassay Potency: $90-110\%$ of PRS.

---

#### **5.0 Statistical Modeling for Expiry Extension (Predictive Analytics)**
GHS utilizes the **Vertex AI** suite to predict reference standard stability. The model incorporates historical data from the CHO-K1 GS knockout derivative expression platform.

**Formula for Predicted Shelf-Life ($t_{90}$):**
The time to reach 90% of original activity is calculated using the Arrhenius equation:
$$k = A e^{-E_a / RT}$$
Where:
- $E_a$ (Activation Energy) is derived from accelerated stability studies ($25^{\circ}C/60\% RH$).
- $R$ is the gas constant ($8.314 J/mol \cdot K$).
- $T$ is the storage temperature in Kelvin ($203.15 K$).

The automated alert system adjusts the "T-Minus" triggers based on the variance between the **Predicted $t_{90}$** and the **Observed $t_{90}$**. If the variance exceeds 5%, a **Level 3 (Amber)** alert is triggered immediately regardless of the calendar date.

---

#### **6.0 Regulatory Compliance and Audit Trail**
In accordance with **FDA 21 CFR Part 11** and **ICH Q7 (Section 11.1)**, every automated alert, acknowledgment, and subsequent action is logged in an immutable distributed ledger (Blockchain-inspired audit trail) within Google Cloud.

**Table 3.2.S.5.4-B: Audit Trail Log for Batch GLUC-2025-002 (Sample)**

| Timestamp (UTC) | Event ID | User / System ID | Action Performed | Result |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| 2025-03-15:08:00 | ALRT-9921 | System_Nexus | Triggered Level 1 Alert (T-180) | Notification Sent |
| 2025-03-15:09:12 | ACK-4432 | J. Doe (Lab Mgr) | Acknowledged Alert; Assigned to AD | Workflow Active |
| 2025-03-16:14:00 | DATA-881 | Cloud_Stability_Bot | Pulled SEC-HPLC data (Batch 2025-002) | Purity: 99.4% |
| 2025-03-16:14:01 | CALC-009 | VertexAI_Bot | Re-calculated $t_{90}$ projection | Stable to 2026 |

---

#### **7.0 Handling of Expired Standards (Quarantine Protocol)**
Upon reaching **Level 5 (Critical)** or $T-0$, the following automated actions occur:
1.  **LIMS De-certification:** The batch status for **GLUC-2025-XXX** is changed from "Released" to "Expired/Quarantined."
2.  **Physical Access Lock:** The RFID-enabled freezer drawers (Equipment ID: **GHS-FRZ-099**) will not unlock for any user attempting to check out the expired material.
3.  **Impact Assessment:** The system automatically generates a list of all GMP batches released using this standard within the last 30 days to ensure no retrospective quality impact (per **ICH Q10** Pharmaceutical Quality System guidelines).

---

#### **8.0 References**
1.  **FDA Guidance for Industry:** *Analytical Procedures and Methods Validation for Drugs and Biologics (2015).*
2.  **USP <1225>:** *Validation of Compendial Procedures.*
3.  **ICH Q2(R2):** *Validation of Analytical Procedures.*
4.  **ISO/IEC 17025:2017:** *General requirements for the competence of testing and calibration laboratories.*
5.  **Google Cloud Whitepaper:** *GxP Compliance on Google Cloud Platform (v3.1).*

**End of Subsection**

## Usage History and Traceability

# MODULE 3: QUALITY (3.2.S.5 REFERENCE STANDARDS OR MATERIALS)
## SECTION: 3.2.S.5.1 REFERENCE STANDARD CHARACTERIZATION AND CONTROL
### SUBSECTION: Usage History and Traceability for Glucogen-XR Reference Materials

---

#### 1.0 INTRODUCTION AND SCOPE
This subsection details the comprehensive usage history, genealogical lineage, and digital traceability protocols for the reference materials associated with **Glucogen-XR (glucapeptide extended-release)**, manufactured by **Google Health Sciences (GHS)**. 

In alignment with **ICH Q6B** (Specifications: Test Procedures and Acceptance Criteria for Biotechnological/Biological Products) and **ICH Q7** (Good Manufacturing Practice Guide for Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients), Google Health Sciences maintains a bifurcated traceability system. This system integrates physical sample management with the **Google Cloud Life Sciences (GCLS) Immutable Ledger Technology (ILT)**, ensuring that every milligram of reference material is accounted for from the point of purification to its terminal use in analytical release testing or stability studies.

#### 2.0 CLOUD-BASED TRACEABILITY ARCHITECTURE: THE "DIGITAL TWIN" MODEL
Google Health Sciences utilizes a proprietary Cloud-Based Reference Material Tracking (CBRMT) system. Every batch of Glucogen-XR Reference Standard (Primary, Working, or Interim) is assigned a **Digital Object Identifier (DOI)** linked to the batch number (e.g., GLUC-2025-XXX).

##### 2.1 Metadata Integration
The CBRMT system captures the following parameters in real-time:
1.  **Storage Telemetry:** Continuous stream of temperature and humidity from the GHS South San Francisco Cold Chain Vault (Equipment ID: GHS-REF-VAULT-09).
2.  **Usage Log-ins:** Biometric verification of the analyst accessing the material.
3.  **Gravimetric Precision:** Integration with Mettler Toledo analytical balances (Model XPR205) to record the exact mass withdrawn.
4.  **Assay Association:** Automated linking of the reference material aliquot to the specific HPLC, CE-SDS, or Bioassay run ID.

---

#### 3.0 USAGE HISTORY AND BATCH GENEALOGY
The following tables delineate the history of the current Primary Reference Standard (PRS) and Working Reference Standards (WRS) utilized in the clinical development and planned commercial launch of Glucogen-XR.

##### Table 3.1: Primary Reference Standard (PRS) Lineage and Inventory History
| Batch Number | Manufacture Date | Site of Manufacture | Original Quantity (vials) | Current Balance (vials) | Primary Purpose | Status |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **GLUC-2024-PRS-01** | 12-JAN-2024 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | 500 (10mg/vial) | 412 | Characterization of Working Standards | Active |
| **GLUC-2025-PRS-02** | 15-FEB-2025 | 3000 Innovation Dr, SSF | 1,200 (10mg/vial) | 1,200 | Planned Commercial Transition | In-Qualification |

##### Table 3.2: Working Reference Standard (WRS) Usage Log (Excerpts for GLUC-2025-WRS-01)
This table represents the high-fidelity tracking of Working Reference Standard Batch **GLUC-2025-WRS-01**, derived from Primary Batch GLUC-2024-PRS-01.

#### 4.0 PROTOCOL FOR TRACEABILITY AND WITHDRAWAL (SOP-GHS-REF-001)
To ensure the integrity of the usage history, all laboratory personnel must adhere to the following protocol when accessing Glucogen-XR Reference Materials.

##### 4.1 Access and Identification
1.  **Authentication:** Personnel must authenticate via GHS-Identity at the South San Francisco Storage Facility.
2.  **Selection:** The CBRMT system identifies the specific vial number (RFID-tagged) to be retrieved based on the "First-In-First-Out" (FIFO) or specific stability-protocol requirements.
3.  **Scanning:** The vial’s 2D Matrix code is scanned using the GHS-Cloud-Link handheld device.

##### 4.2 Handling and Reconstitution
1.  **Thermal Equilibration:** Vials are removed from -80°C and placed in a 2-8°C stabilization chamber (Equipment ID: GHS-STAB-02) for 45 minutes.
2.  **Gravimetric Verification:**
    *   Tare the sterile, DNA-free glass vial.
    *   Record mass of lyophilized Glucogen-XR powder.
    *   *Calculation:* $M_{final} - M_{tare} = M_{net\_solid}$.
3.  **Dilution:** Add 1.0 mL of USP Sterile Water for Injection (WFI).
    *   *Target Concentration:* $C = \frac{M_{net\_solid}}{V_{diluent}}$.
    *   The CBRMT system automatically calculates the concentration and pushes this value to the Empower 3 Chromatography Data System (CDS).

##### 4.3 Documentation and "Dead Volume" Accounting
Every microliter of the reference standard must be accounted for.
*   **Aliquot Log:** If the vial is split into multiple sub-aliquots, each sub-vial receives a child-barcode (e.g., GLUC-2025-XXX-A1).
*   **Waste Tracking:** Residual material remaining in the vial (dead volume) must be measured by weight and logged as "Analytical Waste" to close the mass balance in the Cloud Ledger.

---

#### 5.0 STATISTICAL CONTROL AND DRIFT ANALYSIS
As per **USP <1225>** (Validation of Compendial Procedures), Google Health Sciences monitors the usage history to detect any systematic drift in the reference material’s performance over time.

##### 5.1 The Control Charting Mechanism
Data from every HPLC injection using WRS GLUC-2025-XXX is aggregated in the Google Cloud BigQuery environment. The "Main Peak Area Ratio" and "Retention Time" are plotted on a Shewhart control chart.

**Formulas for Drift Detection:**
*   **Mean ($\mu$):** $\bar{x} = \frac{\sum x_i}{n}$
*   **Standard Deviation ($\sigma$):** $s = \sqrt{\frac{\sum (x_i - \bar{x})^2}{n-1}}$
*   **Warning Limit (WL):** $\pm 2\sigma$
*   **Action Limit (AL):** $\pm 3\sigma$

If the usage history indicates three consecutive data points exceeding the $2\sigma$ threshold, the CBRMT system triggers an automated **Reference Material Out-of-Trend (OOT)** investigation, and the batch is temporarily locked in the cloud (status: "Hold").

---

#### 6.0 INTER-LABORATORY TRACEABILITY (GLOBAL NETWORK)
Google Health Sciences operates multiple manufacturing and testing sites. The traceability of Glucogen-XR reference standards extends across the following nodes:
*   **Primary Hub:** SSF, California (3000 Innovation Drive).
*   **Secondary Hub:** GHS Dublin, Ireland (Data Center & QC Lab).
*   **Contract Testing:** Eurofins/PPD (Accessed via GHS-Cloud Secure Portal).

##### Table 6.1: Cross-Site Transfer History
| Origin Site | Destination Site | Date of Transfer | Quantity | Courier Tracking (FedEx/ColdChain) | Receipt Confirmation ID |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| SSF-Hub | Dublin-QC | 20-JAN-2025 | 50 Vials | CC-8812-GHS-01 | GHS-DUB-REC-09 |
| SSF-Hub | PPD Lab-01 | 05-FEB-2025 | 20 Vials | CC-9904-GHS-02 | PPD-GHS-REC-12 |

---

#### 7.0 REGULATORY COMPLIANCE AND AUDIT TRAIL
This usage history is maintained in a "Validated State" as defined by **21 CFR Part 11**. 
1.  **Non-Repudiation:** All entries are cryptographically signed.
2.  **Immutability:** Once a withdrawal is logged in the GCLS Ledger, it cannot be deleted or altered without an authorized Change Control (SOP-GHS-QA-005).
3.  **Accessibility:** During an FDA inspection, the "Usage History Report" for any specific batch of Glucogen-XR can be generated in real-time, providing a granular view of every analytical procedure that utilized the standard.
